# 广成集

**Guangcheng Collection**

*Scripture Title:* *Guangcheng Collection*. Seventeen juan. Compiled by Du Guangting of the late Tang and Five Dynasties period. Based on the *Zhengtong Daoist Canon*, *Dongxuan Section*, *Memorials and Memorials Category*.

**Guangcheng Collection, Juan One**

*Composed by Du Guangting, Inner Offering Attendant of the Supreme Clarity Palace in the Upper Capital, Imperial-Commissioned Literary Virtue and Power, and Purple-Robe Bestowed Great Master*

**Memorial Substituting for Minister Tao Fu on the Restoration of the Jin River Mouth Transcendence Sanctuary and Request for Its Name Plaque**

Your subject humbly states: The Jin River Mouth Transcendence Sanctuary is the eighteenth of the Twenty-Four Transcendence Sites, its seasonal node aligned with Lesser Fullness and its stellar correspondence with the Net Star. Traces of Chen Anshi’s ascension to heaven in broad daylight remain, as do the chariot tracks of the Lady of Bao, who attained the Dao. Each spring and autumn, by imperial decree, prayers and offerings are conducted here. Yet since the recent wars, all has been ravaged. The ancient halls stand empty, the altars bare, with only their foundations left. The sacred images and visages of immortals lie hidden beneath brambles and weeds. Pilgrims no longer come to pay reverence, and officials and commoners alike have no refuge for devotion. Who could have foreseen that this blessed site would fall into such desolation?

Your subject has undertaken its restoration, wishing to contribute to the sacred longevity of Your Majesty. I humbly recall that Your Majesty, heir to the numinous origins of the Xuanyuan Emperor and the immortal lineage of Mount Gou, succeeds Heaven in ruling the realm, governing the people through the Dao. The myriad lands bask in the vastness of your compassion, and the Three Teachings are renewed by your grace. The fields of magic mushrooms and the gardens of immortals all benefit from your solemn devotion. Even ancient temples and Confucian halls have received your restorative care. How much more, then, should this sanctuary of the Everlasting Life Teachings be honored with reverent repair?

Thus, I have cleared the overgrowth, rebuilt the halls and chambers, spared the sacred images from exposure, and enabled the faithful to resume their rites of burning incense and offering prayers. The distant traces of transcendence are once more a place of sublime cultivation. Lamps and incense now have their proper place, and the rituals of purification and offering suffer no lack. I have also summoned the Daoist masters Yang Xuanjing, Dugu Zhiyuan, and He [given name omitted], who have taken up residence at the sanctuary.

Yet, as the desolation endured for so long, the gate plaque has been entirely lost. I dare to beseech the favor of your beneficent grace, that this realm of gods and immortals may be specially adorned.

May I humbly beseech Your Sacred Grace to graciously bestow, in accordance with the former name of this sanctuary, a plaque inscribed with the august title "Shengshou." Permit this humble servant to craft and hang it, that the silver characters on jade tablets may forever bask in the radiance of sun and moon, and the immortal mountains beside the Han River may eternally celebrate Your Sagely Longevity. This servant is overwhelmed with gratitude.

---

**Memorial of Thanks for the Restoration of the Golden Register Daoist Ritual at the New Hall**

Your servant humbly reports: By imperial decree, I, together with Right Street Ritual Master He Chonghui and twenty-one others, conducted a seven-day Golden Register Daoist ritual within the new hall, commencing on the fourteenth day of this month and concluding on the twentieth. Palace Attendant Yang Shaoye performed the scheduled rites of obeisance, and the memorial of merit and praise has now been duly submitted.

I reflect that Heaven has blessed Your Sagely Work, renewing the grandeur of the imperial palace. Its jade terraces and vermilion gates surpass the palaces of the Three Isles, while its azure portals and cinnabar doors transcend the phoenix towers of the Nine Heavens. It embodies the splendor of the imperial residence and the solemn majesty of the Son of Heaven’s abode. All nations gaze in reverence, and a thousand spirits stand guard in awe. Scarcely had the construction of this jeweled palace been completed when the altar of the Golden Register was first established. Every detail was meticulously renewed, and each act of devotion was marked by profound purity. The fragrance of dragon incense ascended, and it seemed as though ten thousand sages had descended; the glow of the toad moon shone low, and it appeared as though a thousand perfected beings had gathered. May Your Sagely Lifespan be extended, and may the imperial realm endure forever.

Your humble servant, bowing in reverence, offers words of praise to the chief ministers, his heart filled with devotion and prayer. Auspicious omens have duly converged, and boundless blessings have been bestowed. May the great treasure of the throne flourish for a thousand springs, uniting the eight directions under one rule. We, your servants, have been favored with appointment to the sacred teachings and have taken part in these rites of devotion. We have feasted on jade delicacies from the celestial kitchens and trodden the cloud-paved courtyards of the immortal realm. Our honor is already beyond measure, yet further imperial gifts have been bestowed. We humbly acknowledge the gracious bestowal of supplementary funds, silver vessels, and bolts of silk—favors as deep as the vast ocean and as weighty as Mount Song. How can one as insignificant as a crane or swallow repay such sagely rewards? This servant is overwhelmed with gratitude.

---

**Memorial of Thanks for Appointment as Vice Minister of the Ministry of Revenue, with Additional Rank and Title**

Your servant humbly reports: By imperial grace, I have been appointed Grand Master for Splendid Happiness, Vice Minister of the Ministry of Revenue, Supreme Pillar of State, Duke of Cai, and Master of Broad Achievement. The warmth of Your Sagely Benevolence shines forth like spring, and the imperial brush has bestowed its radiance. Overwhelmed by such honor, I can scarcely comprehend its magnitude; burdened by such favor, I know not how to respond. Your servant offers his deepest gratitude.

I have heard that when a sagely ruler sits upon the throne, he must appoint the capable to office. When the worthy and good serve in government, they must exert their utmost. Those who ascend the ranks must embody the Dao; those who govern must be adept at adapting to change. Above, they must possess the ability to assist their ruler; below, they must fulfill the duties of a minister. Having found their proper place, they must apply themselves to the needs of the times. If they fail to benefit the people, they will surely incur the reproach of seeking mere favor.

As for your servant—obscure and timid—I have been honored to serve under such a radiant reign. Yet, looking inward, I see only my mediocre talents and dare not presume upon such extraordinary favor. I reflect that Your Majesty, in inaugurating this era and assuming the throne, has embraced the mandate of Heaven. Your wisdom outshines the twin luminaries, and Your virtue harmonizes with the vastness of Heaven and Earth. You have swept away the mists of corruption and revived the world. Your achievements have united all things in common purpose, and Your transformative influence has brought the eight directions under Your sway. Dreams have bridged the chasms of mountains and valleys, and Your ministers have answered the call of destiny; the mists and waves of distant lands have turned in admiration, and Your aides have fulfilled the omens of loyalty. The great pillars of state, steadfast in their support, hold aloft the sun and prop up the heavens. Heroes of the age, they are as stars descended from the heavens and peaks risen from the earth. The Eastern Palace aids in governance, and the sun and moon shine with renewed brilliance; the Southern Palace stands firm in loyalty, and the pillars of the realm are strengthened.

Your servant, a lowly being from rivers and lakes, possesses but modest talents. As a scholar, I have failed to achieve the heights of the unicorn; as a Daoist, I have been content to sketch the tiger. Moreover, I have been absent from court for many years, serving Your Majesty from afar. Though I have received no favors from mountains and streams, I have often been moved by the encounters of wind and cloud. For over thirty years, I have dwelled in seclusion, nurtured by Your light. The favors bestowed upon me are as weighty as Mount Song and as deep as the vast seas. You have transformed withered roots into lush grass and raised broken bones into robust flesh. Yet, though I call this a wondrous achievement, it scarcely compares to Your sagely rewards.

Thus, I prostrate myself in earnest supplication, my gratitude accumulating before Your Imperial Benevolence. Day and night, my spirit is stirred, and my shadow startles me. I have not repaid even a hair’s worth of Your kindness, yet my heart overflows with awe and trepidation. Now, at the dawn of this new era and the beginning of Your reign, You have bestowed upon me the elegant title of "Master of Broad Achievement," akin to the illustrious ranks of the Northern Bureau. I am unworthy of the discourse on serving the state with one’s person. How can I, who have failed to offer counsel at Your knee or present ideas to ease Your heart, presume to occupy such an exalted position? To covet further honors beyond my rank would be the height of greed. How could I dare to tread upon such extraordinary favor, ascending the ranks of the pure and distinguished? You have bestowed upon me a title as resplendent as the azure heavens and gathered my flawed being into the gates of mystery.

Yet, even in the Han dynasty, Dongfang Shuo was celebrated, and in the Jin, Pei Kai of Zhichuan was honored. Never before has one been granted consecutive appointments to such esteemed offices or twice bestowed with such exceptional ranks. Weighing my worth, I am filled with trepidation, torn between advancing and retreating. Facing Your Imperial Majesty, I have no means to decline. I can only vow to steel myself with diligence and forever repay Your boundless grace. This servant is overwhelmed with gratitude.

---

**Memorial of Thanks for the Imperial Decree Exempting This Servant from Joining the Two Teachings in Processions for Court Celebrations**

Your servant humbly reports: By Your Sagely Grace, it has been decreed that whenever court celebrations or congratulatory audiences arise, I shall no longer stand in the same rank as the Daoist and Buddhist clergy but shall instead be summoned alone for private audience, apart from the general assembly. Such exceptional courtesy transcends customary norms. The praise originates from Your Sagely Heart, and the honor uniquely illuminates the realm of the Dao. The weight of this favor is more than I can bear.

Your servant is both honored and awestruck, bowing his head again and again.

I reflect that Your Majesty, in Your divine wisdom, has inherited the mandate of Heaven and wields the symbols of imperial authority. You encompass Heaven and Earth in Your embrace and suspend the sun and moon to illuminate all below. The brilliance of Your golden mirror leaves no darkness unexposed, and the harmony of Your jade candle nurtures all things in spring. Thus, dew descends from the roots of Heaven, and Your grace flows across the face of the earth. You have pacified the realm through martial prowess, subduing the rebellious and instilling awe in the wicked; You have cultivated civil virtue to tame the distant and transform the treacherous. Even the nomads of felt tents and the dwellers of ice caves have come to court, offering tribute and observing the winds of change.

The realm settled, music arises; achievements complete, rites proceed. You have raised the fallen norms of the Three Dynasties and revived the lost canons of a hundred kings. There is renewal and reform, without faction or bias.

When the lords of the land assemble to pay court, You govern with ease, Your robes hanging loose, attended by ministers as stalwart as the Three Heroes and Ten Worthies, surpassing even the sagely talents of Feixiong and Shenxiang. The splendor of culture and ritual outshines past and present alike.

Some, clad in cloud-patterned robes and feathered garments, gaze toward the vermilion steps and raise their voices in homage; others, barefoot in square-cut robes, stand in the vermilion court and offer solemn blessings. At such times, this humble minister, though but a traveler in the ranks, has been permitted to approach the cloud-like steps, ever astonished at his own insignificance—like a mere ravine or gorge—yet finding himself lifted above the mist and clouds.

Now, Your sagely favor has been lavished anew, transforming all former observances. Though my humble person has been privileged to don the cap and sash of office and to enjoy the emoluments of a pure and elevated rank—my talents first employed in the northern ministry’s illustrious service, then transferred to the southern bureau—You have, in this moment of audience, singled me out from among the ranks of black-robed and yellow-clad officials, granting me a private summons to display Your boundless grace.

In former times, the Wei honored Jian’s reverence for Liang’s purity, and the Han praised Manqian while Qin lauded Ziping; yet even then, no new forms of ritual were devised, and courtly decorum adhered to established norms. Now, however, You have bestowed a mandate bright as the nine heavens and established a grand design for ten thousand generations. In quiet reflection, I am overwhelmed by awe; in my frailty and insignificance, how can I bear the grace of Your rain and dew? I can only strive to offer my utmost sincerity in eternal repayment of Your vast beneficence.

This unworthy minister is utterly overwhelmed.

**Memorial of Thanks for the Privilege of Private Audience, Ordered to Be Entered into the National Histories**

Your servant humbly states: By Your sagely grace, I have been specially favored with a private audience, exempted from the general summons. Moreover, my memorial of thanks has been ordered to be entered into the Histories. From the depths of Your imperial regard, this extraordinary courtesy has been extended, and my gratitude shall be forever recorded in the annals of truth, bearing witness to Your boundless favor. Overwhelmed by such honor, I am at a loss.

I prostrate myself in gratitude, reflecting that Your Majesty, in Your great wisdom, governs the realm, proclaiming sagely achievements. You have expanded the embrace of Heaven and Earth with martial grace and spread the radiance of sun and moon to illuminate all. The worthy and good have come to assist You, and the court abounds with ministers of exceptional talent. The Hua and Yi alike submit to Your benevolence, and the treasuries overflow with tribute from distant lands. All peoples enjoy prosperity and longevity, and without exertion, the realm approaches the harmony of Huaxu.

Thus, the palaces of Penglai and the halls of Zhi are all aglow with splendor; the sacred groves and imperial gardens are adorned with solemn magnificence. The Four Spirits manifest their auspicious forms, and the Six Qi harmonize in timely accord, bearing witness to Your blessings. The profound and the learned flourish, and the black-robed and brown-clad rejoice together. Though I am but an ordinary man, I have been blessed to encounter this glorious era, my name recorded among the honored and my office twice elevated to exalted rank.

Yet You have further distinguished me with singular favor, granting me a private audience. Amid the ranks of black-robed and yellow-clad officials, I received the summons and ascended directly to the heavens; in the court of the mandarin ducks and egrets, I glanced at my shadow and wondered if wings had sprouted upon me.

Now, this honor has been inscribed in the national histories, proclaimed throughout the realm—a grace beyond all precedent, forever enshrined in imperishable records. My long-standing dullness and insignificance cannot withstand the depth of Your rain and dew; my meager worth, like the smallest blade of grass, can never repay the virtue of Heaven and Earth. I can only devote myself to diligent service in reverent response to Your sagely wisdom.

This unworthy minister is utterly overwhelmed.

**Memorial in Celebration of the Yellow Clouds**

Your Majesty,

I, your humble servant, have observed the memorial submitted by Minister of Rites Zhao Wen-gui, reporting that on the twenty-third day of this month, as Your Imperial Majesty graced the De Xian Tower to inspect the troops, the Crown Prince returned from reviewing the cavalry encampment south of the city and entered the gates. At the hour of *you*, two golden clouds appeared above the city walls, shaped like canopies of blossoms, lingering before transforming into a purple hue.

I humbly note that at the birth of Emperor Yao, golden clouds descended in shelter; during the reign of Emperor Shun, golden clouds congealed in the heavens. Moreover, when Emperor Xuan of Han visited the Ganquan Palace, purple clouds entered the hall; when Emperor Taizu of Song ascended the throne, purple clouds manifested at the Gate of Uprightness. The Yellow Emperor had auspicious clouds by which he ordered his officials. Now, as virtue stirs Heaven’s favor, propitious clouds appear in the skies. Both Hua and Yi gaze in reverence; seas and mountains join in celebration.

I, your servant, offer my deepest congratulations. Your Majesty embodies the Dao and wields the Mandate, divinely endowed with sagely wisdom. Your benevolence embraces all living things; your grace extends across the earth. You pacify distant lands with civil brilliance and subdue fierce foes with martial prowess. As the Central Plains remain unsettled and all things restless, you have resolved to restore order and relieve the suffering of the people. Your commands have crushed the southern rebels like serpents; your campaigns have swept away the northern dust like smoke. Iron axles and dragon-prowed ships gleam upon the waters; frost-edged spears and snow-bright halberds march upon the land. Mountains and rivers tremble at your might; thunder and lightning hasten at your call. With boundless magnanimity, you expand the realm of Heaven and Earth.

Thus, you have entrusted the Crown Prince with the training of the Six Armies and the enforcement of the Three Commands. Warriors in chariots and armored ranks soar with valor; men of titanic strength blaze with courage bright as the sun. All stand firm as metal and stone, their loyalty unshaken. Truly in accord with Heaven’s will, the divine favor has manifested: twin clouds arose in majestic splendor, their forms coalescing like golden branches and jade leaves. High above the imperial throne, they deepened to purple, resembling blossoms in full bloom, descending to embrace the royal city. First assuming the guise of a cauldron’s shade, they gradually took on the hue of a frontier pass—clear signs that the vault of Heaven applauds your virtue, now ascendant. This surpasses the omens of Yao and Shun, exceeds the portents of Han Xuan and Song Taizu. Henceforth, the eight wilds shall submit as guests, and the myriad lands shall share a single path. May your sagely years stretch into the thousands and millions; may your grand foundation stand eternal and unshaken.

I, your servant, have been deeply favored by your wisdom and twice witnessed these wondrous signs. Dare I compose verse to express my sincerity and offer song to extol your sagely virtue? I humbly present a poem in tribute.

**Memorial in Celebration of the White Magpie**

I have further observed that Li Yan-tao, a commoner of Chongshan Village in Duogong District of Yandao County, captured a white magpie from a nanmu tree and presented it as tribute. The Five Phases reveal their auspiciousness, heralding the flourishing of the Metal Cycle; all officials gaze in unison, celebrating the celestial bounty bestowed upon the Jade Capital.

I, your servant, offer my most sincere congratulations. I have heard that when a true king rectifies names and establishes teachings, he embodies Heaven’s will, curbs cruelty and eliminates slaughter, thus comforting the hearts of the people. Then do rare trees and precious birds appear, coming to pay court at the palace gates—frost-touched feathers stirring with color, deep-blue talons marking their marvel. Folding their wings to display their form, they put to shame the vain boasts of Han and Wei; transmitting their cries to convey joy, they soar in homage to Your August Brilliance.

I humbly reflect that Your Majesty’s auspicious signs surpass those of all former kings, your achievements transcend those of the Three Antiquities. In harmonious sequence, winds and rains follow the measures of Yu; dispelling darkness, your mirror-like wisdom fills the halls of Xuantai. Nurturing all within the Four Seas, you have twice established the foundation of Heaven and Earth; illuminating the lands below, you have renewed the radiance of sun and moon. You have outshone the feeble Han, whose people rested their shoulders, and surpassed the contented Tang, whose people drummed their bellies. The people sing of abundant harvests; all things rely on the peace of the times.

Moreover, your legions—tens of thousands of fierce warriors, thousands of encampments gleaming with armor—capture the wicked and eradicate corruption, shelter the weak and nurture the orphaned. Thunderous rolls of war drums advance; clouds darken with the unfurling of banners. At your commands, the bold and mighty leap to action; through your grace, the weary and afflicted revive. The Five Planets move in their courses to bestow blessings; the Eight Seas submit to your influence and calm their waves. Thus do mountains and rivers offer their felicity, and birds and beasts present their omens.

Far from their nests upon the sea, they come to face the palace amid the clouds. Behold them in their jade cages, their snowy forms revealed at a glance. Unstartled, they do not circle the imperial gardens in flight, but before your celestial benevolence, they dance with joy. Coming and going along the jade steps, perching beside the beaded curtains, their pure white plumage is hard to distinguish, yet their new songs sound familiar. They are no companions for bridge-building magpies, nor are they part of flocks circling trees. Having manifested their snowy-white beauty, they truly herald the flourishing of the Metal Cycle.

I await the day when weapons are laid down and treachery is eradicated. The smoke and beacons of the battlefield shall be swept away, forever returning to the North Star; the brambles and thorns of the realm shall be stilled, pacified from the West. Truly, you surpass the might of Wei’s virtue and eclipse the achievements of Han’s prosperity.

I, your servant, have been blessed to witness this flourishing era and repeatedly behold these wondrous signs. Thus, I dare to present verses of song and praise, humbly offering them for Your Sagely Inspection.

I further humbly submit a poem in celebration of your sagely virtue and the auspicious omen.

**Memorial in Celebration of the Auspicious Grain Presented by Tianzhen Army**

I, your servant, have observed that Cui Shan, Acting Military Commissioner of Tianzhen Army, has presented a depiction of double-eared grain offered by Wang Youtian, a commoner of Shehong County. Your sagely virtue reaches far, and auspicious signs arrive in succession. Civil and military officials gaze upon them in awe; all within and beyond the realm rejoice.

I, your servant, have consulted the Auspicious Omens Record, which states: "Auspicious grain is a most excellent omen. In years of abundance, when the ruler’s virtue extends to the earth, two stalks grow from a single root." In ancient times, Tang Shu obtained such grain, with different fields bearing identical ears. King Cheng asked the Duke of Zhou: "Does two ears on one stalk signify that all under Heaven is in harmony?" The king commanded Tang Shu to compose the *Ode to Auspicious Grain*. Thereafter, the Nine Lands were united, the Eight Directions submitted, tribute of mastiffs came from the west, and pheasants arrived from the south. For thirty generations, the grand foundation endured; for seven hundred years, the great enterprise flourished—outshining the Xia and eclipsing the Shang.

Now, in this sagely and enlightened age, such an omen has again appeared. I humbly reflect that Your Majesty has inherited the sacred lineage of the Xuanyuan Emperor and carries forward the great source of the Zhou sovereigns. Aligned with the Mandate of Heaven, you unite Hua and Yi as one, ruling like the Thearch. In reverence and frugality, you have renounced the pleasures of music and wine; in sagacity and divine insight, you possess the clarity of keen sight and sharp hearing. Spreading martial virtue, you first punish those who defy the law, sweeping away treacherous rebels like lightning; disseminating civil culture, you swiftly pacify the Rong and Qiang, who come bearing tribute like clouds. You labor with concern for the people’s welfare, pitying the toil of farmers. Year after year, harvests are bountiful; fields know neither drought nor flood.

Your virtue reaches the earth, manifesting in the shared bloom of two stalks; your resonance with Heaven is revealed in the identical ears from different fields. This fulfills the omen of the sagely ancestors and heralds the Zhou’s auspicious grain; it signifies our sovereign’s expansion of the realm. In the past, harmony united Heaven and Earth as one; now, your embrace encompasses all lands in a single realm. Moreover, as the royal armies prepare for punitive campaigns, swearing to relieve the people’s suffering, your awe-inspiring might has already cowed distant lands, and auspicious signs first appear in nearby regions. We await the restoration of peace, the eternal dispelling of miasmic turmoil. You shall reveal the radiance of sun and moon across the Nine Heavens, fulfilling the Zhou’s divinations; you shall unite the hopes of all living beings across the Four Seas, matching the Tang’s auspicious grain.

I, your servant, gazing upon the Auspicious Omens Record, join in singing of your sagely influence. I wish to be included in the annals of those who gather poems, aspiring to follow in the footsteps of Tang Shu’s ode. I humbly submit a poem in praise of your sagely virtue and the double-eared grain.

**Memorial Requesting That the Imperial Carriage Not Proceed to the Northern Army Front**

I, your servant, have received the imperial decree that the imperial carriage shall proceed to the northern army front.

Your servant has heard that the inspection of righteous deeds and the review of meritorious service are enduring rites handed down in the ritual classics, while the punitive expedition against rebels and the suppression of traitors are universal norms of statecraft. Such measures aim to extend radiant illumination to every region and to gather the five auspicious omens from the feudal lords. They serve to eradicate violence and disorder, bringing solace to the suffering masses. Yet the rebellious tribes of Bin and Qi, long deluded and estranged from the Great Norm, shall soon—indeed, within days—witness their annihilation. There is no need for Your Imperial Carriage to personally advance upon the war chariot, venturing afar to the lair of cunning foes. The earnest pleas of the multitude, united in their apprehension, give rise to widespread alarm and doubt.

I humbly reflect that Your Majesty surpasses the luminous virtue of Shun and transcends the divine martial prowess of the Zhou kings. You wield the commanding severity of autumn frost while bestowing the nurturing breath of spring’s renewal. Entrusting all to perfect impartiality and extending boundless sincerity, your transforming influence sweeps across the realm like wind bending grass. Yet in the lands of Long and Wei, among the customs of Qian and Qi, the people have grown accustomed to the harsh qi of frigid valleys, forsaking the warmth of yang; they have embraced the yin of foul waters, shunning the solitary radiance of your illumination. Relying on anthill-like fortifications for false security, they nest in tented encampments, clinging to fleeting peace.

Now, with your supreme generals leading the expedition and your mighty armies pressing the assault, your celestial strategies shall surely sever the roots of rebellion. I privately consider that the roads of Hanqu and Baochuan, now gripped by winter’s chill, present perilous paths where frost and snow render the treacherous passes nearly impassable. How easily could they be ascended? To loose a thousand-jun crossbow at a mere minnow or a fly would be as futile as expending the awe of ten thousand chariots upon a desolate, crumbling fortress. I humbly beseech Your Sagely Compassion to heed the will of the people, to revoke the decree, and to await the triumphant news of victory, thereby ensuring the eternal unity of Hua and Yi.

In presumptuous defiance of Your Celestial Majesty’s authority, I am seized by trembling, dread, and overwhelming trepidation. With utmost reverence, I present this memorial at the palace gate, prostrating myself in gratitude.

**Second Memorial**

Your servant has received the imperial decree that the imperial carriage shall proceed to the northern army front, and that the Crown Prince, the chief ministers, and all officials have submitted memorials in earnest petition, yet no assent has been granted.

Though the inspection of regional customs and mores is an ancient rite of the classics, the consolation and reassurance of the troops reflect the compassionate illumination of a sovereign and father.

Yet the journey is fraught with peril—land and water congeal in harsh rigor, while hearts near and far burn with genuine anxiety. I humbly reflect that Your Imperial Majesty embodies the compassion of Yao and surpasses the wisdom of Shun, desiring that all within the four seas bathe in the harmony of your transformative virtue. Yet in the regions of Qian and Long, so close to the frontier, long-standing covenants have been betrayed, and profound trust has been violated. Those who recognize the need for change have already bound themselves to loyalty; those still lost in defiance cling to false security, covering their ears. Thus, the people of this land nurse grievances accumulated over years. They have long witnessed the barking of dogs at Yao, yet yearn for Shun with no means to reach him. Therefore, you have entrusted generals with halberds to marshal the troops and erected altars to swear oaths before the masses. Commands fly like the wind, and valor surges like rain. The might of your commanders shakes the earth like thunder, their resolve firm as iron and stone. They pledge to achieve victory by a set date, ensuring the land’s pacification. Why then should Your Majesty personally ride the jade carriage, wielding white-feathered arrows? Six dragons and eight steeds would traverse treacherous paths; ten thousand riders and a thousand officials would traverse distant peaks beyond. Frost and snow now fall, and biting cold draws near. I humbly beseech Your Celestial Mercy to heed the sentiments of the myriad people and temporarily suspend the command to inspect the frontier. Thus, you will uphold the ancestral altars above and console the hearts of Hua and Yi below. Awaiting the triumphant report, may your realm expand further. Overwhelmed by Your Majesty’s profound favor, I yet feel unworthy of such luminous sincerity. My trespass against your august dignity is unbearable; my longing for grace is urgent, and my prayers are fervent.

**Memorial of Thanks for the Imperial Favor to Renovate Xingsheng Abbey under Master Hongyi Zhang Qian**

Your servant has received the imperial decree granting Master Hongyi Zhang Qian of Xingsheng Abbey on the Left Street the honor of renovating and presiding over the abbey. This grace flows from Your Majesty’s sacred heart, bestowing glory upon the realm of the Dao. The robes of the faithful rejoice, and the sacred groves shine with renewed splendor. I prostrate myself in gratitude, reflecting that Your Majesty’s Dao equals that of the Yellow Emperor and your sagacity rivals that of Emperor Yao. You dwell in thought upon the peaks of Guye and dream of the land of Huaxu. In your care for the great teachings, principle harmonizes with the wellspring of life. The spiritual and the formless merge in non-action, while your mind cherishes those of hidden virtue. Your transformative influence aligns with purity and stillness, benefiting the state and its people. Yet the abbey’s halls stood desolate, its images veiled in dust. Now, your profound favor has been bestowed, commanding its restoration. This abbey, adjacent to the Jade Purity precinct, was once a center of Daoist learning. Later, it was renamed Zhenyuan Abbey, then designated the Purple Ultimate Palace. In the Zhide era, it was renamed Xingsheng, fronting the broad thoroughfare and bordered by the Jin River to the east. Truly a numinous site, a blessed place within the imperial capital. Its gates and halls remain intact, its sacred images preserved. It is a trace of immortals through the ages, a land of fortune for the imperial city. Now, it undergoes thorough renovation, all impurities swept away. Dust is cleared from its humble corners, revealing jade-like visages; tiles and bricks are purged from the overgrown thickets, and a jasper altar is newly raised. Rain and dew nourish the trees, enhancing their splendor; incense and musk adorn the countenances, imbuing them with solemn dignity. Zhang Qian and his peers devote themselves to carving and polishing, faithfully upholding their duties. Evening chimes and morning bells pray for Your Majesty’s longevity; morning incense and evening candles seek the eternal flourishing of the imperial enterprise. I, though unworthy, have been counted among the faithful and personally honored by your radiant favor. My gratitude is boundless.

**Memorial of Thanks for the Imperial Favor of Bestowing a Bell for the Yamen Hall**

Your servant has received the imperial decree bestowing a bell to be struck during rituals in the Riyuan precinct before the Yamen Hall. This grace descends from the heavens, honoring the faithful, filling me with joy beyond measure, and amplifying the radiance of my humble station. I reflect that Your Majesty’s virtue spans the Two Modes and shelters the Three Luminaries.

The radiance of Your Majesty’s grace floods boundlessly, and your benevolence has been bestowed for generations. Thus, the eight seas have stilled their waves, and the great leviathan shall be extinguished in this flourishing age; the five planets follow their constant course, and the mighty comet dissolves into the eternal night. The barbarian and the civilized lands alike have been pacified, and weapons of war sheathed in submission. Yet Your Majesty’s compassion further extends to the mysterious teachings, preserving the profound Daoist path. This has moved the numinous realms to respond, and signs of divine favor have manifested among the immortals. Rightly should Your Majesty’s sacred longevity rival the sun, moon, and stars, and the imperial destiny be exalted above heaven, earth, sea, and mountain.

Now, mindful that within my temple precincts the ritual instruments remain incomplete, and that on days of fasting and offering, the resonant tones of the bell are still absent, I lack the means to commune with the true, and the rites to summon the sacred cannot be harmonized. Yet from the jade steps of the celestial palace, the sound of the sun’s resonance descends from on high; from the bountiful peaks, the frost-laden chime is bestowed upon the mortal realm. This act surpasses the honor of bestowed music, and the grace of this bell’s gift is beyond measure. I shall forever burn fragrant herbs and offer prayers to the true spirits, beseeching the advent of auspicious fortune. Humbly aspiring to repay Your Majesty’s favor, I reverently receive the bestowed bell with incense and gratitude, overwhelmed by gratitude.

**Memorial of Thanks for the Imperial Bestowal of the Jade Bureau’s Laozi Statue**

Your servant humbly acknowledges the imperial decree bestowing the ancient stone statue of Laozi from the Jade Bureau’s grotto gate, to be enshrined and venerated in the western chamber beneath the Imperial Portrait Hall of Longxing Abbey. The accompanying stone canopy has been dismantled and reassembled at the abbey, and funds have been granted for a vegetarian feast for the Daoist assembly, along with banners, flowers, and ceremonial processions to escort the statue to its new home.

The imperial grace descends like a soaking rain, illuminating the gates of the mysterious Dao; the grand thoroughfare is transformed, and Daoists and laity alike rejoice. I, your servant, prostrate in gratitude. I reflect that Your Majesty’s governance unfolds the primordial Dao, ruling with effortless transformation. You have propagated the principles of purity, tranquility, and non-action, and spread the power of emptiness and non-interference. Great peace has been achieved, and unity is at hand. Though the visage of the Primordial Lord has long been near the imperial residence, where incense and lamps are never lacking, the proper place for veneration is within the sacred halls of the Dao. Thus, the imperial command was issued, and the feast was richly prepared. Sandalwood and aloeswood incense waft fragrance, while banners and canopies stand in solemn array. The clamor of golden cymbals and jade chimes has scarcely faded from the palace courtyard before the procession, swift as wind and clouds, arrives at the gates of Longxing Abbey. All hearts gaze in reverence, and the multitude follows in joy. The thunderous acclamation of praise resounds, and the mist of sacred blessings gathers.

I, along with the Daoist assembly, have found refuge in the great teaching and repeatedly received Your Majesty’s profound favor. We shall redouble our devotion in cultivation, striving to repay your sagely grace, overwhelmed by gratitude.

**Memorial of Congratulation on the Recovery of Longzhou**

Your servant has learned that before the northern army, the military governor of Longzhou, Sang Jian, along with his troops and the city itself, has surrendered and returned Longzhou to imperial control. Your Majesty’s far-reaching strategy has been proclaimed, and loyal generals have rendered their service. With but a slight exertion of force, a formidable city has been reclaimed.

I, your servant, prostrate in congratulation. I reflect that Your Majesty’s sagacity surpasses that of the Yellow Emperor, and your martial prowess exceeds that of King Wu of Zhou. Your divine calculations unfold as if held in the palm of your hand, and every move achieves success; you assess formidable enemies as if viewing them within a nutshell, and every strategy is flawless. Since the rebels in the Qi borderlands betrayed their oaths and broke the alliances beyond the passes, they have deeply violated the rites of amity and abruptly severed the bonds of neighborly harmony. Clinging to a pack of jackals and wolves, they relied on the strength of their three regions. Like birds nesting in broken reeds, they sought fleeting security, or like one sitting atop a pile of firewood, they claimed false stability. The lesser failing to serve the greater is a crime the *Spring and Autumn Annals* condemns. Thus, righteous warriors lifted their gaze in indignation, and strategists clenched their fists in resolve, all resolved to eradicate the threat and take up arms.

The six armies surged forward in eagerness, and the eight encampments silently roused their courage. They trampled the dust in anticipation of crushing Wu Peak, and watered their horses at the Wei River, preparing to pay homage. Sang Jian, adapting wisely to changing circumstances and discerning the right path, laid down his weapons and presented jade in surrender, offering his allegiance. He has presented a thousand *li* of mountains and rivers without a single blade being drawn, and restored a region of households and populace without the slightest harm. The blades of the imperial army have been sheathed, and the masses of Shang and Shou have been reclaimed without effort. Envisioning the roads of Huizhong, the rebels find no path of retreat; gazing upon the solemnity of Bashang, they realize nowhere to flee. It is certain that the vile shall soon be captured and executed. Behold the unity of the eight rivers and three mountains, and the eternal dominion over the nine provinces and four seas. All shall be encompassed within the reign of Shun and the domain of Yu.

I, your servant, have been blessed to witness this flourishing era and repeatedly behold such great victories, overwhelmed by gratitude.

**Memorial Presenting the Statue of the Perfected Zhang on the Birthday of the Celestial Han**

In the second month and eighth day of the first year of Tianhan, your servant humbly observes that the imperial enterprise shines eternally, and the Supreme Emperor bestows auspicious omens. From the northern pole and the jade pivot of the heavens, a radiant rainbow light heralds the birth of Your Majesty’s sagely brilliance...

In the central heavens, the jade Dipper gathers purple lightning to congeal its splendor. The myriad states rejoice in reverent gaze, and the hearts of all people swell with exultation. We humbly reflect that Your Majesty embodies the luminous spirit of Heaven and Earth, and the Nine Heavens amass auspicious omens. Your perfect governance fills the cosmos, and Your clarity and solemnity command the reverence of gods and spirits. Having laid the grand foundation for thirty generations, Your reign now surpasses the glory of the Zhou; having ushered in four hundred years of radiant fortune, Your enterprise is poised to transcend the legacy of the Han. Your profound virtue and grace extend to the dark-haired people, and the balmy winds of Your benevolence stir both Hua and Yi lands.

Now, as the grand festival of Shouchun approaches and the sacred day of Your Majesty’s birth draws near, tribute pours in like clouds, and vessels from across the waves converge. All offer the humble gift of celery in observance, continuing the mountain-shaking acclamations. Together with the Daoist priests of this abbey, I reverently sweep the resplendent altar, meticulously following the secret rituals. We chant the sacred texts with jade-like clarity, unfurling scrolls veiled in mist. The frost-white silks are immaculately arrayed, and our purified sincerity shall eternally expand the blessings of Heaven and Earth.

The Perfected Zhang, once a disciple of the Daoist Patriarch, personally received the sacred scriptures. He transmitted the true records of the Primordial Heaven and sealed the jade texts in the blessed realms. He foresaw the flourishing of the imperial enterprise and penetrated the mysteries of the Dao’s pivot. When compared to Song Gao’s recognition of the Divine Yao or Tao Hongjing’s acquaintance with Emperor Wu of Liang, his discernment and virtue are beyond parallel. Thus, we dare to adorn the silk with elegant embellishments, offering this image for veneration. Through the burning of incense, may we perpetuate the auspicious blessings. With utmost reverence and trepidation, I present this memorial, unworthy as I am to approach Your Majesty’s august presence.

The details of the painted image’s merits and virtues are respectfully submitted to the palace gates for Your Majesty’s perusal, awaiting Your sacred decree.

**Memorial of Thanks for the Bestowal of Purple Robes and Daoist Titles upon Huang Wanyou and Deng Baijing**

I, your servant, observe that by Your Majesty’s sacred edict, the Daoist priest Huang Wanyou of Kuizhou has been granted purple robes and a Daoist title, and the Daoist priest Deng Baijing of Luojiang County has been bestowed purple robes. The Great Sage rules the heavens, and His divine works extend to all things. Within the court, worthy and capable ministers assist; beyond its walls, no worthy person is left unrecognized. All within the realm pay homage, rightfully so under the radiance of Your sagely reign.

I, your servant, humbly express my gratitude. Huang Wanyou and his peers have long embraced their aspirations in the forests, gathering like deer in the wilderness, dwelling deep among the cliffs and vines, untouched by fame or profit. Some possess the power of cinnabar and flowers to revive the dying and halt the advance of time; others wield vermilion talismans to expel demons and dispel misfortune. All have expanded the application of the Dao, subtly aiding this enlightened era. Suddenly, imperial summons arrived like crane-borne decrees, calling them to the phoenix gates of the palace. Wanyou hastened from the brocade-laden waters, and Baijing journeyed from Luojiang. Together, they gaze upon the heavens of Yao and bask in the grace of Shun. Surveying the annals of history, none can compare to this honor.

We humbly reflect that Your Majesty’s Dao surpasses that of Tang Yao, and Your achievements tower above those of the Yellow Emperor. Even in the days when the spirit congealed by the Fen River, the Ninefold Gates remained distant; when the carriage was labored to Mount Kongtong for counsel, the journey was arduous. Yet now, the imperial reed-boats arrive in abundance, and cassia-oared vessels come like clouds. They forsake the mist-laden vines and personally attend the imperial throne. With illustrious titles conferred and splendid robes bestowed, their glory shall shine in the records and illuminate the humble headdresses of Daoist priests. I am overwhelmed with gratitude beyond measure.

*End of Guangcheng Collection, Volume One*
*Guangcheng Collection, Volume Two*

The Memorial of Thanks for the Imperial Summons to Meet with Grand Master Hongdao Huang Wanyou, Composed by Du Guangting, Court-Appointed Literary Master of the Supreme Clarity Palace in the Upper Capital, Bestowed the Purple Robe

Your servant humbly states: By imperial decree, I was commanded to proceed to the Inner Privy Council to meet with Grand Master Hongdao, Huang Wanyou.

Heavenly kindness extends its compassion, stooping to embrace the frail and lowly. The burden of grace is too weighty to bear; my awe and honor redouble without end.

Your servant prostrates himself in gratitude. I humbly reflect that Your Majesty’s transformation is vast and rooted in the Dao, and Your governance upholds perfect benevolence. Your toil and care extend to all quarters, and Your compassion leaves nothing untouched. Thus, reclusive scholars who slumber among clouds hasten their hearts toward the imperial court from afar, and lofty men who scorn the world now fully comprehend the rites of attending the Son of Heaven.

Grand Master Hongdao has long delved into the profound arts and dwelled in seclusion among towering peaks. Though his name and fame were known, his form remained unseen. Now, heeding the imperial summons, he has come directly to the palace gates, exchanging his hempen sash and lotus robe for the honored purple vestments and the title of Grand Master. This event shall illuminate the annals of history and bring glory to the Daoist gate.

By Your sagely grace, I was commanded to meet with him, receiving the favor of Your radiant wisdom and beholding the countenance of a crane soaring among clouds. My steps tread the celestial precincts of the Jasper Pool, ascending the immortal isles of Penglai. I am overwhelmed by this extraordinary favor, my honor shining upon ten thousand lives.

Yet how can one as insignificant as a wren or sparrow repay the virtue of Heaven and Earth?

Your servant is at a loss.

---

*Memorial Submitted at the Jade Bureau of the Dragon Prosperity Abbey*

Previously, on the twenty-second day of the tenth month of this year, Your servant received an imperial edict bestowing an old Jade Bureau abbey hall, along with a stone statue of the Venerable Lord Lao, to be relocated to the present abbey. Now, upon the completion of the new hall constructed on the foundation of the lecture hall behind the main殿, the stone statue of the Venerable Lord Lao has been duly installed for offerings and reverence.

The sacred mountains and great rivers, the Twenty-Four Transformations, and the seasonal sacrifices of spring and autumn are all prescribed in ancient rites. For the regular offerings at the Jade Bureau Transformation, I humbly request that they commence on the eighth day of the second month of the first year of the Tianhan era, to be conducted by the local prefecture and county officials before the stone statue of the Venerable Lord Lao at the Jade Bureau within the Dragon Prosperity Abbey. May this prevent any neglect and align with reverent devotion.

Moreover, the Northern Mang Transformation in Junzhou has lacked offerings and prayers for many years. As it lies within the realm, it is fitting to restore the proper rites. For this transformation as well, I propose that it be conducted at the Dragon Prosperity Abbey alongside the Jade Bureau rites. May the extended blessings bring eternal fortune to the sagely court.

I respectfully submit the above for Your Majesty’s consideration and await Your imperial decree.

A Memorial on the Emperor’s Establishment of a Vegetarian Feast for the Crown Prince’s Birthday

Your servant humbly receives Your Majesty’s sacred decree, which, in celebration of the Crown Prince’s birthday, bestows sixty strings of cash from the Manor and Estate Treasury. These funds are to be disbursed at the Northern Emperor’s Abbey, where twenty-one selected Daoist clerics shall be dispatched to inaugurate a seven-day-and-night Yellow Register Daoist ritual on the eighth day of the seventh month, concluding with the dispersal of the vegetarian feast on the fifteenth.

As the purple qi fills the court and the Eastern Palace brings forth a sage, joyous voices resound across the Six Directions, and felicitous qi congeals within the Ninefold Enclosure. All within the realm reverently offer their congratulations. Your Majesty’s grace extends throughout the realm, and Your compassion embraces Your ministers. Mindful that the Crown Prince has long been devoted to self-cultivation and ever cherishes frugality, You fear that unwarranted expenditures might deplete the people’s resources and burden their labors. Thus, all government offices have been instructed to curtail their ritual observances. Yet from the Inner Treasury, funds and goods have been specially allocated to open a sacred altar within the abbey, invoking the Perfected Ones of the Jade Capital and Golden Gates, and amplifying the blessings of the Radiant Hall and the Four Quarters. This noble rite surpasses even the finest precedents of antiquity.

Your servant, having received this august command, shall proceed with reverent offerings and prayers. Witnessing this renewed grace and beholding the vast and magnanimous design, I am overcome with boundless joy. With utmost reverence, I record this memorial in celebration and respectfully submit it for Your Majesty’s consideration.

---

A Memorial on the Yellow Register Ritual at the Venerable Lord Lao’s Hall

Your servant humbly receives the imperial decree instructing that at the Northern Emperor’s Abbey, before the Most High Lord Lao, a three-day Yellow Register Daoist ritual be conducted, concluding with the dispersal of the vegetarian feast. Sixty strings of cash from the Manor and Estate Treasury are to be disbursed, and twenty-one selected Daoist clerics are to be dispatched to perform the rites of recitation and repentance with utmost purity and devotion.

Your Majesty’s achievements surpass those of the Five Emperors, and Your virtue excels that of the Three Sovereigns. From beneath the suspended tassels of Your crown, the winds of the Dao are spread abroad; from behind the upright screen, the transformation of non-action is unfurled.

Your Majesty’s profound intent moves in secret, and the myriad spirits respond in silent communion; Your sagely thoughts extend afar, and the four seas follow like clouds to attend the Sacred. Thus do Heaven and Earth unite in harmony, sun and moon shine with unblemished radiance, the years yield abundance and peace, and winds and rains come in due season. Where the divine spear points, the long serpents and great boars are all subdued; where Your boundless grace extends, drought demons and lurking dragons retreat of themselves. Thereupon, from the immortal mountains and secluded grottoes, auspicious omens arise in ceaseless succession; jade seals and bronze talismans, pillars of good fortune, appear in due course.

Now, as You deliver the realm from the calamity of overflowing chaos and raise an army like timely rain, You shall expand the Eight Seas to unite all under one rule. Yet still, with reverent heart, You honor the teachings of the Mysterious, yielding virtue to the august heavens. On this day of the Zhongyuan Festival, when purity is observed, You prepare the assembly of incense and flowers across the Three Realms, repaying the sacred power of the Primordial Lord and opening the precious altar of the Yellow Register. Through this, boundless blessings shall be secured, great fortune firmly established, and Your jade-like reign and sagely longevity perpetuated.

Your servant, favored by Your exalted grace, humbly presents this report in praise of Your virtuous decree. With utmost sincerity, I reverently offer prayers through the burning of incense. The weight of this honor is beyond bearing.

This memorial is respectfully submitted to express gratitude for the proclamation of peace and the pacification of the frontier.

Your servant, [Name], prostrates to receive the sacred edict, which proclaims the memorial submitted by the eastern and northern frontier armies. The report details the return of the surrendered officials Jian Wang and Yan Liu from Fengxiang, who have provided intelligence on the rebels’ affairs, along with popular ballads foretelling the pacification of the frontier by the coming year.

Your servant ventures to declare: The Dao of Heaven is subtle and profound, silently overseeing the signs of fortune; the workings of the divine are obscure yet truly govern blessings and omens. Thus, the words of folk songs serve to herald auspicious decrees. In ancient times, the green youth’s ballad on the broad roads of Wu foretold its fall; the strange bird descending upon the high terrace in Chen presaged its destruction. The flight of the five stars marked the moment Yu Shun received the realm; the transformation of a horse into a dragon signaled the rise of Emperor Yuan. All these arose from the will of Heaven, resonating deeply in the hearts of the people. Upon careful examination, such propitious words invariably reflect the sagely virtue of the ruler.

Your Majesty, inheriting the Mandate of Heaven and manifesting divine wisdom, has responded to the joyous acclamation of the multitudes, governing the seas and mountains; bearing the cherished charge of the vast heavens, You have delivered and saved all living beings. The treasures and sacred talismans of the realm have arrived unbidden; rare tributes from distant lands and border tribes have come in droves, drawn by the radiance of Your rule. Yet the northern frontier, ungrateful for Your grace, has turned its back on righteousness, perching upon a pyre only to invite its own conflagration, standing at the edge of a reed only to ensure its own destruction. Now, the divine has revealed its portents, and the streets and alleys hum with prophecy. The words thus proclaimed bear the promise of swift victory. The "frontier" mentioned refers to the lands beyond the nation’s strategic passes. At this time of the nation’s strength, under the leadership of the "rain-bringing" army, the divine will speaks, and auspicious light manifests. The ballad of the coming reign foretells triumph over the enemy, and success is within reach. Soon, the Three Qin shall be pacified, and all under heaven shall be unified under Your rule. May Your jade-like reign and precious destiny endure as long as heaven and earth.

Your servant, favored by the celestial benevolence, has personally heard these auspicious words. I humbly present my shallow insights, trespassing upon Your sacred dignity, overwhelmed by the weight of this honor.

**Memorial of Gratitude for the Bestowal of the Tianxi Abbey Estate**

Your servant, [Name], prostrates to receive the sacred grace, which has decreed the bestowal of one estate in Tongji County, Hanzhou, formerly belonging to Tang Youze, upon the Tianxi Abbey, to be held in perpetuity as its permanent endowment.

Your Majesty, inheriting the Mandate of Heaven and responding to the cosmic order, has extended Your sacred robes to govern. The grand design was preordained in the Upper Clarity, and the precious registers have emerged from the depths of the earth. The renovation of the abbey’s halls fittingly answers the auspicious omens. The images in the Three Halls are majestic and solemn, and the incense and flowers offered year-round are pure and refined. Now, You have specially bestowed Your sagely favor, generously granting estates and fields, converting fertile lands into permanent endowments. The imperial benevolence descends from on high, enhancing the glory of the Daoist teachings. Henceforth, the daily provisions for vegetarian meals shall be secured without want; morning incense and evening candles shall burn with undivided devotion. May this pray for the eternal prolongation of Your sacred longevity and the everlasting prosperity of Your grand foundation.

Your servant, undeservingly honored by Your sacred reward and personally favored with extraordinary grace, is overwhelmed by this honor.

**Memorial of Gratitude for the Renovation of the Zhangren Abbey by the Monk Xingzhen**

Your servant, [Name], prostrates to observe the memorial of the Great Master Monk Xingzhen, which reports the completion of the renovation of the True Lord Zhangren Hall on Mount Qingcheng, as decreed by Your sacred edict.

Your Majesty, in Your benevolence, governs all directions, and Your compassion extends to both teachings. The Jetavana Grove and Penglai Isle alike share in the grace of Your reverence and adornment; the Deer Park and the Turtle Palace together receive the gift of Your renovations. Now, for this abode of the immortals, You have specially commanded a eminent monk to undertake the carving and construction, bringing to completion its magnificent splendor. The newly completed hall stands deep and resplendent, forever anchoring the court of blessings. May the spirits of the Five Peaks and Ten Caves augment Your longevity, matching the heavens in enduring kalpas.

Your servant, dwelling within the Daoist teachings and personally favored by the imperial grace, is overwhelmed by this honor.

**Memorial for the Daoist Ritual and Abstinence on the Birthday of the Imperial Prince**

Your servant, [Name], prostrates to declare: The Nine Heavens have gathered their blessings, and the Three Luminaries have congealed their auspicious signs. The moving pivot of the palace radiates light, and the spring chamber of the Eastern Palace brings forth a scion of excellence. All within the realm, from the Hua to the Yi, rejoice as one. The Emperor has generously dispensed coins and treasures, devoutly observing the fast to accumulate merit. May the Upper Clarity look upon this with favor, bestowing boundless longevity upon Your sacred person; may the Perfect Dao confer blessings, bringing a thousand auspicious signs to the heir apparent. May the great treasure flourish and the Nine Regions be eternally governed.

Your servants, having diligently performed the rites of incense and purification, are honored to receive the imperial bestowals, overwhelmed by awe and reverence.

**Memorial of Gratitude for the Approval of the Honorific Title**

Your servant, [Name], prostrates to receive the imperial decree approving the honorific title proposed by the ministers and myself.

Our earnest petition has been presented above, and the imperial brilliance has gazed upon it below. By the Mandate of Heaven, all within the realm rejoice as one.

We humbly reflect: The Emperor, like the black bird that heralded the rise of Shang, and the red omens that marked the founding of Han, has rescued the world from fire and flood, endowed by the divine with a talent for the age; with the sun’s halo and the moon’s mystery, Heaven has bestowed its timely signs. Your majestic achievements and sagely virtue surpass those of former dynasties; encompassing the celestial reckoning and expanding the grand foundation, You have reverently received the precious Mandate. Thus, the Three Spirits have altered their divination, and the myriad states have submitted. You surpass the rulers of Tang and Wu, who marshaled their armies with axes; You scorn the founders of Wei and Sui, who bullied the weak and oppressed the orphaned. Shaking Your robes, You bring peace to the Nine Regions; with Your crown tassels still, You illuminate the great treasure. Inheriting the golden destiny of the Yellow Emperor, wielding the talismans of the White Emperor, You hold the golden mirror to illuminate the world, uniting the spirits and the people in harmony; grasping the jade armillary, You survey the seas and islands, as the multitudes joyfully acclaim Your rule. Thus, at the Upright Gate, auspicious vapors fill the halls; upon the Circular Mound, divine soldiers attend Your retinue. At the ancestral temple, dark clouds gather in volumes, and the moon shines brightly at midnight; bearing the grand title, white mist lightly ascends, and smoke envelops the broad steps. Unicorns appear in the ponds, dragons leap in the river rapids; plants and trees bear patterns, clouds and rosy dawns display their hues. Golden talismans dance in their scripts, and jade seals radiate their light. Though You defer to the virtue of the Upper Mystery, Your deeds already fill the annals of the Grand Historians.

Moreover, from the ends of the earth to the farthest frontiers, from the northern deserts to the southern wilds, rare treasures are arrayed in the bright court, and divine steeds are presented from the celestial stables. Precious incense arrives from distant lands, and exquisite jade is offered from foreign realms. Like Emperor Wu of Han, who received tributes from the four corners, You bestow the correct calendar; like Emperor Gaozong of Tang, who unified the myriad states, they now seek to share in Your culture and governance. Soon, You shall restore the ancient boundaries of Yu, and further expand the lands of Yao.

The hundred offices follow their seasons in perfect order, and the six harmonies of music resound in concord. Trust extends even to the creatures of land and water, and grace embraces all that moves and grows. You pardon debts long overdue and relieve the imprisoned, reducing punishments. No star of imprisonment appears in the heavens, nor does the earth bear the ominous *qi* of slaughter. Captives, their necks bound in ropes, are spared the axe and halberd’s might; even the guilty kin of condemned rebels receive grants of silk and coin. Sacrificial beasts are fat and sleek, and grain offerings pure and abundant. Thus do You dare to manifest reverence before the divine, honoring the worthy with robes and caps. Your sincere heart reaches Heaven and Earth, and Your utmost devotion is displayed in the suburban rites. Every feeling finds response, and every movement meets timely favor.

You do not flaunt extravagance nor indulge in delicate splendor. No excess attends Your pleasures, nor do You fall prey to dissipation. You do not delight in reckless riding nor yield to the chase or the hunt. In stillness, You are solemn and stern; in action, You adhere to ritual and precedent. Wealth is abundant and the people harmonious; violence is forbidden and the populace secure. The grand review corrects martial prowess, and the great muster displays the army’s might. A million fierce warriors stand ready, all equipped with chariots and arms. The finest stallions—thousands strong, each a dragon’s descendant—are rebuffed; the swiftest steeds, worthy of Sun Yang, are rewarded for loyalty and filial piety. Talent and ability are broadly sought: no good deed is overlooked, and even the smallest merit is recorded. Those devoted to the classics are spurred by lofty examinations; recluses of pure integrity are bound by noble rank. Rewards encourage diligence and strengthen the foundation, while farming is promoted and agriculture urged. The year yields abundant grain in the fields, and the granaries overflow with the season’s plenty. The countryside teems with ripening crops like clouds, and the nation prospers as households grow rich. No beacon fires trouble the four frontiers, and within a hundred *li*, songs and joy abound.

Generals blaze like stars with martial prowess, their achievements towering and their ranks resplendent; scholars rise like mountains with vast learning, their Confucian influence majestic and profound. Though Sun Quan once flourished south of the Yangtze and Liu Bei held the southwest, when compared to Your surpassing merit, how faint their glory appears. Now the passes and rivers are at peace, watchtowers silent, and neighboring states exchange envoys bearing gifts. Nearby borders lay down their weapons. The people rejoice in wealth and longevity, governance is harmonious and prosperous, and loyal ministers—civil and military—long to enhance Your glorious virtue. From within and without, all humbly beseech You, and the lands of Hua and Yi speak with one voice. May You indeed restore the radiance of sun and moon, and in Your benevolence, bestow the imperial assent.

Wearing the round heaven as a crown and treading the square earth as a mat, all within the realm and beneath the sky rejoice. As we await the appointed day of the grand ceremony, gazing upon the lofty heavens, we leap for joy.

---

Your servants, along with the assembled Daoist clergy, cannot contain our exultation, our jubilation, and our fervent devotion.

**Memorial Requesting Restoration of the Original Surname**

Your servant has heard that the lineage of the unshakable rock admits no other clan, and the weight of the ramparts’ defense truly rests upon its own branches. To establish enduring and grand principles, one must properly define the distinctions of kinship. Your servant, though versed in literary arts, is ignorant of martial classics. Yet, having trodden the path of war, I early received the grace of Your celestial favor. Wielding spear and sword, my sole intent was to repay my lord; in northern expeditions and southern campaigns, I ever swore to serve the throne with devotion.

Since Your Majesty has marshaled heroes and swept clean the realm, I have been mindful of even the slightest service. In recognition of my humble efforts, You have bestowed extraordinary grace, granting me kinship and placing me among the imperial lineage. Yet, I strive to dedicate my life, hoping to repay Your sagely favor.

Now, as the cosmos undergoes transformation, Heaven and Earth bestow their blessings. The virtue of earth subtly shifts, and the mandate of metal begins its course. Responding to the acclamation of Hua and Yi, You fulfill the allegiance of the myriad peoples. Seated in tranquility, the divine regalia come to You, as in the abdication of Shun; governing with reverence, the dragon chart is inaugurated without the need for Zhou’s conquest. The sacred lineage of Mount Gou shall endure as the heavens, and the jade source of the Huai River shall last as the earth. The majestic imperial succession must be upheld by the unbroken line of descendants; the vast imperial foundation cannot be mingled with the offspring of common gates.

Reflecting upon myself, I find that honor has only deepened my anxiety. Thus, I dare to lay bare my earnest plea, though it risks offending the imperial scales. I seek to distinguish noble from base and forever order the celestial from the mortal. I humbly beseech Your sagely compassion to permit Your servant to return to his original surname. In presuming to offend Your august dignity, I await punishment, overwhelmed by tears of gratitude and prostrate in awe.

**Memorial on the Solar Eclipse That Did Not Occur**

Your servant observes that the Bureau of Astronomy has reported that on the first day of this month, at the *dingwei* hour (9–11 a.m.) and four *ke* (one *ke* = 14.4 minutes), the sun was to be eclipsed at 11 degrees in the constellation *Zhen*, and was to be restored to fullness by the *wei* hour (1–3 p.m.) and four *ke*. Yet, upon verification, no eclipse occurred.

The sun’s brilliance ascends, and the ruler’s virtue equals its majesty. Surpassing the calculations of astronomers, it did not wane, revealing Your sagely luminosity and responsive perception.

**Memorial of Gratitude**

Your servant prostrates himself in reverence, reflecting that Your Imperial Majesty, born of the primal yang, has brought forth sagely radiance, and the two luminaries shine with equal brilliance. Rising like the fusang tree in the eastern palace, Your pure splendor illuminates the Qian Dao. Embodying the winter sun’s warmth, Your grace flows to the Nine Regions; emulating the spring breeze’s kindness, Your mercy extends to all beneath heaven. Thus, the great light gains luster, its brilliance beyond the reach of measuring instruments. In perfect accord with the singular blessing of heaven and earth, it transcends the ordinary bounds of yin and yang. Auspicious radiance grows ever more resplendent, and Your mysterious virtue moves heaven. Surpassing the Han’s twice-restored sun and eclipsing Yao’s conjoined luminaries, this glory shall be inscribed in the annals of history, crowning all celestial charts.

Your servant, privileged to witness this flourishing era, has beheld such gracious favor. Looking back upon the twilight of my years, my heart, like the sunflower, turns ever more fervently toward the sun. Words fail to express my boundless joy.

---

**Memorial on the Completion of the Renovation of the Hall of the Perfected Lord at the Zhangren Abbey**

Your servant humbly notes that Master Xingzhen of Changping Mountain has reported the completion of the reconstruction of the grand hall of the Perfected Lord at Zhangren Abbey, as commanded by Your August Decree.

The sagely enterprise spreads far and wide, and the immortal sanctuary is renewed. A monumental achievement is accomplished, and the numinous traces gain greater glory. Your servant reflects that Your Majesty’s virtue permeates all directions, and Your benevolence extends to both teachings. The civilizing influence reaches distant lands, where even foreign courts offer sincerity; martial prowess shines forth, and barbarian tribes heed commands as stern as frost and snow. From the palaces of Penglai to the gardens of Nai, all are restored and rebuilt. Within the realm, all gaze upon the rites of music; both Chinese and foreigners recognize the teachings of the Daoist and Buddhist clergy. Such merit surpasses antiquity, and such glory outshines former kings.

Last winter, as the Zhangren Abbey had stood for many years and its halls and corridors had fallen into disrepair, You commanded eminent monks to oversee its reconstruction and bestowed resources to ensure its flourishing. Thus, stones were quarried from distant mountains, timber felled in secluded valleys. Fine beams were hewn for use, and craftsmen applied their skills. In no time, a magnificent edifice stood firm, rivaling the heavens in grandeur. Its soaring eaves gaze upon the sun, its vast terraces span the sky. Clouds brush against its lofty beams, winds whisper through its lattice windows. Though its walls and foundations remain unchanged, the painted murals appear freshly rendered. Hills are leveled to open courtyards, and streams are diverted to protect the steps. No rushing currents can reach it, no flying stones can assail it. This wondrous achievement manifests Your sagely and divine benevolence. Such extraordinary merit shall endure forever, prolonging Your sacred longevity without end.

Your servant, though unworthy, has long stood at the gates of the mysterious, deeply bathed in Your imperial grace. With reverence, I burn incense to repay Your radiant kindness.

---

**Memorial on the Thanksgiving Ritual for the New Hall of the Zhangren Abbey and the Installation of the Earth Deity**

Your servant humbly received Your August Decree, commanding that a thanksgiving ritual be held to consecrate the newly completed hall of the Zhangren Abbey on Mount Qingcheng and to install the earth deity.

Your servant reflects that Your Majesty’s benevolence encompasses land and sea, and Your grace extends to both Confucian and Daoist teachings. Turning toward the sacred mountain, You bestow favor upon the immortal abbey. Its halls and chambers had long fallen into ruin, and the restoration of its teachings had no means to proceed. By Your sagely command, a true monk was appointed, and the nation’s resources were allocated. The grandeur of the reconstruction seemed divinely wrought, its towering magnificence rivaling the works of the gods. May this blessed foundation endure forever, as eternal as heaven itself.

Your servant, honored by Your sagely favor, has reverently prepared the ritual altar. With solemn incense and candles, I have performed the rites, offering thanks to the true spirits. Amid cloud-wreathed peaks and misty valleys, I seem to hear the echoes of "Long live the Emperor!" The jade registers and golden talismans further extend Your reign, multiplying Your years like the thousand-cycles of the *chun* tree.

Having completed the ritual on the twenty-third day of this month, I now return and respectfully present this memorial at the palace gates to report on the proceedings.

---

**Memorial Congratulating the Presentation of the Divine Sword and Offering a Poem**

Your servant humbly notes that Zhao Kuangye has today presented a divine sword retrieved from the river at Hezhou, which has been displayed throughout the realm.

Your servant reflects that as the era of grand peace dawns, auspicious omens must appear. To purge evil and calamity, a divine sword has manifested. It aids Your sagely power in severing malevolence and embodies the heavens’ and earth’s support.

Your servant reverently considers that Your Majesty’s merit surpasses the Three Sovereigns and Five Emperors, Your awe commands the world, Your benevolence reaches both seen and unseen realms, and Your Dao equals heaven and earth. Thus, mountains and rivers, forests and valleys emit golden flames from towering cliffs; winds and rains, thunder and lightning reveal frost-edged blades across ten thousand *li*. This single strip of autumn water first reveals its earth-emerging form; this several-foot gleam of tempered light displays its sky-leaning might. Its transformations further manifest its divine marvels.

In ancient times, the First Emperor of Qin retrieved such a sword from the river’s heart and indeed swallowed the Six Kingdoms. Now, Your Majesty has obtained it from the river’s surface, and You shall unite all under heaven. Who could compare to its jade-cutting, metal-slicing edge? What blade that beheaded horses or severed serpents could rival it?

Your servant, honored to live in this flourishing age, has witnessed this wondrous omen. I humbly offer a poem in praise, wishing to extol Your sagely influence. With reverence, I present a regulated verse of seven characters per line, four rhymes, in tribute to Your sacred virtue. I presume to offend Your august dignity, overwhelmed by awe.

---

**Memorial Congratulating the Execution of Liu Zhijun**

Your servant humbly notes that by Your August Decree, Liu Zhijun, for his persistent violence and cruelty, has been executed.

His crimes had reached their full measure, and both men and gods were outraged. Rightly did Your sagely judgment mete out stern punishment. Your servant rejoices with boundless joy, bowing his head in reverence.

Your servant reflects that Liu Zhijun was by nature treacherous and cunning, his abilities base and mediocre. His heart harbored the greed of a ravenous wolf, yet he lacked any intent to repay kindness or cherish grace. Driven by desperation, he submitted to our great court. You bestowed upon him the boundless mercy of rain and dew, then entrusted him with command and banner. Though his appointment was extraordinary, You placed unwavering trust in him. You further elevated him with the utmost favor, granting him sole authority over military campaigns.

Yet he raged with unbridled arrogance, his heart filled with cruelty. He slaughtered the common people, flouting laws and decrees. He subverted the court’s policy of pacification and betrayed Your sagely benevolence in punishing and comforting the realm. Having betrayed Your boundless mercy, he could not escape the manifest punishment.

Your servant reverently considers that Your Majesty’s benevolence spans heaven and earth, Your kindness surpasses that of Yao and Tang. Embracing the supreme Dao, You cherish life; spreading the warmth of spring, You illuminate all things. The barbarian tribes of the four directions all know the depth of Your compassion; the sun, moon, and stars all witness the vastness of Your magnanimity.

Yet Liu Zhijun alone defied Your sagely enterprise, wantonly wielding cruel punishments. His actions obstructed the distant lands’ path to enlightenment and hindered the four directions’ turn toward civilization. Now, the thunderous decree has struck, and the axe of execution has fallen. Thus, all under heaven rejoice in the virtue of eradicating evil and eliminating malevolence.

May the imperial lineage flourish through the ages, and the people forever enjoy blessings.

Your servant, [Name], having witnessed the majesty of Your celestial authority, is overwhelmed with boundless joy and exultation.

**Memorial Congratulating the Revival of Withered Cypress Trees at Crane Cry Mountain**

Your servant, [Name], humbly observes that Commissioner for Military Training of Qiongzhou, Zhang Jingzhou, has memorialized regarding the report from Guo Zhaomei, Master of Mysterious Unity at Crane Cry Mountain in Dayi County. Within an ancient cypress grove, seven withered trees, barren for many years, have suddenly revived, their branches and leaves flourishing with extraordinary vigor. The prefectural authorities dispatched officials to verify the phenomenon, confirming its authenticity.

A divine mountain’s auspicious omen, a propitious tree’s manifestation—this marvel attests to the resonance of Your sagely virtue and the flourishing nurturance of divine power. Your servant is utterly overjoyed, bowing his head in reverence again and again.

According to the *Auspicious Omens Record*: When an emperor’s virtue extends to plants and trees, and governance achieves great peace, pines and cypresses remain evergreen, and trees display wondrous anomalies.
