**Lower Prime**
As the Dark Emperor governs the season and the Water Official orders the time, this is the season for seeking blessings and extending grace, a period for concentrating the mind and purifying the thoughts. Moreover, the Jade Bureau’s immortal traces and the jade altar’s grand rites are observed. For nine periods, prayers are offered, surely bringing auspicious blessings; for three days, the fast is solemnly kept, daring to join in repentance and gratitude. I hope that misfortunes will cease, karmic debts be dissolved, sins be absolved, and the living and the dead together enjoy peace. I vow to forever uphold my devotion in gratitude for the mystic grace.

---

**Lu Wei, Grand Master for Assisting the Prime, Offers Hymns for the Upper Prime Yellow Register Rite**
I prostrate myself, acknowledging that the Great Dao pervades all, the Three Primes establish their teachings, and the bright scrutiny of their judgment leaves nothing, however minute, unexamined. Early in life, I admired the mysteries of the void and from the first revered purity. With each display of reverent devotion, I have prayed for the shining mercy of their protection. Now, at the Jade Bureau’s sacred altar and the Upper Prime’s assembly of blessings, I humbly present incense and candles to assist in the fast and offerings. I pray for the dissolution of misfortunes, the cleansing of sins, the eradication of illnesses and hardships, and the augmentation of my years.

**Lu Wei, Grand Master for Assisting the Prime, Offers Hymns for the Upper, Middle, and Lower Prime Yellow Register Rites**

May the merit of good deeds extend to both the living and the departed, and may blessings of prosperity embrace all kin. With unceasing devotion, I strive to fulfill the boundless grace of the Dao.

**Upper Prime**
At this season of scrutiny, when the auspicious hour precedes spring’s renewal, the Upper Prime’s festival of bright judgment arrives—the very time when all beings find ease. With utmost sincerity, I offer my reverent prayers. Now, in the radiant transformation of the Brocade Capital and at the Jade Bureau’s jade altar, where the true rites of the Yellow Register unfold and the grand liturgy of the Mysterious Code is displayed, I humbly present incense and offerings to aid this virtuous cause. I pray that the host of sages and the myriad Perfected Ones, in their mercy, will witness my devotion and bestow blessings: universal grace upon the living and the dead, the far-reaching absolution of sins, the dissolution of misfortunes before they manifest, and the renewal of fortune and longevity. With an enduring heart, I seek to align with the profound favor of the Dao.

**Middle Prime**
As the four beginnings cycle through the year and the Three Primes establish their registers, their scrutiny pierces the bright and the obscure, leaving nothing unexamined. I have long upheld the Daoist precepts and early embraced the mysteries of the void. At every auspicious gathering, I have redoubled my devotion. Now, as the Jade Bureau’s Frost Altar completes its rites for the Morning of the Prime, I present incense and candles to assist in the purification of the fast. I pray for the great mercy of pardon, the descent of celestial blessings, the healing of illnesses, and the extension of life’s span. I reverently commend the spirits of my ancestors and seek grace for all my kin. May I forever receive their vast protection and honor the primal merit.

**Lower Prime**
As the virtue of Water aligns with the season and the dark winter unfolds, this is the time when the two qi retreat in solemn stillness and the assembly of celestial scrutiny convenes. It is fitting to rouse the will toward the profound and concentrate the mind upon the supreme Dao, to cleanse faults, repent transgressions, and beseech blessings and favor. Moreover, at the Jade Bureau’s imperial altar and the Brocade Capital’s assembly of blessings, I dare to prepare incense and offerings to join in the fast and rites. For three days, I maintain solemn reverence; at nine intervals, I present my repentance. I hope to receive manifest protection and the abundant bestowal of auspicious signs: the ascension of my ancestors, the liberation of the departed, the deliverance of the living and the dead, and the dissolution of misfortunes. May grievances be released in the nocturnal courts, and sins erased from the earthly records. May illnesses be healed, life’s span lengthened, and my vow of steadfast devotion ever align with the protection of the Perfected Ones.

*End of Scroll Four of the* Guangcheng Collection
*Scroll Five of the* Guangcheng Collection *begins*

To the Most Sacred Supreme Clarity Palace in the Upper Capital, the Eminent Virtue of Literary Works for Imperial Service, Purple-Robed Bestowed Du Guangting, composes:

**Prayer for the Yellow Register Fast of the Jade Bureau’s Transformation of the Multitude on the Upper Prime Festival**

We have heard that the Dao emerges beyond the formless void, its office lying in generation and completion; its virtue surpasses benevolence and righteousness, its merit encompassing compassion and nurturance. Its transformation endures through countless kalpas, its teachings spread across all directions. Thus did the Three Sovereigns govern heaven and earth through the Dao, and the Five Emperors inherit the cosmos through virtue. People attained fortune and longevity, customs achieved harmony and prosperity.

Though the cycles of metal and wood shift and the march of time renews, in ordering the household and prospering the state, the Dao alone takes precedence. When followed, the Four Seas become tranquil and clear, and the age returns to pristine simplicity; when violated, the Central Plains fall into chaos, and all things grow shallow and degenerate.

Our dynasty revives the winds of highest antiquity, continuing the teachings of the Mysterious Origin. Embracing the Dao and holding to virtue, it follows the legacy of Shun and recounts the ways of Yao. Thus has it wielded divine martial prowess to sweep away the dust of turmoil and restore the phoenix’s reign; illuminated sagely culture to secure the altars of the state and firmly establish its grand design.

We, your servants, have long been nurtured by the Dao’s compassion and have encountered this radiant destiny. Though our meager merits remain unmanifest, the grace bestowed upon us runs deep. We aspire to the sincerity of fasting and purity, looking upward to repay the virtue of ruler and kin.

Now, as the Celestial Officials govern the seasons and the Wood Emperor presides over the direction, we approach the season of the Upper Prime’s reckoning and correction, the time for the lower lands to refine their devotion. Together we present ritual offerings and approach the sacred altar. We prepare the jade baskets and golden beans, array the rites of the Ten Poles and Four Flowers. Lotus lamps scatter their flames, continuing the sunlight to illumine the dark passes; orchid incense wafts its smoke, guiding the stellar paths to convey our humble pleas.

We earnestly hope that the host of Perfected Ones will turn their chariots, that the ten thousand sages will wheel their carriages, deigning to look down upon the hearts of the multitude and pour forth vast blessings. Above, may they uphold the imperial throne, securing the dynasty’s rule for as long as heaven endures; below, may they support the ancestral counsels, stabilizing the earth’s foundations for eternity. May border beacons remain unlit, the seasons harmonious, grains abundant, and all living beings at ease. May the realm enjoy concord, its carriages and roads united. May noxious influences not arise, and auspicious signs accumulate.

May we, your servants, in life and death receive boundless fortune; may our seven generations of ancestors ascend to heaven. May our clans share in glory, the three disasters cease. Some among us may bear sins from past lives or this existence, their karmic nets not yet cleared; others may carry old debts or lingering grievances, their transgressions unresolved. Some may have erred in legal judgments or governed unjustly; others may have caused harm through intent or accident, forming karmic retribution. Some may have acted with minds that offend the divine, or indulged in extravagance in earth and timber, in attire and adornments. The Three Officials record their faults, the Five Emperors oversee their wrongs. Through this repentance and prayer, we hope all may be washed clean.

Grant us, your servants, extended years and distant blessings, the removal of calamities, the reconciliation of enmities. Those who have served the throne with single-minded devotion, who have labored for the king with all their strength—though frost and dew first startled them, and the swift passage of time now separates them—we recall them in the nocturnal courts, wishing them to enjoy felicitous karma. May the causes of deliverance be extended, and the paths of transcendence all be attained. For those whose ancestral rites have long been abandoned, who drift in the dark without refuge, may they too be reborn and not remain mired in suffering.

May the dragon spirits and the five ancestral shrines, by the special grace of the Yellow Register and the radiant blessings of the Mysterious Capital, purify the winds and scenery, securing and pacifying all regions. May plagues not invade, weapons not be raised. May strange creatures and unusual forms, all beings of the six destinies and four births, the three paths and five sufferings, by the command of the Nine Dragons and the majestic light of the Three Treasures, universally bathe in divine power and together ascend the true Dao.

---

**Eulogy for the White Jade Sphere’s Luminous Fast in Praise of the Most High Lord Lao**

We have heard that the Dao originates in perfect nonbeing, its transformation unfolding into wondrous existence. Its merit encompasses all under heaven, its grace extends to both the manifest and the hidden. Households and states rely upon it for peace; the living and the dead depend on it for deliverance. Its divine majesty and numinous blessings are of boundless efficacy.

We, your servants, at the Jade Bureau’s Grotto-Heaven, the transcendent abode of immortals, now offer reverence and present our imperial observances. Thus have we, for the secluded chambers of our mysterious ancestors, sculpted the true image. Its gaze is dignified and solemn, its attendants arrayed in order. It seems as though the Pearl Palace has just descended, or the Jade Throne floats in midair. With this great work completed, the wondrous countenance grows ever more majestic. The sun’s corner and moon’s mystery shine forth, illuminating the lord of all beings; the green brows and hoary hair tower as the august one among the ten thousand sages. May it eternally bless this land, securing its numinous transformation.

Therefore, we devoutly prepare this eulogy and prayer, fully expressing our sincerity. We open the jade archives, observe the rites of the Illuminated True, recite scriptures, circumambulate the Dao, light lamps, and burn incense. We pour forth our pleas to the Most High, our minds fixed upon the lower realms.

We humbly hope that the radiance of the Three Realms will incline, that the chariots of the Nine Heavens will turn. May they look down in compassion upon this dust-like existence and descend a cascade of auspicious blessings. May they secretly uphold the precious mandate and covertly protect the sagely dynasty. May they align with the winds of natural purity and attain the principle of the Great Antiquity’s nonaction.

Next, may the earth’s foundations be solemn and tranquil, the river lands peaceful and secure. May auspicious omens be heard, and calamities not arise. May the nine generations of our ancestors and the seven generations of our forebears emerge from the courts of endless night and ascend to the halls of the Radiant Yang. May those whose names were stricken from the earthly registers soar upon the celestial thoroughfares. May all sentient beings of the three paths and six destinies universally partake in this luminous fortune and each attain their destined fulfillment.

We, your servants, having dissolved our accumulated sins and erased our long-standing flaws, find disasters dispelled like mist and the winds of the Dao’s transformation blowing freely. May we obtain the mysterious pearl of the formless and enter the secret registers of the serene and invisible. We vow to refine our devotion in repayment of the profound grace.

---

**Prayer for the Communal Fast at Zhaoxian Abbey in Wenjiang County**

We have heard that the wondrous Dao fuses with the true, towering beyond the primordial chaos; the Heavenly Worthy established the teachings, their light spreading before the vast kalpas. Through the ages, enlightened beings have appeared, aiding beings according to their capacities. For the greatness of states and the salvation of both the manifest and the hidden, all rely upon divine power and universally receive radiant blessings.

We, your servants, have been favored by this sagely destiny and have long been imbued with the true teachings. We revere the Mysterious Origin as the fountainhead of virtue and the Dao, and have witnessed the immortal traces of our illustrious ancestors. Yet we remain entangled in the world’s nets, not yet freed from its cages. We apportion land and employ heaven, reverently upholding the teachings of the mysterious and the classical; we moderate wealth and restrain ourselves, never forgetting the private grace of heaven and earth.

Now, as the Most Sagely One governs with effortless rule, the founding merit pacifies the people, the five weapons are stilled, and the hundred grains offer their bounty.

The countryside resounds with songs of joy, and the people enjoy wealth and longevity. In this month when the Nine Wells bestow life, and this season when the Three Terraces manifest auspicious signs, we seek first to repay the boundless grace through the Yellow Register rites. Thus, we humbly gather the strength of all, together preparing the offerings of faith, meticulously adorning the immortal traces, and reverently following the secret protocols. We lay bare our hearts to the ten directions, surrendering our lives to the myriad heavens. With lamps kindled and incense burning, we convey our sincerity and earnestness.

We humbly pray that the Three Honored Ones may pause their radiant presence to gaze upon our crimson hearts, and that the ten thousand sages may turn their chariots to bestow their mysterious blessings. Above, may they uphold the altars of state, harmonizing with heaven and earth to ensure peace and prosperity; below, may they assist the sagely person, shining with the brilliance of sun and moon. May the auspicious stars of the Three Terraces forever illuminate the earth’s foundations. May the strategies of the ancestral temple and the plans of the court forever govern the wells and towns. May one region flourish in peace, the four borders remain secure, pestilence be kept at bay, and weapons of war stay sheathed.

May we, your servants, along with our nine generations of ancestors and seven generations of kin, transcend the gates of the underworld; may our five clans and six relations be truly blessed with prosperity. May sins and transgressions be dissolved, and calamities and misfortunes be pacified. May agriculture and sericulture be preserved in abundance, and the suffering and afflicted all find relief. May dragon deities guard and stabilize, and wind and rain be harmoniously regulated. May the transformative power of the Dao spread far and wide, and its numinous might extend universally.

Across the vast nine lands and the teeming four kinds of beings, by the merit of the Yellow Altar’s universal repentance and the command of the Most High’s Nine Dragons, may all ascend to the fruits of the Dao and universally mount the immortal ranks. May the wandering souls of flower-strewn sacrifices and the spirits touched by frost and dew no longer suffer from disease and pestilence, each attaining rebirth. Wherever the power of the Dao reaches, may eternal fortune prevail.

---

The Liu Yin, Fei Shun, and Huanglu Memorial for the Yellow Register Rites:

We regard the pure and tranquil origin as the foundation of the profound mystery, establishing teachings; the root of creation relies upon the wondrous pivot to manifest its works. Households and states receive it and flourish, while past and present revolve by it without exhaustion. Of all transformations, the Dao’s influence first emerged before the emperors. Now, as the sagely and wise govern the heavens, the primary terraces divide their domains, spreading and magnifying virtue and the Dao, nurturing and fostering the multitudes. Their benevolence rivals that of Yao, Shun, and Yu, and their virtue surpasses that of Hou Ji and Gao Yao. The myriad regions enjoy peace, and the four borders know no peril. Moved by this extraordinary grace, how can we ascend to repay it?

Thus, we lead and encourage our subordinates to examine and adhere to the scriptural canons, meticulously adorning the altar grounds and fully observing the rites of purification. With refined incense and lamps, we convey our earnestness, and with offerings of faith, we express our sincerity. We focus our thoughts on the Nine Pures and direct our hearts toward the Three Realms.

We humbly pray that the mysterious light may descend to illuminate, and that the Most Sages may spiritually commune, graciously perceiving the sentiments of all and abundantly bestowing their vast blessings. Above, may they uphold the imperial enterprise, gloriously assisting the sagely court, shining as brightly as the three luminaries and standing as firmly as heaven and earth. In the lands of Kun Pond and Phoenix Cave, may the sound of teachings spread afar; in the regions of Mulberry Ford and Meng Valley, may the scripts and decrees be unified.

May the frontier regions be safeguarded, and the generals be aided and protected. May the heavenly blessings forever increase, and the span of life grow ever broader. May our nine generations of ancestors in the dark realms transcend suffering and pass through the gates of obscurity; may our five clans and all relations enjoy the good karma of the Dao’s domain. Within the borders, may the three agricultural seasons yield abundant harvests stored in granaries; amid the governance, may auspicious omens daily be recorded in the annals.

May weapons of war fall silent, and pestilence be kept at bay. For those with lingering bones and wandering souls, long grieving in wind and dew, or suffering in ruined tombs and dilapidated temples, may they, by this meritorious cause, all attain wondrous joy. May dragon deities remain peacefully in their abodes, and the people and officials flourish anew. May all living beings, great and small, together ascend to the realm of blessings.

---

Memorial for the Yellow Register Rites on the Occasion of the Imperial Heir’s Birth:

We have heard that the Dao is supreme, employing its mysterious power to give birth to and nurture heaven and earth; the emperor is most honored, wielding the great pivot to govern and shape creation. He broadly oversees the myriad states and distantly rules the multitudes, receiving the radiant mandate from the Three Pures and establishing the grand foundation across the nine lands. Thus, jade charts accumulate auspicious signs, and the Silver River shines with splendor, giving birth to the illustrious heir and expanding the great enterprise.

Now, as auspicious rainbows shimmer with color and precious lightning flashes with light, during this season when the sun’s brilliance awakens and the entire land reverently observes this sacred time, we dare to open the cloud-bound scriptures and humbly approach the immortal altars. We prepare the sacred precincts of the Numinous Treasure and solemnly convene the grand assembly of longevity. Whale-bone chimes and phoenix bells resound through the nine heavens; crane flames and dragon smoke convey our sincerity to the Three Realms.

We humbly pray that the imperial domain may flourish eternally, equaling the boundless rain and dew; that the sagely lifespan may rise high, matching the vastness of the eight seas. May the six palaces and inner offices harmoniously assist the imperial residence, and the myriad beings and regions widely proclaim the wise virtue. May the imperial heir possess the dragon’s pattern and phoenix’s form, as steadfast as mountains and as pure as pines, surpassing the Han and exceeding the Zhou, wisely supporting the unified realm and universally harmonizing transformation, extending even to the humble and black-haired people.

May all together revere the era of the Dao and unite in the governance of non-action. Your servant, so-and-so, cannot express the utmost of his reverent prayers and devout surrender.

---

Memorial for the Yellow Register Rites Offered by Wang Chengxiu, Grand Master for Splendid Happiness, on Behalf of His Mother:

We have heard that the supreme sages transmitted their canons, and the heavenly perfected established teachings. Their divine works save all beings, leaving nothing—neither the moving nor the still—unattended; their benevolent power spreads grace, universally reaching both the ascending and the descending. From the most ancient times to this very day, we have received their blessings and kindness, the limits of which are beyond knowing.

Thus, in the northern precincts of Mount Feng, they secretly dispelled the dust of evil and pestilence; in the southern precincts of the Dipper’s extremity, they broadly bestowed the warmth of creation and sustenance. Yet only through reverence and purity can one attain spiritual resonance. Your servant, though base and insignificant, has been honored by the shade of the Dao, encountered the wise favor, and ascended through the ranks of office. Within, I attend the celestial steps, ascending high above the nine heavens; without, I hold the bamboo tally, honored to govern a thousand miles.

At times, I must solemnly lead troops, wielding the authority of punishment and law; at others, I must pacify the frontier regions, employing the majesty of command. Fearing that I may deviate from the mean or incur blame, I am ever vigilant and anxious, my heart truly burdened.

Now, my mother, Lady Dou, born under the celestial signs of *jiazi* in such-and-such a month, has been ensnared by baleful influences and afflicted with illness. Though she has diligently taken remedies, she has yet to recover. I fear this may stem from karmic debts or lingering grievances from past lives, where sins of former existences and this present one have entwined. Perhaps it is the malign aspect of stars or the inauspicious passage of years that has brought misfortune, wearing down her fate and fortune. Day and night, I am consumed by anxiety, at a loss for how to aid her. Moreover, as I am charged with royal duties, journeying far upon the roads, I cannot personally attend her at home, nor prepare her medicines and meals. My heart races across ten thousand valleys; my gaze stretches beyond a thousand mountains. I can only rely on the compassion of the Great Dao, hoping for the efficacy of spiritual resonance.

Thus, I turn in devotion to the sacred observance, bowing my head before the flower-strewn altar. I establish a *Huanglu* Daoist ritual, invoking the Perfected and Supreme Saints of the Mysterious Realms. May the sagely gaze turn toward me, bestowing blessings and good fortune. Grant my mother an exchange of her brief span for a long and prosperous life. Dissolve her calamities, wash away her misfortunes, harmonize the six *qi*, and restore health to her hundred meridians. May her faults be absolved, her grievances settled, and her karmic debts resolved. Let her behold the radiance of sun and moon, and receive anew the blessings of creation and sustenance. May those lost in the three wretched paths and the six realms of existence alike partake of this meritorious cause, together attaining the grace of goodness. May the Nine Mysteries open the way to salvation, and the Five Lineages dwell in peace.

If I may ever serve my parents in life, I shall fulfill my filial duty with sweetness and devotion. Honoring the sagely court, I shall forever offer my loyal and sincere heart. With this solemn vow, I humbly submit to the mysterious protection. Unable to contain my earnest supplication and reverent plea, I respectfully submit this petition.

---

**Petition for the Huanglu Ritual by Attendant Censor Hu**

I have heard that the wondrous origin is subtle and imperceptible, the utmost truth empty and tranquil. Through the workings of divine power, it nurtures and transforms; through the molding of all things, it brings forth creation. Its responses are impartial, its circulation tireless. Thus, across the Nine Mysteries and the Three Antiquities, all proclaim its encompassing compassion; between heaven and earth, all bathe in its nurturing grace. The golden precepts and jade statutes, the cloud-script and jade chapters, precede the myriad dharmas in bestowing their teachings, and through the nine schools, they save the world. Great indeed is this supreme teaching—beyond all praise.

I have long been favored by the grace of the Dao, and now rejoice in this glorious era. I wander in the mysterious workings of creation, bathing in the imperial wind. At ease, I follow the harmony of heaven; in all things, I partake of the great transformation. Early on, I entered the secret registers, ever striving to cultivate clarity and sincerity. Like fire-drill and incense, I have maintained reverence from dawn to dusk; like jade rituals and treasured texts, I dare not falter in respect and devotion. My kin and close relations have ever enjoyed its sheltering protection.

Thus, I now perform the *Huanglu* ritual with utmost sincerity, offering it to the mysterious favor. Following the rites of the Ten Flowers and Three Realms, I prepare the feathered fans, chime-stones, frost-bells, and ritual platforms. My heart turns to the myriad saints; my head bows to the hosts of heaven. I humbly beseech that you look upon my sincere devotion and, in your boundless grace, bestow blessings and good fortune.

Grant that my nine ancestors and seven generations ascend to heaven and attain the Dao; that my six relations and five lineages receive fortune and glory. May the living and the dead alike know the benevolence of salvation; may all, in motion and stillness, receive the gift of peace and constancy. May disasters and misfortunes cease, grievances be settled, and faults be absolved; may lifespans be extended, and all beings under heaven—all that lives upon the earth—share in the bond of virtue. May they forever delight in the harmonious transformation of the Dao. Unable to contain my reverent plea, I respectfully submit this petition.

---

**Petition for the Ritual for the Deceased Daughter by Li Xuanjing**

I, from my humble origins, early embraced the true teaching. I have been deeply favored by the mysterious grace, long blessed by the divine favor. Yet, entangled in worldly affairs and bound by the web of the age, I have long been constrained by official duties, unable to fulfill my original aspirations. Though I yearn for the feathered robe and long to take flight, my desire remains unfulfilled. In my devotion to cultivation and reverence, I dare not neglect my private sincerity. Yet, misfortune has befallen me: my daughter has passed away. Time slips away, and my grief is unbearable.

My daughter, in her fifteenth year, was wed to the Yi family. After her husband’s death, she vowed to dedicate herself to the Dao. She had already made her ritual robes and copied scriptures and registers, intending to wear the cap and sash and devote herself to cultivation. But when I was called away on royal business, her wish could not be fulfilled. Soon after, she fell ill and suddenly passed away. Holding my hidden sorrow, I have no way to express it; thinking of the gates of the underworld, my resentment only grows.

I humbly beseech the Three Honored Ones to show compassion, and the host of saints to take pity. May you, in your boundless mercy, bestow the grace of deliverance. Let her soul find refuge and return to the fold. May the karmic debts of her past lives be dissolved, and the faults of this existence be absolved. Rescue her from the suffering of the dark springs, and let her dwell in the bliss of the good realms. May the mysterious power of the Dao ever protect and guide her.

The scriptures, registers, and ritual robes she had prepared, I now reverently burn before the ritual altar, offering them in supplication. I humbly beseech the Perfected Saints to look upon my foolish heart and command her soul to receive and ascend. Unable to contain my earnest plea, my grief, and my sorrow, I respectfully submit this petition.

**Petition for the Birthday Offering of the Eastern Court by Heavenly Commissioner He Wenji**

I have heard that when Heaven and Earth divided their numinous essence and sovereign and subject established their positions, they necessarily relied upon assistance and support to bring about the flourishing of all things. As the wind awaits the tiger and the cloud responds to the dragon, so too do omens appear in dreams and auspices manifest in cauldrons. The wise are born in accordance with their images, as Gao Yao and Kui emerged in the time of the Tai clan; the virtuous rise in succession, as the Eight Elements of Yao’s reign and the noble winds of the Yu court. None failed to illuminate the imperial enterprise and shine forth in the annals of history, bringing peace to the multitudes and blessing the realm entire.

Now, as the year bears the cyclical sign *renchen*, the day holds *gengwu*, the new moon aligns with the celestial markers, and the month accords with the Water Balance. Auspicious omens gather at the Southern Dipper, and propitious radiance converges upon the Eastern Mound. The balmy breeze enters the pitch-pipes, the stellar fire heralds good fortune, the birth-star descends upon Mount Song, and the season is truly fitting. Though I, unworthy, hold a place among the blue-robed officials, I dare to beseech the grace of the Mystic Saints. With reverence, I approach the resplendent altar, praying for the bestowal of boundless fortune. Orchid lamps burn through the night, sandalwood incense rises at dawn. Looking upward, I present the threefold petition, that it may surely reach the scrutiny of the Nine Heavens.

I humbly hope that with azure tablets and vermilion brushes, my name may be inscribed in the Eastern Pole’s register of longevity; that with crimson slips and vermilion records, I may be enrolled in the Southern Palace’s ledger of attainment. May my years rival the mountains in height, my emoluments match the seas in depth. May my joyous realm grow ever clearer, and the virtue of the mulberry-clad one be manifest. May the wild geese in formation inherit the splendor of the Three Terraces, and the carp in the courtyard surpass the seven generations of heroes. May I refine and govern the Nine Regions, aiding the Primordial Sage, unifying governance, and harmonizing customs in great unity. May the blessings extend universally to all lands, and the culture of concord be eternally secured.

I, so-and-so, having received extraordinary favor, reflect upon my own emptiness and frailty. Only by knocking my head before the numinous and true do I express my profound gratitude. Unable to contain my earnest and reverent devotion, I respectfully submit this petition.

---

**Petition for the *Mingzhen* Offering for the Deceased Son Zhaoyin by Military Commissioner of Xuan Sheng Army, Wang Dang**

I have heard that the great transformation knows no bounds, and the divine power is universally bestowed. It penetrates the realms of darkness and light, responding to all appeals, and extends its grace to both the living and the dead. None are left unrelieved, and from ancient times to the present, all have received its blessings.

Recently, I led an expedition to the northern lands, commanding troops in battle. With black bows drawn against the foe, I swore to fulfill my loyal duty; wielding carved halberds, I pledged my life to cleanse the nation’s store. Yet the mountains and rivers were vast, the supply lines strained by transport. As I strove to bring matters to order, my anxiety and vigilance were acute. Moreover, the soldiers suffered from pestilence, their dead and wounded strewn along the roads. My youngest son, Zhaoyin, was also afflicted by illness, his life hanging by a thread. With sincere devotion, I made vows and supplications, hoping for the scrutiny of the Mystic Saints. Soon after, we turned our weapons homeward, sparing the court from neglect. Upon returning to the vermilion steps, I reverently received the emperor’s grace and humbly acknowledge the favor of the Dao. Thus, I now offer thanks and repay this debt.

Following the standards of the *Dongxuan* and the rituals of the *Lingbao*, I have examined the rites for the long night of the Nine Dark Springs and adhered to the *Yugui*’s *Mingzhen* protocols. With utmost sincerity, I have conducted this fast and offering to repay the divine mercy.

I humbly beseech the Three Realms to shine their light and the hosts of heaven to show compassion. May the nine generations of ancestors and the seven lineages be delivered from the suffering of the dark gates, and may my kin and relations enjoy felicity in this illustrious age.

I bear the karmic faults of past lives and the enmities of former existences. Since assuming my duties, I have incurred both public and private transgressions—whether in rewards or punishments misapplied, or judgments ill-considered. The resentment of the people and my own errors are recorded in the unseen ledgers. Thus, obstacles have constantly beset me, and I have known no smooth passage. Day and night, my heart is heavy with sorrow and trepidation. Through this offering and repentance, I beg for the absolution of all these faults.

My son Zhaoyin died before reaching his prime. His wandering soul now dwells in a foreign realm; his untimely passing fills me with profound grief. Whether by malevolent influences or the restraint of dark spirits, I earnestly implore the power of the Dao to guide his spirit to life. May he cross the Southern Palace’s flowing fire and ascend to the radiant precincts of the Upper Realms. May he partake in the mysteries, attain enlightenment, and ascend to perfection. May his sins be absolved and his karmic debts resolved.

May my own calamities be lifted, my misfortunes dispelled, and my rank, emoluments, and longevity further extended. With unwavering devotion, I shall forever repay the emperor’s grace; through diligent cultivation, I shall uphold the protection of the Perfected Ones.

---

**Petition for the *Mingzhen* Offering for the Deceased Father by Wang Chengyan**

I have heard that the Supreme Dao unfolded its plan, and the Three Honored Ones bestowed their teachings. Their kindness extended to both the hidden and the manifest, their grace permeated life and death. They traversed the Eight Gates, spreading compassion to relieve suffering; moved by the sorrows of the dark night, they turned the torch of the Dharma to cast its light. The Southern Palace opens its courtyard of refinement, and the cinnabar registers initiate the ledgers of transcendence. The wise youths of the upper realms desire to know the causes of sin and blessing; the flying deities and divine beings request the forms of repentance and supplication. Expounding the profound and wondrous canon of *Mingzhen*, they deliver souls from the dark gates; unfolding the numinous rites of the *Yugui*, they dissolve the trials of the deceased. The obscurities of the mysterious and pure are dispelled, and parched sorrows are quenched. All lost souls are rescued and become beings of bliss. Through endless kalpas, all bathe in the mysterious mercy.

My late father encountered the winds of the Dao in his time and frequently partook in the sacred registers. Born in an age of sagely rule, he repeatedly attained official honors. Yet within the web of the world, could he have been without error? Amid the dust of the mortal realm, he must have incurred transgressions. Moreover, as steward of the kitchens, he was required to slaughter; as commander of troops, he often meted out punishments. Leading an army in the field or serving in the inner court, he may have oppressed the strong or protected the weak. Though he issued three commands and five exhortations, any misjudgment of severity or leniency would have constituted an offense. Separated from his homeland by war and chaos, his ancestral tombs may have been desecrated, and disputes over graves may have extended to his descendants. In selling his property and relocating his residence, the construction of earth and timber may have offended the bright spirits. For all these causes of anxiety, I now seek repentance and absolution.

Thus, I have followed the standards of the *Lingbao* and established a *Mingzhen* ritual altar. With pure incense and lamps, abundant offerings and sincere vows, I lay bare my heart and beg for grace. I humbly implore the Three Honored Ones of the Supreme and the hosts of saints in the ten directions to cast their divine light downward and pour forth their benevolent favor. May my late father’s accumulated sins and deep calamities across lifetimes be pardoned, his name erased from the earthly ledgers, and his essence cleansed in the celestial thoroughfares.

For past transgressions of accidental harm, for the debts of former grievances, for the faults that have extended to descendants, and for the blemishes of ancestral resentments—may all these be absolved, leaving inner and outer purity.

Thus, I beseech that the elixir of divine refinement be bestowed, that his name be inscribed in the Registers of Azure Radiance. May he bypass the trials of Mount Tai and Fengdu, and swiftly attain the celestial path of blessed halls. Above, may the Nine Lineages be delivered, the Seven Ancestors ascend; may graves rest in peace, the netherworld lie still. May the Three Paths and Six Realms together partake in this sublime merit, and may both kin and allies alike receive luminous protection.

With heart carved open and tears wiped in blood, I bow my head and pray to Heaven. Overcome with sobbing and choking grief, I humbly submit these words.

---

**Prayer for Clear Skies by the Crown Prince at a Banquet for Generals**

It is said that the supreme Dao responds to circumstances as echo answers sound, and that the enlightened spirits attend to devotion as shadow follows form. Reflecting on the unseen blessings I have received, I am ever grateful for the grace bestowed.

On the twenty-second day of the sixth month, the Crown Prince hosted a gathering for his generals, having already selected an auspicious hour. As this was the season of summer rains, prayers for clear skies were offered. Indeed, the divine favor was granted, and this earnest plea was answered. In but a moment, the torrential downpour ceased. The mountains gleamed in dawn’s verdant light, the sky cleared as if a screen had drawn back the clouds; the six directions were swept by pure winds, and the sun, hastening onward, saw the Radiant One take up the reins. The banquet was fully prepared, and all within and without rejoiced together.

Now, as we prepare to mobilize our forces and commence punitive action, a thousand troops surge like thunder, and the mountains and rivers are freed from the threat of mud and flood. Ten thousand horses race like stars, their armor and weapons gleaming with crystalline brilliance. Awaiting the pacification of the rebellious and the great deliverance of the people, I seek to repay the Perfected Officials and thus present this offering of a fast. Lotus lamps cluster in the night, orchid tassels flutter at dawn. The rites are performed with utmost reverence, incense and flowers abundant in their splendor.

May this reach the sages of the Pure Capital, and may the merits of the Purple Palace be further exalted. I knock my head in reverence to the mysterious power, that the great enterprise may flourish. Overcome with devotion, I humbly submit these words.

---

**The Emperor’s Prayer for the Yellow Register Fast in Honor of Lord Lao**

It is said that before the chaos of primordial vastness, beyond the formless and silent, there dwells the Supreme Sage, whose radiance fills the Nine Heavens. He expounds the school of tranquil emptiness and practices the teaching of non-action. From the Three Antiquities onward, across the ten thousand regions, the reverence for the true wind has assisted and fulfilled the transformations of the age.

Since the inception of governance and the assumption of the throne, I have constantly striven to manifest sincerity, ever offering reverence and devotion. The divine favor has been repeatedly bestowed, and auspicious blessings have followed one another. The immortal abode granted the talisman of the Mandate, greatly securing the foundation of the realm; the Hall of Audience gave rise to prayers of supplication, and the response was invariably felt.

Thus, wind and rain have been harmonious, malevolent influences have not arisen, the four borders have known no alarms, and the hundred grains have flourished. Grateful for these graces, I earnestly seek to express my thanks.

Therefore, at this season, I specially establish the fast altar, observing three days of reverent solemnity and six periods of purification. I hope that through this offering, I may repay the mysterious power above.

Now, as I dispatch masters and disciples to quell the rebellious, I still rely on the power of the Dao to eradicate the nests of evil. Borrowing the might of Fenglong and Lieque, may the clans of the greedy and rapacious be swept away. May further blessings be bestowed, and the realm forever enjoy peace. Overcome with devotion and longing, I humbly submit these words.

---

**Prayer by the Imperial Son-in-Law of Shuzhou for the Yellow Register Ritual of Disaster Dispelling and Salvation**

Your servant has heard that the supreme Dao is profound and subtle, its mysterious power vast and great. It encompasses the myriad heavens to spread transformation and extends its grace to all beings.

Thus it can descend to deliver those beyond the gates of darkness, broadly pacify the state and nation, stabilize and secure the land, and harmonize and enlighten the spirits. All rejoice in the governance of the Ruler, exhausting the power of compassionate mercy. From ancient times to the present, none—whether hidden or manifest—are left unblessed.

Your servant has long revered the mysterious grace and early received the imperial favor. Yet before I could render even the slightest service, I was suddenly honored with the dignity of office, burdened with the weight of manifold duties, and charged with overseeing criminal law, adjudicating disputes. I feared straying from the principles of benevolence and forgiveness; leading troops, I truly lacked the essentials of discipline and order, and my actions often incurred faults and blame. Constantly gripped by trepidation and anxiety, since assuming governance of this commandery, I have ever remained vigilant and cautious. Yet calamity and punishment have swiftly befallen me—how dare I hope for survival? Bound by ritual constraints, there is no escape from destruction. Though I cling to this fleeting breath, further profound grace has descended. With bloodied tears, I cry out to Heaven—lonely and helpless, to whom can I appeal?

I have heard that the Mysterious Origin established the teachings, and the Purple Yang possesses the rites of deliverance; the Orthodox Unity transmitted its precepts, and the Yellow Register offers the path of repentance and prayer. Therefore, I dare to solemnly purify the public office, erect the altar for the fast, prostrate myself before the Nine Heavens with this memorial, and send forth my words to the Three Realms. I humbly implore the Three Honored Ones and the host of sages to extend their compassionate mercy; may the nightly courts and the gates of the Yellow Springs open the way to ascension. May the soul of the Lady of Yun State, such-and-such, attain peace and prosperity, her blessings and goodness perfumed by virtue. May all her accumulated transgressions and deep stains be washed away. Unbound by the earthly prisons, may she ascend directly to the Heavenly Hall.

May the seven generations of ancestors and the nine lineages of descendants, all those departed and passed away, together ascend by the power of the Dao and assemble in the courtyard of blessings. Within the halls of this dwelling, repeatedly renovated and altered, I fear that disturbances may have arisen, preventing tranquility. I pray that through the merit of this fast and offering, the transgressions of offense and violation may be resolved. May the dragon spirits return to their positions, the earth gods be at peace, the residence be favorable and fitting, and all misfortunes and disasters be extinguished. May the city gods of the walls and moats, the local deities of the wards and domains, and the true officials of the land secretly receive divine favor and forever dwell in the land of blessings.

Above, I wish for the imperial enterprise to be firmly prosperous and the sagely lifespan to extend in abundance. May the Crown Prince and the various princes uphold great fortune in service to the state; may the empress, consorts, and imperial concubines receive radiant blessings to assist the court. May the officials within and beyond the court, the six armies, and the myriad people together rejoice in flourishing fortune and attain perfect peace and stability. May the years bring abundant harvests, and the customs be free from plague and pestilence. Within the realm, may the ten thousand regions be unified. May all together reach the land of benevolence and longevity, and together uphold the transformation of supreme peace.

With utmost reverence, I prostrate myself, lay bare my heart, and offer my sincerest and most earnest prayers.

Respectfully submitted by Zhang Taibo, Prefect of Qiongzhou, on behalf of the restoration of the withered cypress at Heming, for the performance of the Golden Register Fast.

I have heard that the supreme Dao is profoundly penetrating, and divine power broadly operates. It shapes and completes Heaven and Earth, and assists and praises the emperors and kings.

The sovereigns of Fuxi, Shennong, and Suiren, the lords of Yao, Shun, Yu, and Tang—none failed to take the profound and formless as their teacher, drawing forth harmony and radiance. Thus did they secure the enduring majesty of their dynasties and amplify the resplendence of their renown. Some rode the winds across the azure seas; others attained ranks in the Purple Courts. Their light illumined the nine distant realms, their longevity matched the Three Luminaries.

We humbly reflect upon the Great Emperor of Shu, who governs the pivot of the cosmos and grasps the Dipper to stabilize the primordial. Wielding the Great Image, he pacifies Hua and Yi; mounting the Six Dragons, he soothes the hundred millions. His virtue surpasses that of Yao and Yu; his sagacity exceeds that of Fuxi and Shennong. The lords of the felt tents and distant lands present tribute and turn toward civilization; the barbarians beyond the Han’s farthest reaches, though their tongues differ, come as guests. His beneficence saturates mountains and rivers; his benevolence extends to grasses and trees. Sacred birds nest in the inner gardens; auspicious beasts dwell in Shanglin. The triple blossoms manifest omens; the ten cowries signal wonders. Yet still he labors in humility, yielding virtue to the celestial mandate; though his deeds overflow the bamboo annals, his modesty deepens.

Now, with the hidden aid of immortals and the gracious descent of numinous transformation, profound blessings moisten the withered roots, and branches and trunks revive upon the dead cypress. When the wind stirs the verdant cliffs, its fragrance drifts far and near; when the moon passes the sacred altar, the luxuriant shadows reappear. This auspicious sign surpasses all in antiquity. It reveals the flourishing of the imperial lineage and the eternal endurance of the sacred reign. Though the sprouting grain in the ancestral temple and the *ming* leaves in the vermilion court were wondrous of old, they pale beside this divine response.

I, honored to encounter this flourishing fortune and entrusted with the seal of this prefecture, have witnessed this supreme omen. With brush and ink, I present it at the Dragon Gate; with silk and thread, it is proclaimed upon the Phoenix Edict. The imperial response bestowed, the rites of offering and prayer are solemnly renewed. Praise resounds in splendor; honor and favor abound. Though I measure the imperial grace, the vast sea is not deep enough; bearing the sacred favor, heaven and earth cannot repay.

Daring to seize the emperor’s natal day, I establish the Golden Register Daoist sanctuary, raising my crimson heart in reverence, to beseech the mysterious blessings. May the hosts of heaven descend their gaze; may the ten thousand sages manifest their presence. Pour vast fortune upon the altars of state and the august spirits; augment radiant protection for the ancestral temples and former sages. May the Two Modes stand firm; may the myriad states share a common script. May the emperor’s longevity equal Mounts Min and Emei; may his brilliance match the sun and moon. May he universally proclaim the correct calendar and unify the earth beneath the seas.

May the empress receive blessings in the Purple Chamber and extend her years through the cinnabar registers. May the crown prince forever uphold the imperial pole, nurturing virtue in the Azure Palace. May the princesses, consorts, and concubines honor and assist the sacred sun. May the myriad princes and officials revere and support the imperial foundation. May the nine lands enjoy peace; may the five weapons be sheathed. May the dust of war vanish; may the harvests be abundant. May all beings—those that move and grow, fly and sink, the three paths and six destinies—together receive the imperial bounty and all attain the courts of fortune.

I vow to pour forth the principles of loyalty and filial piety, repaying the sagely grace from above.

*Guangcheng ji*, Volume 5 concludes
*Guangcheng ji*, Volume 6 begins

The Most Reverend Du Guangting, Great Virtue of Literary Composition by Imperial Commission and Purple-Robe Honoree of the Supreme Clarity Palace in the Upper Capital, respectfully presents the *Jiao* Petitions for the Northern Emperor’s Yamen Ritual.

We humbly acknowledge that the Five Qi’s Mysterious Heaven and the Great Emperor of the Northern Palace oversee good and evil, govern life and death. All matters of longevity, fortune, fortune, and misfortune are subject to their judgment and record. We fear that celestial asterisms may bring calamities of illumination upon us, and that our fate in this life and our annual destiny may incur the faults of punishment and harm. We beseech the Perfected Saints to specially prepare expiatory rites. With utmost sincerity, we jointly perform the *jiao* ritual, humbly praying for the dissolution of disasters and the extension of years. May our names be stricken from the death registers of the Northern Feng and inscribed in the life rolls of the Southern Culmen. May public and private affairs flourish in harmony, and our families dwell in peace. Thus do we look up to receive the benevolent protection of the Imperial Lord.

---

**Petition for the Three Assemblies’ Register Ritual**

Your servant has received the Orthodox Perfection and partaken of the Mysterious Registers, inwardly aspiring to cultivation to preserve body and mind, and outwardly hoping for numinous power to dispel disasters and pestilence. Following the ritual codes, I have early attained the precious talismans. Yet I fear being constrained by worldly affairs and ensnared by mundane mechanisms. On days of fasting and abstinence, my morning audiences may be deficient; at times of cultivation, incense and lamps may be lacking. Good deeds remain unestablished, while faults and transgressions readily manifest. The Perfected Qi and Numinous Officials have not bestowed their protection, and the Mysterious Bureau of Heaven’s Court reproaches my lack of devotion. The three destinies and five phases have not dispelled calamities and declines. Day and night, I am filled with dread, as if holding ice and fire in my breast.

Now, on the day of the Upper Assembly and the time when the Heavenly Officials review merits and demerits—when all deeds, good and evil, great and small, are laid bare—we dare to pour forth our sincerity, repent our faults with utmost devotion, and diligently perform the *jiao* ritual, presenting this petition. We implore the host of saints to show mercy, pardon our transgressions, and send down numinous responses to dissolve disasters and misfortunes. May the officers and soldiers of the Three Bureaus ever grant their protection. May we enjoy health and peace in all our movements and repose, forever partaking of

**Petition for the Northern Dipper *Jiao* Ritual by Attendant Wang Qian**

Your servant, though base and insignificant, has been blessed to encounter the transformation of the Dao. Constantly receiving your sheltering protection, I am truly indebted to your true compassion. Since the first year of the *Longji* era, when I was dispatched on a mission to the branch commanderies, I carried the imperial decree forth—only to suddenly tread upon the mechanism of disaster. In that perilous dread, the true numina looked down in aid. My body and life were preserved, all anxieties and doubts dispelled. Yet, separated by two lands, we have been cut off for three years. My son, Yan Gui, earnestly offered prayers and supplications, repeatedly beseeching the divine luminaries. Heaven’s scrutiny of his sincerity ran deep, and he personally witnessed the response in omens. Gazing up to the Most Sagely, I am shielded by this extraordinary grace. I yearn to exhaust my cinnabar heart in repayment and thanksgiving.

Now, at the great festival of the Upper Prime and the auspicious time for invoking blessings, I have prepared the *jiao* altar to requite your radiant favor. I humbly implore you to overlook the meagerness of this offering and accept my humble sincerity. Fulfill the vow of old in this very year, and bestow your grace upon this day. I shall forever uphold my devotion to bear the divine hemp.

**Petition for the Southern Dipper *Jiao* Ritual by Minister Ma**

I have heard that when the clear and turbid divided their forms, the high and low were fixed in their stations. The Northern and Southern Dippers govern the registers of life and death, while yin and yang partake of expansion and contraction. Thus, the august deities of the Southern Dipper—saints of the Six Palaces—record merits and exalt goodness, inscribing the script of immortality. They preside over the ledgers of fate and determine the years, ever initiating the root of long life. Their wish is that all things return to the Dao, and all people ascend to perfection, complementing the Heavenly Honored One’s boundless compassion and upholding the Great Dao’s principle of cherishing life.

Yet the waves of the dusty world easily drown, and the mind’s horses vie in their gallop. The net of transgressions is a tight cage; none find a path to soar. The passions are firmly barred, never a gate of liberation. Your servant dwells in the mortal realm, his heart shackled by worldly duties. Holding the reins of power, he must enforce the statutes of reward and punishment; overseeing punishments and rewards, he cannot indulge in the harmony of equanimity. I fear my faults and errors have accumulated in the courts of the unseen. Moreover, with calamities and misfortunes converging, this has become a time of tribulation. Though I have repeatedly offered prayers and repentance, knocking at the gates of heaven, I have not yet poured forth my luminous sincerity to lay it before the Southern Culmen.

Now, on this auspicious day of divination and felicity, I have reverently arranged the *jiao* altar. Following the true canons, I lay bare my cinnabar sincerity. The multitudes of the lower realm humbly display their offerings upon the jade steps; the radiant perfected of the upper realm will surely descend to the jeweled mats. I dare to hope for your compassionate pardon, that you might look upon this humble one with mercy. Release my sins and dispel disasters, striking my name from the yin ledgers of the Northern Palace. Bestow added years and augment my blessings, inscribing my name in the yang registers of the Southern Dipper. May the Six Palaces forever record my name, and may the Five Planets secretly nourish my fortune. I pray that my ninefold ancestors and sevenfold lineage receive blessings from the Vermilion Mound, and that my fivefold kin and sixfold affines extend their felicity in the Purple Palace. I vow to diligently uphold my devotion in repayment of your vast compassion.

**Li Guan’s Prayer for the Nine Luminaries Offering**

I have heard that the two qi descend in harmony, thereby shaping all things; the Three Radiances spread their forms to nurture the multitude of beings. Among these, the most numinous is revered, as it receives the bright blessings of Heaven. All matters of conduct and concealment, good and evil, movement and rest, fortune and misfortune—all are governed by the heavens above, which oversee the earth below.

I, your servant, have fortunately inherited past blessings and have been graced by the winds of the Dao. In serving my lord and establishing myself, I have striven to fulfill the duty of loyalty and sincerity. In reflecting upon myself, I have constantly maintained a heart of reverent caution. The emoluments and ranks I have received are bestowed by the divine luminaries. Yet my anxieties have only deepened, for I fear my flaws may bring peril.

For years, I have been afflicted by an eye ailment, enduring persistent suffering. Though acupuncture and medicine have been applied, and I have diligently consumed remedies, I have not yet recovered, and my dread has only grown. I fear that the cycles of yin and yang in this year have brought me grave misfortune, and that the movements of the celestial luminaries have conspired to deepen my distress.

I have previously offered prayers and sacrifices, hoping to attain peace, yet now, as the Dark Void passes through my natal palace, my long-standing illness coincides with this calamitous period. With no recourse before me, I am left bewildered and without support.

I have heard that the true statutes provide a method, and the rituals of offering and libation are recorded in sacred texts. Thus, I humbly exert my utmost sincerity, hoping for the divine gaze. I diligently perform the offering rites, inviting the descent of your august presence.

I beseech the mighty deities of the Nine Luminaries, who divide their light to illuminate and receive. Dissolve my past transgressions, reconcile my grievances, and dispel the entanglements of disaster. Remove the afflictions of my illness. May the Purple Youth guard and protect me, so that my eyes suffer no further pain; may the Azure Emperor shield me, so that my liver enjoys peace and tranquility. May misfortune and decline forever cease, and may my official rank and lifespan be renewed.

I dare not forget my vow of diligent cultivation, that I may repay the gift of your illumination.

---

**Prayer of Minister Ma to the Northern Emperor**

I, your humble servant, though of lowly station, have long heard of the transformative power of the Dao. I have settled my heart in tranquility and directed my thoughts toward the true and upright. Each time I have offered sincere prayers, I have been graciously blessed with manifest protection.

Recently, as the public fields were opened and the wheat in the furrows began to grow, the lingering days of spring brought warmth, yet the dense clouds of oil-like rain had not yet spread. Gazing upon the farmlands, I was filled with deep concern. I knocked upon the gates of the mysterious, and indeed, your vast grace descended. Where the incense from the censer dispersed, the stones glistened with moisture; when the forbidden water was sprinkled, it transformed into a rain as rich as cream. Thus, the autumn harvest became promising, and the spring plowing proceeded without error. The granaries of the capital may soon overflow, bringing abundance to the lands of Shu.

The favor bestowed by the supreme sages is profound, yet how may this lowly servant repay such virtue? I humbly swept the jade altar and arranged a modest offering. Though the bundled water-plants and pondweed are unworthy as offerings, I dare present them alongside silk, candles, incense, and flowers as a small token of gratitude. I pray you deign to accept them and bestow lasting auspicious blessings.

In gratitude for past kindnesses and in prayer for future grace, I dare not elaborate further.

---

**Prayer of Minister Ma to the Southern Dipper**

I have heard that the Great Sage is impartial, responding to sincerity and answering prayers. The perfected ones descend to aid, manifesting their presence in answer to devotion. Their transformations are unhindered by the mundane, and their salvation extends even to the lowliest.

I, your servant, though obscure and unworthy, have secretly admired the mysteries of the Dao. I have purified my heart and relied upon the realm of emptiness, secretly hoping to repent my sins; I have bowed my head in reverence toward the vast and formless, praying to cleanse my past transgressions. First, I sought deliverance for my sevenfold ancestors; next, I prayed for harmony and peace in the four directions.

No sooner had I expressed my humble sincerity than your boundless compassion descended. A divine communion was granted, and I received an auspicious dream. My soul was clear and my qi refreshed, entirely unlike the time when Zhuangzi dreamed of a butterfly; I felt as content as the fisherman who obtained the pearl. This surely portends a year of abundance and the cessation of disasters.

Reflecting upon the divine favor, I now offer this grand blessing. Overwhelmed with gratitude, I am at a loss for words. To repay this spiritual grace, I have once more performed the offering rites. The paired mandarin-duck lamps emitted flames, their light mingling with the radiance of the Jade Dipper; the dragon-shaped incense wafted fragrance, scattering the hues of the Jasper Pool. Casting aside all distractions, I united my heart in devotion.

I beseech the perfected ones of the Cinnabar Palace and the exalted sages of the Six Palaces to turn their crane-drawn chariots and briefly descend beneath the rainbow banners. Accept my humble sincerity and take pity on this degenerate age. Brush clean the golden tablets of longevity and open the vast pardon of great mercy. Grant me extended years and renew my blessings. In governance, may the three agricultural seasons yield abundance; in military affairs, may the seven virtues display their might. May transgressions be erased, public and private affairs flourish, the living and the dead receive blessings, and my kin enjoy prolonged life.

May the Northern Prime expunge the records of my past faults, and may the Nine Treasuries inscribe my name in the registers of extended years. Moreover, as the Five Planets move in their courses, they may at times align with the Three Primes, influencing my fate with hardship or fortune. When the time comes to transform misfortune into blessing, or to reduce my rank and shorten my years, the common lot cannot fathom such matters, and I am left to ponder my fate with worry. Without relying on the compassion of the Dao, there would be no means of self-deliverance.

I have heard that the Most High established the rites of expiation, and the Heavenly Master inscribed the statutes of prayer and offering. Sins are surely erased, and blessings are granted in response to prayer. Today, on the day of my nativity, I humbly present the texts of the Orthodox Unity. Reverently bowing, I arrange this modest offering. To the Three Palaces and Five Planets, I offer my sincere prayers; to the Six Treasuries and Seven Primes, I express my repentance and gratitude.

I pray that the multitude of exalted ones will bestow their protection, and that the Great Sages will deign to descend. Pardon my past transgressions and bestow future blessings. May the Three Disasters be stilled, and the Nine Calamities dispelled. May my lifespan be secretly extended, and my blessings and rank flourish. May my sevenfold ancestors and ninefold lineage transcend the dark prisons; may my fivefold kin and sixfold affines equally receive the shade of the Dao. May public and private affairs forever prosper, and may the living and the dead enjoy peace and well-being.

I now look up in reverence to the boundless grace of the Great Sages.

---

**Tang Dongqing’s Prayer for the Natal Day Offering**

I, your servant, by the fate of my past lives, have encountered the transformative power of the Dao. I have received and upheld the true registers, thereby gaining the opportunity to cultivate myself. Yet my merits and deeds remain unremarkable, and my transgressions and faults easily accumulate. The cycles of yin and yang have gone awry, and I have been afflicted by illness. Overwhelmed with worry, my prayers have been earnest. Indeed, I have received manifest protection and swiftly attained recovery.

On the day of the Middle Prime, I wished to hold a gathering for the Yellow Registers, humbly informing the perfected sages and hoping to fulfill my sincere devotion. Now, the altar rites have been completed, and the merits and virtues have been accomplished. The covenants have been answered, and the winds and rains have not intruded.

The profound kindness of the sagely and numinous is felt in the unseen, yet its repayment remains beyond measure. Daring to take this life’s destiny as occasion, I reverently prepare the ritual observances. Setting forth a modest offering to express my sincerity, I bow in homage to the sacred writ and entreat blessings. Humbly I pray that the Most Exalted may deign to receive this, and that the host of sages may shine their presence upon us. May the vows previously made now come to fruition, and extraordinary auspices descend. Let my transgressions dissolve and misfortunes vanish, my deeds flourish and merits abound. May those I serve in filial devotion be preserved in peace and tranquility, and those I commend from afar surely partake in elevation and deliverance. I shall forever steel my resolve and sincerity to repay the true numina.

No words suffice.

Memorial for the Ritual Offering at the Abbey of the Venerable Master, Mount Qingcheng

I humbly reflect: the immortal mountain of Qingcheng, the sacred abbey of the Venerable Master—its nine chambers open into countless grottoes, and gazing upon the myriad peaks, it stands supreme. Since the Yellow Emperor bestowed its enfeoffment, the Han sovereigns offered their veneration; since Xuanzong erected its halls, former emperors augmented its splendor. The immortal chambers grew ever more majestic, the pure altars ever more solemn. Recently, a worthy magistrate has undertaken its restoration, renewing the numinous palace. Yet to the west of the main sanctuary, vacant land still lies; to the north of the secluded windows, remnants of old foundations remain. The image of the Dark Primordial has yet to be enshrined, while the traces of the imperial scion linger still. I venture, therefore, to propose the construction of an ancestral hall and the establishment of a fasting chamber. May these serve perpetually as the site for offerings and reverence, and enhance the purity and emptiness of this sacred realm. As we prepare to wield shovels and spades, we fear disturbing the dragon spirits. Thus, I dare to arrange this ritual feast and reverently present this solemn announcement. Humbly I pray that this sincere entreaty be granted, and that mysterious blessings descend, ensuring the work’s completion without hindrance above or below. May laborers and artisans dwell in peace and safety, and blessings and goodness be renewed. No words suffice.

**Prayer for the Nine Luminaries Ritual at Zhangren Mountain**

It is heard that when Heaven and Earth divided their numinous powers, the Three Offices fixed the patterns of life and death; when yin and yang suspended their images, the Nine Luminaries bestowed their illuminating radiance. The Southern Palace unfurls the talisman of extended years, while the Northern Bureau displays the register of transgressions. As stars traverse mountains and rivers, their scrutiny admits no partiality. All within the human realm are governed by their dominion.

I, though humble and unworthy, have been graced with profound compassion. Yet in my conduct, I fear I have strayed from hidden blessings; in my thoughts, I have failed to align with the divine. Thus, misfortune has befallen me, compounded by faults and errors. Adversity has swiftly converged, leaving no path for repentance or prayer.

This year, the Central Palace is under the sway of the Celestial Talisman; my station is illuminated by the gaze of Saturn. The great cycle still resides within the baleful stars, and the flying banners are ensnared by the year’s progression. In the three destinies and five phases, I dread encountering harm and conflict; among the constellations and Nine Luminaries, I fear further illumined scrutiny. Hence, my path remains rough, and calamities arise in succession. Without recourse to the Most Sage, there is no way to seek deliverance.

Therefore, I dare to offer my utmost sincerity and conduct this grand ritual. Humbly I pray that the host of sages deign to descend with blessings, dispelling future disasters and absolving past transgressions. May the Six Offices of Destiny augment my fortune in the Crimson Heavens, and may the Seven Sovereign Deities of the Primal Ultimate bestow auspicious favor. May public and private affairs flourish in tranquility, and my kin dwell in peace and health. Thus shall I forever bear the grace of the sages’ protection.

**Prayer for the Life-Prolonging Ritual of the Circumpolar Stars by Vice Envoy Mo Tingyi, Magistrate of Qingcheng**

It is heard that the transformative power of the Dao spreads forth, its mysterious workings embracing all. The unfathomable interplay of yin and yang nurtures all without partiality.

Thus do the Five Emperors and Three Sovereigns govern the Six Rituals and order all things; the Celestial Offices and Watery Palaces oversee the Eight Assemblies and uphold the great net. The Southern Palace records the statutes of good, while the Northern Culmen binds the ranks of transgression. Fortune and misfortune, guilt and blessing—all are tied to the numinous bureaus.

This humble servant reflects that the sacred precincts of All-Sichuan, the metropolis of Huayang, command the frontiers of eight lands and pacify the manifold tribes. Its jade encampments stand lofty, its golden terraces tower high. Abroad, it purifies alien customs, its might and grace drawing equally upon civil and martial arts; within, it wields a mighty host, its decrees enforcing both reward and punishment.

Your servant humbly observes that Minister Zhang has long borne the weight of authority, wielding it with unswerving loyalty. Above, he receives the sagely designs; below, he follows the temple’s grand strategy. At times, he deploys the tiger-like troops to sweep the frontiers clean; at others, he recovers cities and fortresses, leveling the borders. Now he roots out the treacherous and cunning, crushing the violent and overbearing; now he oversees the levying of taxes and the provisioning of the army. Given these manifold affairs, how could punishments be withheld? Yet this servant deeply fears that in the swiftness of execution, errors of weight or lightness may arise, leading to divine censure—all without prior repentance or supplication.

Moreover, the Three Destinies and Five Phases may yet bring decline and adversity; the bright stars may dim, or baleful influences descend. The workings of the spirit-way are profoundly subtle, beyond the reach of mortal understanding. Without recourse to the utmost sagacity, deep stains cannot be cleansed.

Thus does this servant venture to approach the numinous mountain and conduct this grand ritual, traversing the yin and yang bureaus of Heaven and Earth, circling the palaces of stars, sun, and moon. With heart laid bare, he beseeches grace and repents past transgressions. Humbly he prays that the far-shining numinous light may scrutinize and erase all former faults; that beneficent favor may descend, stilling future calamities. May true blessing be vouchsafed, ever fostering fortune and felicity. May the red registers record his extended years, and the black ledgers strike his name from the rolls of guilt. Thus shall the land flourish, and all beings forever dwell in peace. The debt of gratitude is beyond expression.

**Memorial for the Zhou-Tian Offering to the River Lord by Mo Tingyi**

I have heard that the Primal Sage unfolds his radiance, his lofty majesty condescending to transform all. His grace suffuses the ten thousand kinds, his compassion overspreads the myriad heavens. He suspends the luminous statutes of sin and blessing, and sets forth the great law of life and death. Above, he watches over the state; below, he extends to all ministers. All alike enter the gate of his governance, all heed the lessons of his reproof and encouragement. From antiquity to the present, his order remains unconfused, and not the slightest fault escapes his notice.

Your servant reflects that to assist the sagely and establish merit, none but the worthy can accomplish it; to uphold the imperiled and rescue the distressed, none but the virtuous can take the lead. Military Commissioner Wang, his loyalty piercing the divine, his fidelity guarding the altars of state, displayed martial prowess to restore the former court to rightness and drummed forth benevolent transformation to bring peace to the present sage’s reign. For these abundant merits, he was granted this great command.

Yet in the course of his duties, he may have stormed palace gates and extirpated malevolent forces; marched his troops through the Qin heartlands and mustered his legions in Baochuan; swept clean the庸 and Shu lands and pacified the heavens of Tianpeng. Though he quelled the frontier and suppressed the violent, it was not by choice that he could not lay down arms. Thus did he proclaim the Son of Heaven’s might and wield the general’s axe—all in service of righteousness, all for the sake of the times. Still, I fear that in the unavoidable slaying, unintended harm may have arisen, giving rise to unseen offenses. The celestial bureaus and earthly registers may yet record these transgressions. Moreover, I dread that the stars of fate may have cast their baleful influence, that his current year may bear misfortune, that the cycles of fortune may bring decline, or that the astrological divisions may portend calamity. It is thus necessary to prepare this repentance and confession, that all may be illuminated and cleansed.

Your servant, though unworthy of his office, has consulted the sacred texts and charts. With utmost sincerity, I now reverently present this grand offering. I purify the rites and hymns upon the immortal peaks, and offer fine grains upon the numinous altar. Above, I knock upon the void and pray to the highest heavens; below, I bow to the nine earths and entreat with reverence. May my earnest thoughts reach the true powers, and may their blessings flow abundantly.

I pray that the Northern Palace may absolve all sins, and the Southern Culmen extend life. May the obstructions of the Five Phases be dissolved, and the misfortunes of the Three Fates be eradicated. May his years stretch as broad as the rivers, his emoluments rise as high as the mountains. May the grain harvests be bountiful, and the common people rejoice in harmony. May he ever support the sagely sun, and forever bless all beings.

Above, I pray that the state’s destiny be long and enduring, that the sagely court enjoy profound peace, that weapons fall silent, and that the realm be united under one civil order. May the Three Luminaries follow their proper courses in the highest heavens, and may the ten thousand kinds flourish upon the earth below. Whether in the hidden or the manifest, whether upon water or land, may all alike bathe in the true compassion and together attain the great blessings.

I am unworthy.

---

**Memorial for the Zhou-Tian Offering by Mo Tingyi**

I prostrate myself before the myriad spirits of Heaven and Earth, who fulfill their offices in yin and yang. They spread forth the transformations of the Dao, sustaining and nurturing all beings.

The Northern Culmen and Western Palace wield penal statutes to determine transgressions; the Southern Chariot and Eastern Mansion dispense nurturing care to proclaim merit. From emperors and kings down to all officials and commoners, all submit to the governance of the celestial stewards, who distinguish fortune from misfortune.

I have long been favored by karmic blessings and, though unworthy, have entered the official registers. I tread the path of peril and hardship amid the season of weapons and armor. Once following the military banners, twice residing in famed cities, yet the frontiers stretch far and distant, and the levies are heavy and numerous. If I govern with leniency, the collection of taxes yields no results; if with severity, the weary and weak harbor resentment. It is no easier than herding chickens, and far harder than taming pheasants. Moreover, as harmony has not yet been fully achieved, I must still rely on punishments and rewards. Though I have eradicated self-interest and followed only reason, I still fear that the weight of my judgments may deviate from the Middle Way. Deeply anxious over unintended errors, I have thus accumulated flaws and blemishes.

I further fear that the celestial luminaries may cast their influence upon me, or that the years I traverse may bring obstruction, thereby giving rise to calamity and decline. Here, where the borders adjoin immortal mountains, clouds veil the true temples; where grottoes embrace thunder and rain, the earth gathers dragons and spirits. Gazing upward toward the divine capital within the formless, I wish to lay bare my sincere entreaties; beholding the jade countenance beyond the mists and clouds, I pray for the descent of profound compassion.

Therefore, in accordance with the ancient rites of the *Lingbao*, I have arranged the Great Zhou-Tian Offering. It extends to the palaces and courts of the nine regions and invokes the majestic spirits of the ten poles. With bowed hands and reverent submission, I wholeheartedly pray and repent. May all sins, great and small—past transgressions and present faults, unseen disasters, and future misfortunes—all be absolved and pardoned.
