May you graciously grant expiation, dispel all adversities, reconcile long-standing grievances, and augment my modest blessings. May I attain long life, my nine generations ascend beyond, and the Three Paths open to peace.

May my family, kin by blood and bond, scattered across two lands, soon be reunited and together receive purity and fortune. Recently, during construction, I feared inadvertent harm might have been caused. I pray for safety and tranquility, that all may share in auspicious blessings. May the sacred temples within this domain, and the spirits presiding over rivers and marshes, protect the living and dispel malevolent influences. May the towns be free from flood and drought, and the people’s granaries overflow with abundance. Even those lost souls without refuge, adrift and wandering, may they partake of this blessing and attain freedom.

I am unworthy.

*Memorial for the Life-Command Offering at Mount Qingcheng by Mo Tingyi*

I prostrate myself before the Three Luminaries, which manifest auspicious signs, and the Nine Radiant Ones, which condense their splendor. Aligned with metal and wood to govern the directions, the four seasons proceed in proper order;...

Having established the symbols to fix yin and yang, the myriad beings come into existence. Presiding over the hidden and the manifest, You govern both transgression and fortune. I, in my humble and coarse nature, have been granted the honor of serving the True and Numinous. Yet I fear that in the course of my conduct, I may easily incur faults; in the path of cultivation, I have not yet aligned with the divine. Moreover, in the duties I oversee, both weighty and trivial matters rest upon me, and I dread straying from the eternal laws, thereby accumulating further errors.

Day and night, I serve in office, how dare I forget reverence and diligence? Yet good and ill fortune are difficult to foresee, and my apprehension only deepens. In addition, as the celestial bodies have their transits, I exhaust my pleas for repentance and prayer. Thus, on the occasion of my life-command, I reverently prepare this offering feast, presenting incense and flame to offer sincerity, and arranging star lamps to perform the rites.

May the Most Sublime and Sacred deign to look upon my earnest heart; may the Nine Radiant and Most Exalted Ones graciously bestow their mysterious favor. Absolve the faults of the past, dissolve the misfortunes yet to come. May grievances and debts be settled and leveled, inauspicious declines be swept away, and longevity and fortune be further augmented, ever accompanied by blessings and auspiciousness. May my family be secure in peace, and both public and private affairs flourish in harmony. I am unworthy.

**Prayer Upon the Completion of the Painted Merits at the Abbey of the Venerable Master**

Prostrate, I reflect: the immortal mountains of Green Citadel, the sacred abbey of the Venerable Master—long left unrepaired—have lately been restored to grandeur. Now that this great labor is complete, we have commissioned the work of painting. Within the vast hall, the true forms have been depicted: crane-like visages and cloud-borne countenances, as though one might encounter them in the hidden courts of the void; jade-like bearing and refined grace, as if they had descended from the limpid azure palace. Delightful to behold, awe-inspiring as if present in truth—we humbly pray that their numinous power may descend through the virtue of Water, and their blessings flow into the mortal realm. Thus, we perform this offering rite, reverently beseeching their gaze and protection. I am unworthy.

**Prayer for the Painted Images of the Five Marchmounts’ Deities**

Prostrate, I state: the Abbey of the Venerable Master, long fallen into ruin, has lately been restored. With the tasks of earth and timber now undertaken, the work of painting and adornment has been established. Within the secluded hall, the divine forms have been rendered: robes of kingfisher clouds and cinnabar brocade; vessels of dark jade and yellow cong; treasures of stellar radiance and solar essence; the distinctions of the Five Florals and Seven Honors; chariots drawn by two steeds or six horses; palanquins of cloud-wings and rosy canopies. Here are the deputy ministers and the eight mountain stewards who assist the Mandate; the august presences of the Marchmount Lords and Water Sovereigns; the ranks of the Stream Maidens and River Marquises; the elders of mountains and forests, the numinous overseers of pools and islets; the courts of emperors and kings, the offices conferred by canonical decree. Some govern the sea’s edge, eastward reaching Fangzhu; others preside over grotto-heavens, westward neighboring Kunlun’s peaks.

May all shake forth thunder and lightning, roar with dragons and whales. They inspect the hidden and manifest, record the rivers and marshes. They uphold the Supreme’s orthodox and true principles, proclaim the emperors’ nurturing grace. Drinking of the six qi, they complete the great transformation. Like autumn, winter, spring, and summer, they follow the seasonal commands without fail; like wind, rain, snow, and frost, they balance the year’s work without error. All receive the Mandate of Xuanyuan, each wielding the authority of governance. With the Marchmounts and waterways’ numinous hosts, they fulfill the offices of celestial oversight.

Thus the Perfected Lord of Mystery and Silence, bearing the weight of the august sanctuary, assumes the solemnity of imperial presence. The order of audience and tribute must be arrayed in solemn ranks. Now the master’s brush and artisan’s hand have adorned the walls in sequence, gleaming as stars in formation, towering like clouds in embrace. Thereupon, flowing robes and trailing sleeves, jade swords and pearl-studded scabbards; fiery pendants holding stars, jade tablets gathering moonlight. Some with faces like jasper and sleeves of fresh bloom seem to descend from Guye’s peaks; others in strange forms and wondrous postures appear to mirror the shores of Xunyang. The pigments are fully arrayed, resplendent and lifelike.

This must surely resonate with the divine spirits, entwining blessings and felicity. Above, it upholds the state; beside, it protects the common folk. It harmonizes the ten rains and five winds to bring forth the harvest; it pervades the nine provinces and six directions to achieve great harmony. Its vast design rivals the sun and moon, heaven and earth; its mysterious transformation encompasses all creatures, from the crawling to the rooted. Reverently we perform the libation and offering, earnestly we voice our prayers. We await the descent of mighty numen, the sure bestowal of auspicious favor.

Respectfully submitted.
*Guangcheng Collection*, Scroll Six concludes.
*Guangcheng Collection*, Scroll Seven begins.

**Prayer for the Life-Renewal Rite of Mo Tingyi**
*Composed by Du Guangting, Grand Virtue of the Imperial Academy, Purple-Robed by Imperial Favor, of the Great Pure Palace in the Upper Capital*

We humbly acknowledge that the Three Officials keep the registers, the Five Emperors determine life. The Southern Heaven records the tally of blessings, while the Northern Dipper governs the red threads of fate. As for the true courts of the sacred mountains and rivers, the bureaus of one’s life-palace—these preside over retribution without error, examine and weigh the bonds of life and death.

Your servant fears that, having been unworthily entrusted with governance, he has failed to harmonize the realm. The scales of justice may have erred in severity or leniency; the transformative power of instruction may not yet have perfected virtue and righteousness. Thus, faults and transgressions have been inscribed in the numinous archives. Without offering rites of supplication and gratitude, we dread the onset of calamitous omens.

Moreover, we fear that celestial signs and stellar influences may have aligned in ill-omened conjunction, or that the year of one’s life-palace may have encountered obstruction. The Celestial Talisman and Five Demons occupy the positions of Kun and Gen, residing in the hour of one’s natal destiny. With the first month opposing the year’s pivot, we are especially wary of decline and adversity. Therefore, on this day of primordial fate, we dare to approach the sacred mountain with reverence, to prepare the altar and unfold our sincere plea.

We pray that the heavenly bureaus may absolve our transgressions, that the earthly records may dispel our disasters. May misfortune vanish in secret, and blessings gather in radiance. May our years and blessings be prolonged, and our fortune perpetually secured. May the realm know peace, the people health and prosperity. May the grain flourish, drought and flood be averted. May no pestilence harm the people, and may customs attain the beauty of harmony.

---

**Prayer for the Life-Renewal Rite of Mo Tingyi**

We have heard that the Great Dao gives rise to all things, that primordial harmony sets the tally in motion. It shapes the forms of creatures, spreads transformation among the multitudes. It extends the work of the Supreme Dark Lord above, and suspends below the warnings of fortune and misfortune for the earthly realm. Thus, the punishment of evil and encouragement of good stand as unchanging maxims. Harm befalls the full, blessing the humble—this is the constant teaching.

Your servant has long heard the mysterious decree and dares not fail to reflect inwardly, to examine his conduct with trepidation. Though I have thought of the Dao, I remain entangled in worldly dust, holding office yet unworthy of its emoluments. Wielding the brush to define laws for the court, or overseeing the levies of the realm with the rod of punishment—my works may have stirred earth and timber, while my table has not yet forsaken roasted delicacies. The weight of my errors remains unknown, their gravity unmeasured. Thus, anxiety and fear have taken root, lest my faults accumulate and invite reproach.

Moreover, this year the Celestial Talisman has aligned with the hour of my natal destiny, while Venus lingers in a position of sorrow and stagnation. I fear my aspirations may falter with misfortune, lingering amid the allure of fame and desire; my heart may drift with calamity, drowning in the depths of wine and song. Thus, I resolve to vigilance and repentance. On this day of destiny, I dare to perform the rites of burning incense and devotion with utmost sincerity. I purify my heart in the numinous cavern, return my pledge to the sacred mountain. Gazing upon the Dipper and the constellations, I pray to efface past faults; beholding the phoenix canopy and dragon banner, I beseech the bestowal of new grace.

May my offenses be smoothed away, my grievances dissolved, disasters quelled, and blessings prolonged. May kin separated by distance rejoice in health, and the people of the realm prosper in abundance. May the blades of war be forever sheathed, pestilence unvisited, drought and flood restrained, and agriculture and sericulture flourish. May the dragon spirits remain at peace in their abodes, and all, near and far, be suffused with felicity. With a heart of red sincerity, I pledge to fulfill the mysterious design above.

---

**Prayer for the Southern Dipper Rite for Duke Jin**

We humbly acknowledge that the Scarlet Mansion guards its precincts, the Southern Palace of Longevity presides over the direction of pure yang, enacting the transformative power of the Great Dao that gives life to all things. Whatever we pray for, it surely bestows.

Your servant, though foolish and unworthy, has been favored by this sacred day, honored with proximity to the imperial inner court, and blessed with boundless grace. Yet I constantly fear my mediocrity cannot bear such kindness. I dread that the adversities of my year, the baleful influences of stellar conjunctions, may bring trials of punishment and restraint, or obstructions in my path. My apprehension grows, and I dare not rest at ease.

Thus, I offer my red sincerity and reverently perform the rites of supplication. I especially beseech your compassionate protection and the descent of your numinous radiance. May past transgressions be erased, future disasters averted. May the red tablets of the Southern Pole be extended, my years increased; may the black records of the Northern Capital be expunged, my blessings renewed. Grant me deliverance, that I may forever bear your divine grace.

**Jin Gong’s Supplication to the Earth Deity**

I humbly acknowledge that Heaven and Earth, in their vast embrace, bear all things and cover all beings. They give life to the myriad creatures and nurture the host of spirits. The virtue of the Earth, mother of all, shines upon the ten thousand existences. From rulers and ministers, fathers and sons, down to the moving and still, the flying and the hidden—wherever there is sincere prayer, it must be reverently declared.

Within my domain, warfare has repeatedly arisen. Its harm has reached the hills and graves, its slaughter spared neither infants nor the aged. Far and near lie in ashes, neither men nor spirits know peace. The suffering of this land pierces to the bone and marrow. Thinking of these countless people, my prayers are earnest and fervent. With blood poured forth and heart laid bare, I look up in hope of your compassion and protection.

I implore you to bend in mercy and heed my devout supplication, to lend your numinous power. Command the spirits of mountains, rivers, and peaks to aid in quelling calamities; instruct the officers of thunder, lightning, wind, and clouds to still the fields and plains. Fling wide the gates of the sword, that the path to the celestial court may remain unobstructed. Illuminate and revive the weary people, cleanse deep-seated grievances.

Let it not be as in Xiang Ji’s shrine, which could only dispel Shu’s troubles; nor let Jiang Mountain’s temple alone aid the Jin forces. With goblet raised and words spoken, my tears flow unchecked.

---

**Jin Gong’s Supplication to the Northern Emperor**

I humbly acknowledge that the Five Planets traverse the heavens, and the Three Origins govern the flow of qi. Above, they revere the Dipper and the Pole; below, they order human affairs. Yin and yang have their cycles of prosperity and decline, while the celestial bodies follow their appointed courses of influence.

I fear that within the span of fate and the palace of the stars, encounters with harmful conjunctions may bring obstruction and misfortune. Thus, on this auspicious day, I reverently prepare the altar of supplication, knocking upon the threshold of your sacred power, and especially beseech your compassion and protection.

May the trials of the Three Destinies and Nine Palaces be wholly dispelled; may the disasters of bright stars and dark omens be entirely stilled. May the land know peace, the people harmony. May armor be laid aside, weapons stilled, the years abundant, and customs prosperous. Forever I offer my sincere devotion, to repay your mysterious grace.

**Invocation to the Star of Venus and the Wolf Star**

It is heard that the celestial bodies of the highest mysteries each possess their sovereign governance. Some preside over the mustering of armies, others over the origins of baleful vapors. Gazing upward at their radiant splendor, the fortunes of all are bound to their sway.

Within my borders, weapons have clashed for years beyond count. Fields lie abandoned, silkworms neglected; the people suffer in ashes and blood. This grievous oppression weighs upon me, piercing to the very core.

Thus, I prostrate myself, kindling incense, and direct my heart in prayer for blessings. May my fervent plea move you to bestow your luminous gaze. I humbly beseech that the stern might of the Metal phase’s autumnal severity be tempered by the great power of righteous judgment. Aid these martial forces to purge the outskirts and capital. Deliver the land from the peril of drowning, rescue the people from their inverted plight. May bows be sheathed and weapons stilled, rains fall in season, winds blow in harmony. May the hundred grains yield their harvest, and the five weapons know eternal rest.

---

**Invocation to the Great Emperor of the Northern Dipper**

I reflect that the Dipper governs the center of heaven, its reach extending to the eight directions. Where the Pointer star directs, right and wrong are swiftly distinguished.

Now, as the season arrives at the *Zhengyuan* and the time of reckoning is at hand, may all things be graced with the blessings of renewal; may the ten thousand regions receive the nurturing warmth of your transformative power.

**Reflection on the Frontier’s Plight**

This borderland remains ensnared in war, its people mired in suffering, its fields overgrown with brambles. The season for sowing and planting is upon us, yet the common folk are barred from their plows and mulberries. In this anguish, my prayers redouble.

I beseech the Northern Pole’s celestial palace, the Seven Primes’ register of fate: turn from the people’s hollowed gaze, reverse this land’s ruin. Let peace be witnessed, let blades be forever sheathed. If I, your servant, have met with misfortune or offended the stars through fault, I willingly submit to just retribution to atone before all beings.

---

**Petition to the Northern Emperor**

I have heard that heaven and earth sustain all things, yet yin and yang know cycles of growth and decay; sun and moon illumine the world, yet cold and heat follow their ordained succession. Fortune and misfortune turn with fate, prosperity and adversity alternate. Though the course of time brings calamity—floods in Yao’s reign, drought in Tang’s—yet rites of expiation hold their power, as seen in the winds that turned back, the foes that retreated.

Now this land faces its hour of trial. The people remain unsettled, war follows war. Consulting the star-charts, we find Mars ascendant. Thus I turn my heart to the Great Dao, reverently imploring the Supreme Mystery. I open the altar of the Great Unity, perform the rites of the Three and Five. Treading the crimson whirlwind, I plead for blessings; pacing the dark Dipper, I pray to heaven.

May the arrayed fires blaze forth in might, their stellar radiance answering in the celestial realm; may the sun’s light scatter its flames, purging yin’s filth from the earth below. I pray for the sacred person’s grace, for the vast protection of the rivers and lands of Shu. May the people ascend to fortune and longevity, may the fields know rest from spear and blade. Together, let us bathe in the divine power, forever dispelling care and calamity.

Your Majesty,

I have heard that the Dipper and Pole Star hold the highest seat, overseeing the eight directions. They command the myriad forms and govern all spirits. Wherever the Dipper’s handle points, calamity and misfortune naturally cease. Yet now, within our borders, war still rages. The people have not laid down their burdens, and the times tremble with fear. Though we labor in defense, fields lie fallow and silkworms neglected. Gazing upon these overgrown wastes, my sorrow deepens. Thus I dare to offer this libation, renewing my earnest plea.

I humbly beseech the Grand Steward to display his might, the Seven Primes to enforce their decrees. May the chariots of thunder and steeds of lightning sweep the four quarters; may the winnowing winds and timely rains nurture all things. Let our lands be purified, and all living beings sheltered. If my own fate harbors disaster, if yin and yang conspire to bring misfortune, I beg to bear heaven’s punishment, that the people’s suffering may end. With utmost sincerity, I await your luminous judgment.

*Memorial of the Lord of Shu to the Northern Emperor*

I have learned that the celestial signs manifest their power, and the Northern Pole holds the highest station. It oversees all existence and illumines all beings. Its eighty-one transformations command awe; its thirty-six divine warriors embody martial prowess. It purifies creation, scrutinizing both hidden and manifest. It eradicates evil, punishes wrongdoing, and safeguards the people and the state.

Now, as the Vermilion Yang reaches its season and the Red Emperor governs the quarter, the southern winds bestow their nurturing grace, and the four seasons harmonize in clarity. The silkworms near their labor’s end, the fields demand toil—yet pestilence spreads unchecked, drums of war still sound. The people perish in droves, the countryside languishes in flight. With no ground to stand, how can they rest their shoulders? Entrusted with the defense of this land, my sorrow cuts deep. On this occasion of the temple rites, I renew my plea with utmost sincerity.

I humbly pray that the divine warriors lend their strength, dispelling miasmic vapors from the capital’s outskirts; that the cloud-borne cavalry surge forth, sweeping disease from every village. May the people know peace, near and far live without fear. Let the murky mists dissolve forever, revealing the hues of Shu’s mountains and rivers; let the drifting clouds vanish, unveiling the light of sun and moon across the nine heavens. May misfortune be smoothed away, calamity stilled.

Ever devoted, I offer this pure sincerity to match your boundless grace.

*Memorial of the Duke of Jin to the Northern Emperor*

I observe that the six qi circulate in ceaseless flow, for the Dao of heaven is the root of all creation; the seven stars of the Dipper set the measure, for the Lord of the Dipper is the source of all governance. Sin and blessing, fortune and misfortune—all are recorded and weighed.

Yet now, the lands near the capital remain unsettled, weapons still clash. The countryside knows no peace, and pestilence spreads. Mindful of this suffering, my heart aches as if pierced. Thus, on this occasion of the temple rites, I dare to voice my plea once more.

I humbly pray that your sacred power turn in mercy, that your divine might lend aid. Bestow your radiant favor upon the people, still the perils that beset the three regions of Shu. Let weapons be laid down, the times know peace, and the people rest secure. May misfortune be smoothed away, and fortune and blessings converge.

With deepest reverence.

**Thanksgiving for the Northern Dipper Rite**
I, your humble servant, am but a fool, undeservingly clad in official robes. My cultivation has been sorely lacking, my faults and transgressions ever mounting. Punishment has befallen me, and illness has taken hold. My frail form nearly perished, my faint breath barely preserved. The Three Caverns Master Du Hongguang, moved by kinship and grieved by my perilous condition, earnestly unfolded his sincere plea and silently implored the celestial truth. By your grace, extraordinary blessings descended, extending my allotted years. I lift my gaze to the protection of the divine spirits, once more beholding the light of sun and moon. Though my strength is as feeble as an ant’s, the kindness of heaven and earth is boundless. Thus, I offer this rite and libation, looking up to repay the gift of life. I humbly pray that your sacred mercy deign to accept and witness this. Unworthy as I am...

---

**Rite for the Five Planets**
I reflect that the Three Luminaries shed their radiance, the Five Wefts stream their brilliance. Waxing and waning follow their constant course, while past and present know no fixed pattern. In their revolving ranks, they govern all living things. Their influence remains unerring, their auspices and omens inextricably linked. I, though unworthy, have been entrusted with office and entrusted with lands. Yet my benevolence has not reached all beings, and my domain remains entangled in calamity and pestilence. Weapons rage with violence, people flee in displacement. A thousand *li* lie wounded, a single region poisoned by ruin. This sorrow and pain pierce my heart and liver. I recall that the supreme sages cherish life, and the perfected truths nurture all things. Thus, I dare to rely on your compassionate warmth and once more devote myself to this rite of supplication. I humbly pray that Venus display its might, aiding martial prowess on the plains; that Jupiter unfurl its splendor, spreading benevolent grace to the outskirts. May the Five Celestial Bodies follow their paths and manifest blessings, and may all things receive their protection and favor. Let the wilds know no sorrowful laments, and customs be steeped in harmony and peace. I vow to exhaust my sincerest devotion, looking up to requite your divine favor. Unworthy as I am...

---

**Northern Dipper Rite for One’s Natal Destiny**
I have heard that when the Dipper stands at the center of heaven, its handle extends to the eight directions. Where the pivot of the *Kui* points, fortune and blessings surely arrive. Now, in the midst of my fate’s course, earth occupies my natal position. Within the cycle of the *You* year, misfortune looms in the southern quarter. At this time, as the Dipper resides in the southern sky and the sun traverses my natal constellation, I humbly present this rite of supplication, hoping to attain resonance with the divine. May you wield your governing might to still the dark and obscure forces of my destiny. Grant me your profound protection, and I shall never betray your luminous grace. Unworthy as I am...

---

**Southern Dipper Rite for One’s Natal Destiny**
I have heard that the Six Palaces of the Southern Dipper are the abode of the host of sagely beings of Wen Chang. The span of life is bound to them, and the register of birth is under their charge. From the tiniest creatures to the hidden and subtle, all depend on their sovereign rule. Those who pray for life and seek blessings must bare their sincerity. I, undeservingly favored by your grace, have been entrusted with governing a frontier region. My merits are as dust, my faults as mountains. Yet now, in the midst of my fate’s course, I face obstruction and adversity. Within the celestial patterns, inauspicious influences converge. Thus, I dare to approach the altar of memorials, renewing my hopes in prayer. I humbly pray that the sagely beings of the Vermilion Palace and the exalted ones of the Cinnabar Terrace turn their compassion toward averting misfortune and calamity, opening the path from death to life. Let the weapons of this land be laid down and silenced, and the four seasons bring timely rains and gentle winds. Rescue the souls of the plague-stricken from the depths of the underworld, and deliver the wandering spirits from eternal night. Bestow the blessings of primordial harmony, and succor the realms of darkness and desolation. Let no floating clouds obscure the azure sky, and may my loyal sincerity be made manifest in the light of day. My deepest aspirations look up to your vast blessings. Unworthy as I am...

---

**Rite to the Three Honored Ones for One’s Natal Destiny**
I have heard that the great Dao shines brightly, uniquely manifesting the transformation of cherishing life; the celestial perfected ones, in their mercy and kindness, singularly extend their benevolence to save all things. Their nurturing is impartial, their governance without flaw. I, in my mediocrity, have undeservingly received your favor and honor. Though I have not rendered meritorious service, I have been deeply steeped in your abundant grace. Yet, like the snipe and the clam locked in struggle, or the sandpiper and the mussel bringing disaster, my meager virtue has invited misfortune, and adversity has gathered around me. Within the three destinies, there may be clashes and conflicts; among the nine luminaries, inauspicious influences still loom. Thus, on the occasion of my natal destiny, I reverently implore the supreme mystery. I humbly pray that you turn aside this cycle of misfortune and bestow your auspicious blessings. Pardon my past transgressions, and dissolve the calamities yet to come. Let my loyal and sincere heart be poured out, answering the grace of heaven and earth. I vow to steel myself and uphold your divine compassion. Unworthy as I am...

---

**Rite to the Twenty-Eight Constellations of the Celestial Circuit**
I have heard that the celestial patterns hang in the heavens, illuminating all things. From the moving to the still, all receive the impartial virtue of the Dao; from the hidden to the manifest, all partake in the effortless workings of the ungoverning. I, though undeservingly bathed in your favor, have been entrusted with the defense of the frontier. Truly ashamed of my meager virtue, I have nonetheless encountered profound calamity. Cities and towns lie in ruins, the people perish in droves. This sorrow and pain compel me to redouble my sincere prayers. I humbly pray that you grant your divine favor, bringing peace to the afflicted and weary. Let the banners of war be forever furled, and no sound of grievance be heard; let the harvests be bountiful, and the realm steeped in the harmony of peace. As for the disasters and inauspicious periods within the mountains and rivers, and the celestial misfortunes within the paths of the stars, may they all be dissolved and dispelled, that I may attain security and well-being. I vow to exhaust my sincerest devotion, looking up to fulfill your vast grace. Unworthy as I am...

Memorial of Ritual Classics Erudite Su Shaoyuan for the Nine Luminaries Jiao Rite

I, though base and insignificant, have fortuitously encountered this sagely age. I have received the grace of the Three Realms’ illumination and the favor of the Two Modes’ nurturing power. Yet I ever fear that my steps tread in benighted paths, my person entangled in the snares of the vulgar. My cultivation remains deficient, and my transgressions readily accumulate. Though I bear the secret scriptures and reverently partake in the sacred registers, my incense and lamps grow slack, and impurities encroach. The Dao’s qi fails to descend upon the hundred passages, and the numinous officials silently withdraw from the six palaces. Thus do pernicious influences gather within, and ailments coil about me. Day and night I tremble with anxiety, dreading that I may not be preserved whole.

Moreover, I fear that the Five Phases and Three Destinies have met with baleful decline. Saturn and Jupiter, too, now lodge in the Palace Mansion. Considering my humble self, long devoid of meritorious deeds, I am all the more alarmed at this time of calamity. Therefore, I dare to unseal the ancient canons of the River Chart and open the jiao altar, invoking the sacred texts of the Numinous Treasure to beseech the celestial portents.

I humbly pray that your profound compassion may deign to look upon me, that your divine blessings may distantly moisten me. Wash away my faults and transgressions, dissolve and dispel my misfortunes. Let the radiant stars conceal their baleful light, and together bestow auspicious omens. May the Eight Trigrams and Nine Palaces alike avert penal adversities. Let illnesses be healed, and pestilential influences purged. May my emoluments and rank be renewed, and my years extended in perpetuity. May the spirit-generals of my advancing years, the officers of the dharma registers, and the divine soldiers suspend their punishments, exalt my merits, and grant me manifest protection.

I vow ever to cultivate and strive, that I may repay this profound grace. I am unworthy...

**Prayer for the River Lord’s Celestial Net and Earthly Web Ritual**

I have heard that the primal *qi* gave rise to the embryo, and the Three Spirits initiated all beginnings. The odd of Qian and the even of Kun determined yin and yang. Metal, leather, and earth floated, revealing their celestial lodges. The nine arose from Kan, Xu, and Hai, called the Celestial Net; the six emerged from Li, Chen, and Si, called the Earthly Web. These are the realms where the two bodies ascend and descend, the domain where the Two Modes alternate. Yang lies hidden and cannot prevail; yin is severed and cannot endure. The years one traverses mark the very days of calamity.

Moreover, the harmony of heaven and earth nurtures all things, shaping forms and endowing essences, sending forth marvels to command the age. Yet all return to the authority of forging and casting, and none can escape the reckoning of rise and decline. I, a humble and benighted servant, dare not shun this dark obscurity. In the *bingchen* year, the baleful conjunction looms; in the *dingsi* year, the disaster’s term nears its end. Within these two years, I bear a hundred sorrows. I raise my prayers to the mysterious heavens, humbly beseeching dissolution.

May Your Sagely Insight deign to regard my sincere entreaty, manifest Your majestic power, and greatly dispel misfortune. Let the warp of Qian and the weft of Kun quiet inauspicious vapors in every region; let the Earthly Web and Celestial Net release the baleful terms of the lesser cycles. Let songs rise and clods be struck, restoring the plain and unadorned customs of the sagely court; let armor be bound and bows sheathed, fulfilling the subtle teachings of the Mysterious Ancestor. I shall ever tend the incense fire to repay Your profound compassion. I am unworthy…

---

**Prayer to the Nine Luminaries for the River Lord**

I, Your servant, have undeservedly received the state’s grace and been entrusted with military command. The lands of the southwest—mighty Shu and the wilds of Mao—lie under my charge. Three lodges align with the paths of Shen and Jing; eight states control the domains of the Qiang and Man. My jurisdiction is vast, and governance is arduous. I constantly fear my inadequacy, unworthy of this singular trust. Day and night, I am filled with dread and dare not rest at ease.

In recent years, disasters have not ceased: illnesses and pestilence arise in season, and warfare erupts daily. Now, consulting the *Yellow Plan* and examining the mysterious calendar, I find that within my allotted region, Venus is about to descend. Moreover, as I plan campaigns and marshal troops, I rely on the principle of punishing wrongdoing and wield the might of stern justice. I await the stilling of the four frontiers to bring peace to the myriad people.

I humbly pray that the celestial light may look down, and sagely power may secretly aid me. May Your abundant grace moisten the ninefold heavens, and Your salvation reach the perilous from a thousand *li* away. Let bows be unstrung and armor laid aside; let wells be dug and fields tilled. May no household in village or hamlet suffer from pestilence, and may distant and near alike rejoice in harmonious customs. Where the Long-Lived Star points, may all obstructions dissolve.

I shall forever bear the grace of manifest protection. I am unworthy…

---

**Yang Ding’s Prayer for the Life-Destiny Ritual**

I reflect that the Dipper governs the center of heaven, its handle shifting through the stellar ranks. The Celestial Emperor’s chariot moves alone; the floating canopy of the parasol looms high. It judges good and ill, examining and weighing transgressions and blessings. Though the dust of the mortal realm is distant, and I gaze at the starry dials without means to ascend, the celestial hearing is most keen—where there is sincere devotion, it surely perceives. The red sincerity I knock upon shall surely evoke a mysterious response.

I, Your servant, have lately been afflicted by misfortune, encountering hardship and obstruction. Roads are blocked, and kin are scattered. My youngest son and I have been sundered in two places, lost in panic, with no word reaching one another. By day, I pray to the boundless heavens; by night, I gaze upon the Northern Dipper. Hoping for communion, I long for reunion. Burning incense, tears of blood fall together; prostrating, my heart and soul are wholly given.

By Your manifest protection, I swiftly achieved return. I constantly cherish the grace of rebirth, yet have not repaid the bounty from heaven. I pass my days in trepidation, as if thorns pierced my flesh. Now, as the Jade Bureau’s immortal abode and the numinous transformations of Brocade Metropolis appear—below concealing grotto palaces, above linked to the stellar paths—communication with the divine may be expected, and the true spirits shall assemble.

I venture into this sacred realm, wishing to present my ritual prayers. I seek to repay the kindness of blessings and protection, and modestly express my reverent devotion. I await the turning of the true gaze to condescend to my mortal heart.

My youngest son was born under the sign of *renzi*; I, Your humble servant, was destined by *gengshen*. I ever hope for sagely power to eternally grant protection, dispelling the calamities of the Five Phases and Three Destinies, and dissolving the baleful terms of the celestial degrees. May I diligently cultivate and strive, and uphold the radiant and luminous.

Though millet and grain are not fragrant, the true immortals shall perceive. I am unworthy…

*End of Scroll Seven of the* Guangcheng Collection.

**Memorial for the Southern Dipper Ritual Offered by Duke Ling of Shu**

*[Note: #1 Originally written as "长," an error; emended to "辰" according to the context.]*
Composed by Du Guangting, Grand Virtue of the Inner Palace, Bestowed with the Purple Robe, by Imperial Commission

I have heard that heaven covers and earth bears all, relying on the Great Dao for generation and completion; that all beings receive their essence and nurture their spirits, subtly moved by the Most True. Thus do they achieve boundless governance and endless transformation. The True Sovereign presides, and the Mysterious Power commands. Though the Great Void stretches vast and kalpas span distant ages, the myriad beings clamor in tumult, the Nine Gates lie open and desolate. Penal laws and governance grow intricate, the divisions of the land profound. Disaster and fortune are overseen, peace and peril are bound to them.

I, your servant, have encountered the sagely mandate and, though unworthy, been honored with grace. Entrusted with the banner and tassel, charged with the duties of a minister. The land is mighty in Ba and Shu, the borders hold the Qiang and Man. Ashamed of my inability to soothe and pacify, I am ever filled with trepidation and earnest concern. Moreover, to reward the good and punish the wicked requires the use of rewards and penalties; to suppress rebellion and execute the violent demands the wielding of axes and cudgels. Sacrifices to the gods require the preparation of animals, while tax collection and corvée labor bring hardship. To govern is to do what cannot be avoided. Yet I truly fear that my judgment of talent may be amiss, my appointments ill-suited, giving rise to resentment and complaint, and thus bringing about calamity.

Now, moreover, Saturn traverses its degrees, casting its gaze upon this region. As Earth once shifted its palace, it will soon depart from Yibu. The Five Demons approach the *Kun* position, Mars treads the *Sheng* palace. Furthermore, my great fate lies in the realm of clash and rupture, my lesser fate in the year of the tomb of life. Wood is already weak, fire likewise in decline. The Celestial Talisman descends upon my active years, and in my wanderings I encounter the year of life’s end. Earth faces this region directly, and also resides in the palace of the wife. Metal and fire move in concealment, dwelling in stagnant positions. Jupiter lingers in a constellation of sorrow, while dark stars emerge in discordant directions. The celestial signs are most clear, the numbers of yin and yang fixed. How could I not be vigilant, striving to cultivate and refine myself?

Yet I fear that faults may easily deepen, transgressions accumulate, and through my errors, disaster may befall the living. Reflecting upon myself and consoling my heart, I find no rest. I have heard that in the month of the True Yang, on the day of *bingwu*, the Six Stars descend to observe, and the Southern Dipper convenes to determine life. This is the time to cleanse faults and receive blessings, to pardon sins and extend grace. Accordingly, I follow the luminous statutes and humbly offer my thanks. I approach the True Palace of the Mysterious Origin and the Sacred Altar of the Jade Bureau, meticulously preparing the tokens of sincerity, solemnly revering the incense and flame. I invoke the realms of the sun, moon, and stars, the offices of mountains, rivers, seas, and peaks. With wholehearted devotion, I conduct the grand ritual.

I humbly beseech the turning of the impartial gaze, the descent of the unfathomable spirits. From the Southern Palace, look upon this mortal realm. Together, bestow true favor and condescend to perceive my humble sincerity. Dissolve the celestial portents of disaster in this region, dispel the baleful manifestations of the heavens. Quell the calamities of the Three Destinies and Five Phases, remove the misfortunes of the Nine Palaces and Eight Trigrams. Still the afflictions of the land where Saturn casts its gaze, that I may receive auspicious blessings; avert the ominous fate of Earth’s shifting course, that I may be granted felicitous signs.

May the common people all be preserved in peace and prosperity, the grain and crops assured of abundance. May the encampments know security, the four borders be free of peril. May pestilence not encroach, weapons be sheathed and stilled. Above, may the Three Luminaries display their auspices, following the Yellow Way to bring fortune; may the Emperor’s person and the Five Planets proceed in harmony, supporting the Purple Tenuity in its embrace. May the Mysterious Ultimate and the Dragon Chart endure, the Phoenix Calendar flourish evermore.

May the dragon spirits of the land, the shrines of mountains and rivers, all extend their blessings. May they succor both the seen and unseen, reaching the dark passes of the underworld, the wandering souls and suffering spirits, the fluttering and flying, the creatures of water and land—all may they receive the grace of deliverance and protection, forever enjoying peace and blessings.

*Memorial for the Southern Dipper Ritual of the Lord of Shu*

We humbly observe that the stellar path of Shu aligns above with the Quail’s Head constellation, while its terrestrial division below adjoins the Kun quadrant. Positioned in the direction of *shen* and *wei*, it resides within the degrees of *Shen* and *Jing*. Now, as Saturn stands in opposition and Metal and Fire converge in their stations, the Five Ghosts temporarily lodge in the Second Palace, while the Earthly Unity General shifts toward the Yi region. We fear that governance may stray from compassionate nurture, laws may falter in merciful restraint, the wilds may echo with resentful sighs, and the people may suffer calamities and afflictions. Moreover, within this year’s progression and the span of this life, as punishment and conflict coincide with decline and weakness, we dread the onset of misfortune and adversity.

Daring to choose this propitious month of the True Yang, this auspicious *bing-wu* day, we reverently prepare this ritual offering to present our repentance and purification. We humbly beseech that great mercy be extended, that our earnest devotion be regarded with favor. May the inauspicious omens of celestial patterns and terrestrial divisions be dissolved, and the faults of the Three Lives and Five Phases be dispelled. May auspicious blessings be graciously bestowed, and lasting peace and security be granted. We vow to devote our hearts to governance, in repayment of the grace of cherishing life.

We cannot fully express our reverence.

*Memorial for the Zhou Heavenly Circuit Ritual of the Lord of Shu*

We prostrate ourselves before the Heavenly August Emperor, who oversees and inspects all directions, and before the Great Unity and the Ten Spirits, who traverse the Eight Extremities. They bestow disasters or blessings, omitting neither great nor small. How dare we, as ruler and ministers, forget their luminous admonitions? Now, as the Earthly Unity’s position shifts and is about to depart from the land of Shu, we deeply fear that amidst the administration of punishments and policies, there may inevitably be errors and transgressions. Filled with trepidation, we hasten to offer repentance and supplication. Reverently performing the rites of incense and flame, we express our earnest devotion.

We humbly pray that our sincerity be acknowledged and auspicious blessings be conferred. May the realm enjoy peace and tranquility, and the people revive in prosperity. May the seasons be harmonious and the years abundant, with weapons sheathed and bows laid aside. We shall renew our gratitude for the mercy bestowed and never betray the gifts of your oversight.

*Preface to the Zhou Heavenly Circuit Ritual by Attendant Censor Zhou*

We prostrate ourselves before the Dao’s qi in its ceaseless motion, nurturing and harmonizing all things. It divides the myriad spirits to spread transformation and suspends the constellations to adorn the heavens. All beings that possess spirit receive its mandate. It further appoints overseers to determine fortune and misfortune.

I, though unworthy and undeserving, have presumptuously received profound favor. Entrusted with the governance of a frontier region, I have yet to devise a strategy for victory; appointed to administer a province, my achievements in pacification and reassurance have been meager. Moreover, this land borders barbarian settlements and controls the passes of Ba, where my limited talents constantly fear oversight, and the diverse customs prove difficult to soothe and instruct. Only through vigilance and caution have I managed to preserve my position from beginning to end. Having furled the hawk banners, I now rely on the military encampment. Reflecting on the depth of the honors bestowed, how can I find peace in self-examination?

My anxieties run deep, and illness has taken hold. I often contemplate the origins of accumulated existence, extending to this present life. The Three Karmas have woven transgressions, and the Six Emotions have entangled conflicts. Past grievances remain unresolved, and old debts still bind me. Perhaps in the course of governance, rewards and punishments have been misapplied; in matters of life and death, errors may have been unavoidable. Or perhaps within the celestial patterns and degrees of the constellations, there have been encounters with inauspicious alignments. Or within the Five Phases of the Three Lives, there have been clashes and conflicts.

This year, the Five Ghosts reside in the Palace of the Wife, and the Heavenly Talisman enters the Position of Wealth. In the minor progression, the *bing* fortune is entombed, while in the major progression, the Water of *zi* approaches decline. Metal and Fire move through the Palace of the Body, and the Net Star afflicts the Post Horse. All these portend adversity, redoubling my apprehension and doubt. Thus, in times of illness and suffering, I have silently prayed and vowed, hoping for resolution and repayment.

Now, as the myriad sages extend their compassion and the host of perfected beings show their mercy, they deliver me from affliction and grant me healing. Gazing upon the workings of the Mysterious Creation, I know where to turn; moved by the vast grace bestowed, I seek to repay it. Unfurling the true patterns of the River Chart, I approach the numinous altar of the Jade Bureau. Preparing rites of purification and reverence, I establish the Great Circuit of the Zhou Heavenly Ritual. To the stars, the sun, and the moon, I offer my utmost sincerity; to the Earthly Prisons and Heavenly Passes, I extend my declarations of gratitude and repentance.

We humbly pray that our earnest pleas be witnessed and our pure sincerity be accepted. May auspicious blessings be eternally bestowed, and aid and protection be granted. May transgressions and faults be eradicated, and the span of life be prolonged. May grievances and debts be resolved, and calamities and misfortunes be transcended. We vow to diligently cultivate and serve, in accord with the Mysterious Compassion.

We cannot fully express our reverence.

**Wang Zongpu’s Prayer for the Six Jia Ritual**

We humbly acknowledge that the Great Dao congeals in radiance, while the Primordial Venerable unfolds transformation. From the inception of unified qi, the five agents take their places. In ceaseless cycles of beginning and end, the myriad beings are born and completed. Above, the kalpas turn through the revolutions of time; below, human relations are shaped by fortune and misfortune. All who receive form and nurture essence depend on the mysterious workings of the Dao.

Your servant has long revered purity and emptiness, aspiring to draw near the serene and formless. Having been granted access to the secret registers, I have ever hoped to follow and cultivate them. Recently, while on a mission to the capital, I traversed perilous and distant roads. Fearing neglect in my duties, I silently offered prayers. By the hidden aid of the Dao’s power, I was secretly shielded with extraordinary blessings. Arriving in the Qin lands, I met with unblemished fortune; returning to the Shu city, I bore no trace of failure or harm. Gazing upward in gratitude for this numinous grace, I earnestly desire to repay it.

Now, as the esteemed festival of the Double Ninth coincides with the auspicious day of *jiazi*, I humbly prepare my modest sincerity and reverently present this ritual offering. May the divine majesty deign to look upon me, fulfilling my humble wishes. Accept my crimson devotion and proclaim your vast blessings. Let transgressions be swept away, grievances resolved, disasters dispelled, and good fortune assembled. In serving my parents and the state, may I ever receive compassionate protection; in upholding my duties and advancing in rank, may I forever bear the gifts of the true spirits.

**Meng Yanhui’s Prayer for the Northern and Southern Dipper Ritual**

We humbly recall that the Great Dao nurtures the numinous, while the Heavenly Venerable expounds transformation, seizing the moment to manifest auspicious signs and send forth sages to the world. Thus do they rectify the state and succor the age, proclaiming merit and benefiting all beings. Endowed with the pure qi of the stars and constellations, they gather the essence of mountains and rivers. All receive their mandate from Heaven and concentrate their spirits upon the earth, expanding their capacities to the utmost to aid living beings.

Your servant, as Military Commissioner and Prince of Langye, was born under a propitious star and has repeatedly received the sagely favor. With martial might, I have upheld the Tang dynasty; with loyal devotion, I have assisted the sagely enterprise, illuminating the restoration and securing the throne. Tribute has ever filled the imperial treasury, and my integrity has led the feudatories. Given these meritorious labors, I should rightfully receive divine favor.

Now, on this auspicious day of my birth, I prepare offerings of sincerity and reverently perform the ritual. Following the *Taiyi* method of invoking the true, I approach the altar where the Perfected Ones pay homage to the Dipper. Incense drifts through the empty courtyard; lamps glow in the still night. With heart poured forth, I present this petition, hoping for a response. Universally, I contemplate the celestial patterns in silent reflection, offering prayers to all true spirits.

We humbly pray that the stars traverse their celestial paths, that earthly and heavenly offices witness our devotion, that the host of sages turn their radiance toward us, and that the myriad spirits look upon us with favor. Bestow auspicious omens and extend great blessings, opening the realm of longevity and magnifying illustrious merit. May I forever assist the sagely court and uphold the imperial throne. May dragon spirits lend their aid, and the riverine lands know peace. May the hundred grains flourish, and the five weapons be sheathed. May customs be harmonious and the years free from calamity. May all beings, seen and unseen, together attain the transformation of the Dao.

**Prayer for the Nine Luminaries Offering by Minister of Works Zong Ke**

We humbly acknowledge that the Great Dao extends its compassion, while the myriad spirits fulfill their offices. Yin and yang unfold transformation, and the stellar patterns reveal their signs. They illumine the hidden and manifest, shaping all things in their ranks. Governance follows measure, and retribution for sin or blessing knows no error.

I, though base and insignificant, have been sheltered beneath the vast canopy of grace. Undeservingly, I have long enjoyed favor and rank, early granted honors and emoluments. For years, I have led troops and disciples, and still hold the insignia of office. Yet I fear my talents are slight for so weighty a charge, and that fortune may turn to misfortune. Day and night, I tremble with anxiety, daring not rest in ease.

Moreover, this year’s celestial motion has brought the heavenly tally into the central palace, while the direction of royal charge again aligns with the great cycle. The post horse star is opposed by the Five Ghosts. The minor cycle clashes with the major, and both my birth month and natal hour are afflicted. As Saturn traverses its course, illness and calamity have arisen, and I have yet to recover.

Examining myself and reflecting on my heart, I am filled with dread. I have heard that the celestial bureaus and exalted sages record life and death, while the Northern Dipper and Southern Palace govern the clarity of sin and blessing. Thus, I dare lay bare my heart in earnest supplication, prostrating in prayer to seek grace. With reverence, I approach the sacred altar and present my offering with utmost devotion. Though my gifts are meager, my sincerity is fervent.

We implore the myriad sages and honored spirits to open their grace and grant protection. Pardon my sins accumulated over past lives, and dissolve the misfortunes of my three destinies. Strike my name from the Dipper’s death register, and inscribe it in the Southern Palace’s ledger of life. Dispel the convergence of calamities, and reconcile the bonds of grievance. Banish illness and suffering, and extend my allotted span of fortune. I vow to cultivate diligence in repayment of this profound grace.

**Prayer for the Natal Offering by Zong Kui of the Ministry’s Bureau**

We humbly acknowledge that the Great Dao gives birth and completes, while yin and yang nurture and sustain. Governance follows measure, and retribution for sin or blessing is never overlooked.

I have undeservingly enjoyed favor and honor, ever mindful of caution and fear. Though I reflect on my faults and examine my heart, I still dread that in my conduct, the slightest error may go unnoticed.

This year, within my three destinies, the qi of earth and wood is weak; in the course of my fate, both life and fortune are meager. The heavenly tally occupies the position of office and emolument, while the year’s wandering star aligns with the direction of doom. The major cycle is afflicted by Saturn’s influence, and the minor cycle is governed by the original hour. Ketu lingers in a stagnant constellation, while Venus enters a realm of discord. Morning and night, I tremble with anxiety, fearing the onset of disaster.

Thus, I dare follow the sacred statutes and rites, preparing a pure offering in earnest prayer. My spirit races toward divine transformation, and I lift my gaze to the mysterious heavens in fervent supplication.

We pray that the celestial and terrestrial courts, the Nine Luminaries, and the Southern Palace will deign to witness our sincerity and bestow their profound protection. Grant me the grace of renewal, and pardon my past transgressions. Dissolve the calamities of the five phases and three destinies, and dispel the perils of the lunar mansions and dark voids. Cleanse my faults, and reconcile the debts of grievance. May I uphold impartiality and selflessness, and wholeheartedly serve my lord and kin. May public and private affairs flourish, and my household and dependents enjoy peace and well-being. May all, living and departed, together partake in blessings and good fortune.

**Prayer for the Nine Luminaries Offering by Minister of Works Xu Geng**

We humbly acknowledge that the Celestial Court and Earthly Bureau govern the registers of fate, while the Southern Palace and Northern Dipper record the cycles of life and death. The Three Officials hold the documents of judgment, and the Five Emperors preside over the ledgers of destiny. Thus, those of us below are indeed bound to the mysteries above.

Moreover, in this world of existence, good deeds are difficult to manifest, while transgressions and errors easily accumulate. Though I have long been undeservedly honored with distinction, I have failed to render commensurate service. Whether in governance I have erred in penal statutes, or in my domain I have misapplied rewards and punishments, my faults have piled up before the Earthly Bureau and Celestial Court, my sins entwined with the paths of stars and the realms of the sun. Yet I have offered no repentance, nor have my offenses been absolved.

Furthermore, in the midst of my current fate, I now face a time of calamity. Mars flies through my minor destiny, the Celestial Talisman enters my central palace. Mercury lies hidden in the realm of punishment and misfortune, Saturn retreats to a mansion of sorrow and distress. Though the fire of fortune waxes strong, the earth of my natal hour remains weak. For years now, my afflictions have not abated. My earnest supplications arise from deep anxiety and fear.

We reflect that the Supreme Sages and Perfected Ones, in their boundless compassion, nurture all things. With a devoted heart and focused mind, they respond unfailingly to all who call. Thus, we rely upon the bond of incense and flame, meticulously performing the rites of offering and prayer. In sincere repentance, we bow our heads in hope of mercy.

We implore Your compassionate regard for our humble service and Your gracious bestowal of divine protection. Dissolve the calamities already formed, pardon the sins and errors of the past. May the Southern Dipper extend my life, and the Northern Palace remove the mark of death. Secretly increase my allotted years, and grant me peace and security. May my illnesses be healed, my afflictions pacified, and my family and dependents enjoy health and prosperity. Thus shall I forever bear the boundless grace of the Many Sages, who grant me rebirth.

---

**Prayer for the Great Offering to the Southern Dipper by the River Lord and Grand Preceptor**

We humbly acknowledge that the great transformations of creation began with the division of primordial essence, giving rise to heaven and earth and shaping yin and yang. The Three Norms were established as foundations, and the Four Seasons were set in motion to complete the year. Thus, the myriad spirits received their offices, and the five *qi* were apportioned. The Celestial Court and Earthly Bureau oversee the registers of life and judgment, ordering the scales of sin and blessing, and regulating the mechanisms of retribution. Nothing, however minute, is overlooked; from ancient times to the present, no detail has been disordered.

Moreover, above, the celestial bodies trace their paths; below, the mountains and rivers are governed. Their influence waxes and wanes with the cycles of fate, and their warnings are manifest in reverence and caution. Gazing upon the mysterious teachings, how could we fail to cultivate ourselves accordingly?

I have long been favored by Heaven’s grace and blessed with sagely commendation. Elevated to the lofty rank of the balance, I wield the authority of the axe. Yet in upholding the jade statutes and golden laws, I fear I have erred in weighing matters of grave import. Though I have issued repeated commands, I am ashamed to have strayed from the proper path of instruction and governance.

Nevertheless, I have striven to aid my lord and devoted myself wholeheartedly to the realm. I have cut down the long serpents to restore the palace, and quelled great omens of disaster to still the weapons of war. I have reclaimed cities and shattered fortresses, transforming the customs of ant-like swarms and bee-like throngs into a people who turn toward civilization as guests toward a host. The Three Shu regions are now at peace, and the four classes of people live in harmony—all through the power of the Sages above. Though I have clearly received the favor of the divine, I still fear that in governance I may have fallen short.

Perhaps my faults and flaws are too grave to escape scrutiny. Perhaps I have strayed from the Dao and my heart has not yet aligned with the divine. Perhaps the stars of my domain portend disaster, or my current year brings a convergence of misfortune.

This year, my minor destiny encounters the *jiesha*, and my major destiny meets the Celestial Talisman. Saturn opposes my body’s palace, and my current year clashes with my life’s position. Constantly mindful of these warnings, I seek to perform rites of repentance and prayer.

Now, on this auspicious *bingwu* day—the day when the Southern Dipper descends in its true form—and with the Six Palaces of the Many Sages overseeing the registers of fate, I humbly present the rites of offering and libation, hoping to convey my earnest supplications.

We implore the Celestial Gate to bestow its blessings and the Pole Star to extend its mercy. Pardon the transgressions of the past, and grant auspicious protection for the future. May calamities and misfortunes be stilled, and our lands enjoy peace and tranquility. May distant and near regions revive, and dragons and spirits live in harmony. May wind and rain be balanced and timely, and illnesses and plagues be dispelled. Let the prosperity of the people be our greatest omen, and the abundance of the year our supreme blessing. May loyalty uphold the altars of state, and stillness answer the spirits. With sincere devotion, we seek to repay the mysterious grace above.

---

**Prayer to the Perfected Lord of Mount Qingcheng by Jia Zhang**

We humbly observe that Min and Shu form a mighty metropolis, the great bastion of the southwest. Below, its myriad valleys coil in repose; above, it upholds the Nine Purities.

**Prayer to the Perfected Lord of Mount Qingcheng by Jia Zhang**

It is the wondrous court of creation, the hidden sanctuary of immortals. Jade palaces and jasper towers lie concealed within the Terrace of Washings; emerald cliffs and cinnabar crags yawn aloft into cloud and mist. Here the loftiest Perfected dwell in repose, and the supreme Sages wander in leisure. Truly, it governs auspicious omens to bless the seas and lands.

I have been favored to encounter the transformative power of the Dao and have long borne its mysterious grace. Yet ashamed of my meager merits, I find it difficult to repay the virtue of heaven and earth. Living amidst the worldly, I easily accumulate faults and transgressions. In past lives and this present one, how could I be without error? The five phases and three destinies may yet bring misfortune and decline. The celestial paths and stellar patterns may cast baleful influences. Perhaps I am hindered by old grudges or entangled in unresolved disputes. Any of these would be cause for dread.

Thus, I dare to lay bare my heart upon the sacred peak, bowing my head to the immortal capital. With sincere offerings, I present my distant prayers. May you deign to witness my earnest devotion and bestow your mysterious favor, that boundless blessings may flow, life’s span be prolonged, and calamities dissolve. May sins and faults be absolved, grievances and debts reconciled, and official emoluments endure. I further pray for the continuity of descendants and the flourishing of my lineage. With a heart of reverent devotion, I seek to repay the protection of the immortal spirits.

---

**Prayer for the Birthday Offering to the Perfected Lord of Mount Qingcheng by Zong Kui, Prefect of Shuzhou**

We humbly observe that the Dao shapes all things, and the celestial origin establishes the supreme pole. The Perfected Sovereign issues commands, presiding over the myriad spirits. Thus, all beings receive their destiny and assume their forms, each inscribed in the celestial registers and ascending to the mysterious heights.

I have been nurtured by the generative power of the Great Dao and am deeply grateful for the sagely favor bestowed upon me. Entrusted with governance over the lands of Min and Chu, I bear the weight of the imperial balance. Though my achievements are manifest, they have not yet matched the workings of creation; though the honors granted me surpass those of past and present, the times are fraught with peril. The celestial chariot makes its solemn progress, and I regret that I cannot personally support the imperial pole, defend the emperor’s carriage, stabilize the cosmos, purify sun and moon, secure the great treasure, and restore the dynasty to prosperity. Only by invoking the true spirits do I hope to uphold my loyal devotion.

We revere Mount Qingcheng as the divine bastion of the celestial realm, where hosts of Sages reside and ranks of Perfected exercise their authority. Surely, they can marshal their numinous power, command the armies of the unseen, dispel calamities to pacify the Central Plains, and rescue the realm from chaos to restore the great enterprise. Thus, I follow the secret rites and reverently prepare the altar for offerings. May the unfathomable might of the spirits be turned to bestow boundless blessings, that demonic vapors be stilled and the imperial destiny flourish. May the phoenix’s reign and the dragon’s chart endure as long as heaven and earth.

I have accumulated faults and transgressions across lifetimes, and misfortunes loom unmanifest. Through this repentance and prayer, I seek their dissolution. This year, both my major and minor destinies reside in the western quadrant, clashing with my natal sign. Mars shines upon my native region and occupies my life palace. Earth traverses the dire conjunctions of misfortune, while Metal lies in discordant retreat. The year confronts the Three Killers’ position and stands at the Gate of Six Harms. I fear these baleful influences may bring disaster and am deeply anxious. Only through these offerings do I express my utmost sincerity, praying that calamities be averted and my loyalty fully realized. May I fulfill my duty to sovereign and state, accomplish my plans to quell chaos, and gloriously assist the sagely court—all through the protection of the spirits.

---

**Prayer for the Nine Luminaries by Zong Rujiu, Banquet Commissioner**

We humbly observe that the two luminaries radiate their numinous power, and the three origins govern transformation. All beings receive their forms and nurture their essences, looking up to the benevolence of the Great Dao; all are endowed with life and existence, ever indebted to the virtue of the divine.

I have been sheltered by the mysterious grace of the Dao and have fortuitously encountered a time of prosperity. Repeatedly, I have been undeservingly honored with favor and burdened with official duties. Yet my achievements remain unworthy, and I am deeply moved by the extraordinary grace bestowed upon me. In my conduct and self-discipline, I dare not forget vigilance and diligence. Yet in my thoughts and reflections, I fear I may have been remiss. Moreover, my duties are weighty and difficult: overseeing banquets, rewarding troops, preparing feasts, comforting the masses, and disciplining the army. I fear that in administering punishments, I may err in severity or leniency; in butchering and cooking, I may commit unintended mistakes. These could lead to grievances and debts, accumulating sins and flaws. Perhaps in past lives or this one, old transgressions remain unresolved. The five phases and three destinies may yet harbor misfortune. This year, the dimly shining Saturn resides in my life palace, while the celestial tally of the Five Demons approaches my fate’s path. Mars nears the palace of punishment and misfortune, and Venus traverses the position that clashes with my nature. Illness has arisen, lingering unresolved.

Fearing that calamities may deepen, I knock upon the gates of prayer, knowing that the utmost Perfected aid all beings, and the Great Dao cherishes life. It broadly opens the gates of expiation and demonstrates its responsive power. Thus, I follow the prescribed rituals and reverently prepare the altar, baring my heart to the Nine Luminaries and gazing upon the stellar hosts to present my earnest pleas. May the celestial light deign to witness my devotion, and the sagely creation lend its aid. May past injuries and unintended killings be absolved, and sins accumulated across lifetimes be pardoned. May dire conjunctions be dissolved, and calamities dispelled. May the six qi flow freely, and the hundred ailments be cured. May the blessings of my allotted fate be fulfilled, and my official emoluments extended; may the grace of rebirth be granted, and my lifespan prolonged. May public and private affairs prosper, and my family and dependents enjoy peace. I look up to the mysterious grace with reverence.

---

**Prayer for the Perfection of the Cosmos by the Duke of Suifu**

We humbly observe that the Great Dao of emptiness and non-being nurtures all beings, while the myriad spirits of heaven and earth govern all things. As for the bestowal of form and endowment of qi, the manifestation of images and the exercise of numinous power—all rely on the workings of creation and depend upon the generative power of life.

I inwardly reflect upon my meager virtue and have long borne the grace of the Dao. My contributions to the sagely court remain unworthy, yet the honors bestowed upon me as a regional pillar have been abundant. The banners of office and dragon seals, the insignia of authority and military command—repeatedly, I have received the emperor’s favor. Yet mindful of my inadequacy, I am deeply anxious. I constantly fear that rewards and punishments may be unjust, that legal judgments may be improper, that my actions may deviate from principle, and that my governance may fail to harmonize with the people’s will. In construction projects, there is the burden of labor; in banquets and rewards, the expense of feasting. Unintended injuries and killings, old debts and grudges—these sins and faults may incur divine censure.

At times, the Five Phases and Three Destinies, the dimmed luminaries and arrayed stars, jointly weave calamitous entanglements, giving rise to illness and misfortune. Though not yet fully recovered, I am doubly alarmed by the peril. This year, my major fate resides in the domain of declining qi, while my minor fate occupies the position of the broken Horse. Jupiter retreats above the Palace of the Body, Saturn shines upon the direction of the Three Harmonies. The Metal and Water stars lodge in discordant constellations, while the Flying Heavenly Mars occupies the celestial mansion of my natal destiny. The Nine Palaces’ Saturn once more governs my birth month. Witnessing these baleful portents, I am deeply moved to offer prayers and supplications.

Thus, in accordance with the *Mysterious Regulations of the Numinous Treasure* and the *Secret Patterns of the River Chart*, I have arranged a grand *jiao* ritual spanning the celestial circuit, repenting and beseeching the Supreme Mystery. I humbly implore the myriad sages to be moved by my sincerity, the host of spirits to witness my devotion, to accept my earnest pleas, and to bestow blessings and felicity. May past debts and former grievances be dissolved, deep calamities and grave transgressions pardoned. May my mandate and emoluments be prolonged, my years of life extended. Amid the Five Stars and Four Sceneries, may all perils and misfortunes be forever dispelled; within the celestial and terrestrial bureaus, may auspicious omens be newly inscribed. May my ailments be wholly dispelled, granting me peace and ease. May my loyalty and filial piety be further strengthened, that I may better serve my sovereign and parents.

Thus, I reverently rely upon the protective grace of the exalted ones, a favor I can never fully repay.

**Memorial for the Nine Luminaries Ritual Offered on Behalf of the Prince by His Attendant**
I have heard that the celestial bodies manifest numinous radiance, acting on Heaven’s behalf to transform all under heaven. They unfold the efficacy of the Dao and make manifest the wondrous works of the spirits.

At the very inception of cosmic division, the luminaries revealed their sovereign power of illumination. All living beings, moving and still, depend entirely upon their mysterious grace. I have received the celestial benevolence and am deeply steeped in the imperial favor. Yet my achievements remain unworthy of the encompassing earth and sustaining heaven, while my honors and glory already surpass those of all other ministers. I constantly fear that my conduct may stray from propriety, that rewards and punishments may be misapplied. The golden statutes and jade decrees may falter in compassion; campaigns against rebels and executions of the wicked may err in leniency toward the axe and block. Grudges from former ages remain unresolved, while the transgressions of this life swiftly become manifest. Reflecting upon this, I am ever filled with trembling awe.

Moreover, in this year, both the major and minor cycles of my fate converge in opposition. From beginning to end, the eclipsing spirits all take their positions in illumination. My branches are bound to fire and wood, yet lie within the waning qi; the celestial tally flies forth, resting upon the post horse. Together, these portend calamity and stagnation, deepening my anxiety and dread. Recently, I have been afflicted by minor ailments, which have yet to fully abate. Thus, my prayers for grace and atonement are all the more earnest.

On this day of my nativity, I reverently offer this ritual memorial. May the Most Sagely Ones deign to look upon my sincerity, absolve the faults of the past, and dissolve the perils yet to come. May my years of life and allotted emoluments be extended, and all enmities and doubts be harmonized and released. Thus may I fully dedicate my humble devotion, uphold the great treasure, pacify the weary populace, and assist in the restoration of the realm. I vow to devote my heart to self-cultivation and diligence, forever repaying the bounty of the true numina.

*Here ends Volume Eight of the Guangcheng Collection*
*Guangcheng Collection, Volume Nine*

**Memorial for the Nativity Ritual of Minister Zheng Tan of Qingcheng**
*Composed by Du Guangting, Grand Virtue of Literary Works by Imperial Commission, Purple-Robed Bestower, Inner Attendant of the Supreme Clarity Palace in the Upper Capital*

I humbly submit: Born of qi and endowed with spirit, we wholly depend on the Great Dao. Our lives and natures emerge by the grace of the Supreme Mystery. The span of longevity we pray to extend, the boundary between fortune and misfortune—all hinge upon the interplay of the Five Phases and the alternation of the Two Qi. Truly, we rely on the governance of the divine, and dare not slacken in reverent devotion.

This year, the year-star of Mars resides in the direction of my nativity; the Golden Star of the Nine Palaces stands above my current age. Long afflicted by illness, I have yet to recover. I fear that in my conduct and intentions, I may have fallen short in hidden virtue; in nurturing the people and fostering all things, I may have neglected governance. Perhaps lingering transgressions from past lives remain unexpiated, or ancient enmities unresolved. Such grievous calamities have left me no path for repentance and prayer.

Moreover, this site borders upon the immortal mountains, its earth aligned with the grotto-heavens. My sincerity may be declared, and the true numina cannot be deceived. Thus, on this day of my nativity, I dare to prepare the ritual of offering and prayer. With a cleansed heart, I confess my faults and earnestly beseech for life.

I humbly implore that the phoenix-drawn chariots may pause and descend to this mortal realm. Moved by my distress, bestow upon me your grace and repose. Strike my name from the Black Register of death, and extend my years and emoluments anew. Inscribe my fate in the Vermilion Record of life, and absolve all deep transgressions. May enmities be harmonized, calamities dissolved, public and private affairs flourish, and my kinfolk dwell in peace. I vow never to forget my resolve for self-exertion, that I may repay the protection of the true numina.

*Memorial for the Ritual of Offering and Prayer by the Minister of Works of Zongshou Prefecture in Guozhou*

I have heard that the Two Luminaries illumine the heavens, governing all beings below. Life and death are bound to them, as are sin and fortune. Though I am but dust, I have received their gaze and protection. Yet within the three destinies, the forces of water and fire are weak. This year, the celestial net of the year-star and the month-star of *chen* and *xu* ensnares me, while the two cyclical phases meet their tombs—both ominous times. Moreover, Mars has entered the Palace of the Head, and dark stars lurk in the position of my fate. Disasters accumulate, and my dread runs deep.

Thus, I dare to follow the luminous statutes, reverently presenting this ritual memorial. I uphold the blessings of purification and meticulously prepare the offerings of prayer. For three days, I maintain solemnity; at nine hours, I submit my petitions. I humbly hope that the dark compassion may shine upon me, and the vast grace descend. Grant that my calamitous fate be pacified, my misfortunes transcended. May I prolong my allotted blessings, and justly receive felicity and fortune. May I forever preserve peace and constantly receive protection. In serving my parents and sovereign, and in bringing tranquility to the realm and home—shall I not vow to exhaust my sincerity and repay the dark grace?

*Memorial for the Earth-Thanksgiving Ritual by Yang Shentuan*

I humbly submit: The Dao’s qi divides its radiance, and the dark power governs all. Below, it stabilizes the numinous transformations; above, it matches the arrayed stars. Here, the myriad sages gather in repose, and the host of immortals find their abode. From the beginning of kalpas to this very day, the Jade Maidens have ascended as honored guests, recognizing the fragrant springs by the riverbanks; the Dark Primordial One has halted his chariot, leaving the Jade Bureau at the city’s edge. The auspicious splendor of the Heavenly Eye shines forth to pacify the well and net of the land; the paths and tunnels of the Grotto-Palace open to bless the earth’s foundation.

This is the sacred precinct of the Brocade Capital, the divine and transcendent abode of Shu. Yet for long, its halls have lain neglected, its sacred grounds overgrown. The pure altars have become trampled grounds, the secluded halls tainted by the stench of impurity. Our king of Shu, with far-reaching divine insight, gazing upon this numinous threshold, swiftly commanded its purification and restoration. The soot was swept from the stone walls, revealing the immortal’s majesty; the brambles were cleared from the overgrown steps, once more revealing the sacred grotto.

Thereafter, repeated renovations gradually restored its splendor. Halls stand in sight of one another, towers and terraces stand side by side.
