The gates and portals were relocated, now overlooking the bustling thoroughfares. Evening chimes and morning bells now fulfill the rites of dawn and dusk; morning incense and evening lamps now complete the rituals of purification. How may I repay such virtue? My gratitude arises from this.

Thus, I present this ritual of offering and prayer, hoping to reach the true numina. I humbly implore that divine grace be widely bestowed, and great blessings generously conferred. May the sagely sovereign’s years be prolonged, and the myriad regions pacified; may the king of Shu’s longevity be extended like the camphor and cassia, and the Three Shu enjoy renewed peace. May the generals and officers of the encamped troops each be exalted in the annals of merit; may the households of the people together delight in the harmony of peace. May the dragon deities rejoice, and the crops flourish in abundance. May pestilence not encroach, and weapons forever be sheathed.

For those who have defiled this place with foulness or violated it with excavation, through this repentance and prayer, may all be absolved. We, who assist the times and benefit the people, who propagate the teachings and establish merit, who present offerings to the throne and commune with the sacred—may public and private affairs thrive, and our kinfolk dwell in safety. Moreover, may the transformative power of the past teachings and the old virtues of the former masters flow unobstructed, and the fruits of the Dao swiftly ripen. May the officials within and without, the yin and yang generals and functionaries, be promoted in rank and forever assist the court of blessings. May we ever uphold the wind of the Supreme Dao and constantly receive the grace of the exalted numina.

**Prayer at the Yu Temple in Zhongzhou**

We humbly acknowledge that the Three Qi gave form to the embryo, and the Nine Origins shaped the essence. Pure and light, turbid and heavy—true essence refined in the furnace of creation. Emerging from *Zhen* and riding *Qian*, the *Great Ease* unveiled the latent potential of Heaven and Earth. The sky of Yao succeeded in covering, the sun of Shun transmitted its brightness. The Five Teachings were duly spread, yet the fate of Huai and Xiang remained unchanged; the Four Gates were opened, yet the sorrows of darkness and inundation still lingered.

Only our sagacious and luminous sovereign, rescuing this lower realm, toiled for four years and wearied himself for the myriad regions. Vast and untroubled, the hundred grains knew the path of tributary flow; towering and revered, the mountains recognized the supremacy of the sacred peaks. He demarcated the Nine Provinces and pacified the myriad beings. The merit of casting the tripods was accomplished, and the reward of bestowing ranks was made manifest. This great achievement shall shine through all antiquity.

Your servant, having long received your vast grace, is privileged to serve at this immortal shrine. Ba’s rains and Wu’s clouds descend upon the jade hall; the waters of Min and the vistas of Chu gleam upon the crystalline steps. We pray that your boundless mercy may turn toward us, deigning to regard our earnest supplications. Delving into the scriptures of the jade grotto, we perform the libation upon the sacred peak. May this fulfill the distant prayers of the King of Shu and grant this humble servant’s wish to return home.

**Prayer at the Immortal Capital’s Mountain Altar by the King of Shu**

We humbly acknowledge that true essence manifests auspiciousness, and primordial *qi* divides into forms. Accumulated excellence and layers of refinement in the human realm congealed into an immortal mountain; gathered subtlety and wonder beyond the material world established a solemn grotto-heaven. Above, it connects to the stars; below, it blesses the state and its people.

Thus, the palaces of jade and gates of pearl remain profoundly secluded and difficult to glimpse. Feathered canopies and rainbow banners descend in ethereal flight. The Two Perfected Ones and the traces of the Three Capitals are revealed; the merit of the Nine Tripods is fulfilled. Ascending to perfection in broad daylight, they soar through the cinnabar heavens. Their majestic power ever grows, and the phenomena of the world are perpetually renewed. Precious scriptures and true classics, inscribed in jade and encased in jasper, are stored in the cloud palaces as a guardian presence, enduring alongside the illustrious footsteps of the past.

In distant contemplation of the mysterious wind, we gallop our unadorned sincerity. Now, as the Three Rivers witness transformation, we repeatedly encounter the ravages of war. Phoenix missives and dragon writings are no longer found in the walls of Lu; tiger tallies and turtle registers are difficult to seek in the pits of Qin. The Great Teaching has declined—it is fitting to restore and uplift it.

Therefore, we raise our gaze to the verdant peaks and bow our heads to the white clouds. We perform the rites of libation and offering, hoping for the scrutiny of the divine immortals. We set aside the sealed scriptures of the Crane Grotto to serve as the scriptures revered by humans and heavens. We await the completion of this extraordinary merit and the return to the former abode.

We privately reflect that the Dao is present everywhere, and the Dharma permits free circulation. Gazing upward at your great favor, we trust it will truly harmonize with our sincere devotion. We also pray that your hidden blessings may universally extend to the world. May the descendants of the Mysterious Origin flourish and prosper; may the palace city of the sagely sovereign be restored. May the Nine Lands know tranquility, and the myriad beings shine in harmony. May our borders be secure, our people healthy and at peace; may disasters cease of their own accord, and our allotted years and blessings increase.

Ever holding fast to a heart of loyalty and sincerity, we aspire to fully receive the protection of the Most Perfected. We cannot express the depth of our devotion.

Upon Arriving at Mount Xiandu to Present the Offering Text

We humbly consider that since the primordial transformation first divided, this mountain has stood as a guardian. To its front lies the prospect of Chu; to its side, it commands the city of Ba. Myriad streams encircle it in winding loops, its stern fastnesses arrayed as the abode of dragons and serpents; countless peaks stand in guard, their beauty forming the capital of perfected sages. The two Perfected Ones soared aloft in former dynasties, their illustrious traces shining through a thousand years. Its cliffs and peaks block out the sun, its pines and cypresses pierce the clouds. Auspicious omens gleam in its records, blessings silently sustain the state.

The King of Shu upheld the heavens, his flourishing deeds renowned through the ages. With heroic bearing, he ruled the Eight States and the Two Rivers; early on, he was enfeoffed within the royal domains, while the cities of Qian and the passes of Chu all fell within his shaping influence. Yet this immortal mountain alone shines forth across the realm.

Gazing upward to its sacred traces, we bow our heads in reverence; from afar, we extend our sincere prayers. Turning our hearts toward its secluded precincts, we devoutly perform the offering rites. We seek the writings of Yu’s cave, awaiting the encounter with the Eight Assemblies’ scriptures; we delve into the archives of Dongting, hoping to attain the Five Talismans’ secrets. May their profound mysteries be widely expounded, the true lineage fully unfolded.

Moreover, as the great teaching declines and the Central Plains face many hardships, its transmission and practice must await free circulation. We ourselves have traversed vast waves, dutifully following the established command. Burning incense, we make this solemn declaration, praying that our sincere devotion may be witnessed.

We aspire that by the Fenshui Bridge, it shall not be only the Han minister who receives transmission; by the Quyang Springs, it shall not be only Lord Gan who is granted the teachings. Carrying the sacred texts westward, may the sagely teaching be revived in this age of renewal. We cannot express the fullness of our devotion.

**Li Yanfu’s Memorial for the Luo Tian Jiao Ritual on Behalf of the Prince of Shu**

We humbly acknowledge that the Dao crowns the void and nothingness, its merit preceding the covering of heaven and the bearing of earth. It shapes and nurtures all things, its nurturance impartial. Through boundless kalpas it endures, outlasting heaven and earth. Its fashioning never ceases, its life-giving transformations ever more manifest.

Your servant has long been graced with profound favor, faithfully upholding the Dao’s dispensation. Yet my merits are as light as dust and dew, while my burden is as weighty as the balance of state. Across thousands of miles of mountains and rivers, I have traversed the six garrisons; for seventeen years, I have governed and pacified this region. Ever fearful that fortune may turn to calamity, and that my feeble strength may breed conflict, I remain vigilant in self-examination, overwhelmed by anxiety and dread.

Moreover, with the imperial carriage yet to return and the Central Plains beset by ramparts, my exhortations to train troops and inspire warriors are but empty aspirations to serve the state and aid the sovereign. Gazing toward the palace, my heart races—how distant the heavens, how remote the sun! My meager efforts yield no effect; my solitary sincerity finds no outlet.

Now, as the Four Divine Beings embark on their grand procession, lingering in the lands of Yong and Qin, and the Lesser Procession of Heavenly Unity arrives in the regions of Liang and Shu, the earth once more aligns with the Palace of Kun, while the moon’s comet traverses the Well Mansion. Gazing upon these celestial signs, I reflect upon the looming disasters. Deeply I fear that the phoenix carriage and simurgh chariot, though guarded by the hundred-fold passes and rivers, remain unrecovered; that the imperial tombs and ancestral temples, though walled by the nine-fold gates, stand yet empty.

Thus, with earnest prayer, I await your divine regard and protection. In accordance with the mystic statutes and the luminous precepts, I have prepared the Yellow Register Daoist ritual and established the grand Luo Tian Jiao. To the Nine Purities and Three Realms, we present rites of repentance and gratitude; to the celestial perfected and earthly spirits, we offer ceremonies of supplication and prayer. Encompassing the realms of sun, moon, and stars, extending to the uttermost mountains, rivers, peaks, and streams, we exhaust all reverence and solemnity, completing the full cycle of communion and response.

We humbly beseech the Heavenly Worthy to descend his mandate, the Sage Ancestors to bestow their blessings, and the divine powers to lend their aid, that the state’s fortunes may be secured, its grand designs firmly established, and its imperial destiny renewed. May it stand as enduring as the North Star, as eternal as the Southern Mountains.

Your servant, entrusted with heaven’s grace, shall forever uphold the Tang dynasty’s years. May I enjoy the longevity of the pine and cedar, and devote myself with the loyalty of metal and stone. May the realm know no disasters or pestilence, the years be blessed with abundant harvests. May timely rains fall, and weapons of war be stilled. May dragon spirits rest in tranquility, and the people and officials dwell in peace. May the gates of the underworld be touched by the mercy of deliverance, and distant lands yearn for the harmony of our transformative influence.

I vow to magnify the pure and tranquil, in gratitude to the true numina.

**Middle-Level Three Sovereigns Jiao Ritual Memorial**

We humbly acknowledge that the dark canopy floats above, the yellow chariot anchors below. The primordial essence descends as auspicious omens, responding to the unfolding of destiny and the opening of the cosmic plan.

**Grand Supreme Jiao Ritual Memorial for the Luo Heaven**

We grasp the six celestial cycles to reign supreme, our grace encompassing all within the four seas; we embody the Three Powers to shepherd all beings, our benevolence suffusing every living thing. Our moral influence fills the realm, our numinous radiance enduring across the ages, unwaning through time. We, unworthy, have received Heaven’s favor to guard the earthly quadrant. Overwhelmed by the burden of its vast protection, we vow unswerving loyalty and steadfast devotion.

Yet the celestial mandate remains unfulfilled, Heaven’s decree in temporary decline. Gazing toward the clouds, the River Chart and Luo Writ remain distant; bearing the sun aloft, mountains and rivers still bar the way. Our crimson hearts burn with sincerity, yet our toil yields no fruit.

Now the Four Spirits embark on their grand procession through the lands of Yong and Qin; the Lesser Procession of Heavenly Unity halts in the regions of Liang and Shu. The earthly guardian stabilizes the southwest, while the comet traverses the Well Mansion. Consulting the weft-texts and celestial portents, we prostrate ourselves in deep concern.

Thus, we unroll the sacred statutes and reverently prepare the Yellow Register. We conduct the Grand Luo Heaven Jiao, entreating the true numina of the Three Realms. May they bestow divine favor to reverse Heaven’s decree. Let the loyal and righteous, the valiant and resolute, wield the might of wind and thunder to sweep away all obstacles; let the civil and martial deities lend their power to restore order and governance.

May the imperial line flourish anew, malevolent vapors forever stilled. May the Nine Provinces witness an era of clarity and peace, the Three Regions of Shu receive the gift of tranquility. May disasters be averted before they arise, and blessings descend without end. Whether moving or still, living or perishing, all shall together bask in the grace of divine protection.

We dare not presume further.

Your Majesty,

In reverent examination of celestial portents and apterial signs, we find that this year the Great Wandering of the Four Spirits resides in the lands of Yong and Qin, while the Lesser Wandering of Heaven’s Unity has shifted to the region of Liang and Shu. Earth’s Unity has descended to the Palace of Kun, and the Comet of Lunar Eclipse traverses the Well Mansion. Gazing upon the celestial degrees, we trace the ominous conjunction of these signs. Reflecting upon ourselves and pressing hand to heart, we are filled with dread and trepidation.

Thus, we dare to follow the numinous statutes, establish sacred altars, conduct the Yellow Register’s solemn fast, and prepare the Grand Luo Heaven Jiao. We unfold the mysteries of the Dao and reveal the true scriptures. We humbly beseech the august deities to turn their radiance toward the Supreme Mystery, bestow blessings upon the earth below, and extend their auspicious favor far and wide, that calamitous alignments may forever cease. Grant that our borders remain secure, the dragon spirits harmonious, the people hale and prosperous, all regions revived and restored, pestilence averted, and weapons laid to rest. In our devout observance, we strive to fulfill the divine work.

We dare not presume further.

*Invocation for the Luo Heaven Jiao of the Five Sacred Peaks and Four Waterways*

We observe that as the Two Modes rise and set, the firm and yielding assume their places; as the Three Powers expand, rivers and mountains take form. The Earth’s virtue manifests its capacity to bear all things, and the myriad beings receive the gift of life-sustaining power. Though the primordial chaos knows no bounds, the cycles of nine and six still portend peril; though its expanse is infinite, it remains bound to the fortunes of obstruction and flourishing.

Now, as the movements of yin’s intestines dictate, and the apterial signs reveal, the Lesser Wandering of Heaven’s Unity has shifted to Liang and Shu, while the Great Wandering of the Four Spirits has likewise settled in Yong and Qin. Earth’s Unity has descended to the Palace of Kun, and the Comet of Lunar Eclipse traverses the Well Mansion. Gazing upon the celestial degrees, we are struck with awe and dread.

We, undeserving yet long entrusted with the grace of imperial favor, have long guarded the frontier as a shield. Our domain spans six garrisons, girded by mighty rivers. Our waters rank among the Four Waterways in dignity, our mountains stand as the eldest of the Five Peaks. The altars of immortals and numinous transformations bear traces of dragon-drawn chariots and crane-borne flights; the jeweled shores and golden dikes mark the lands where Yu dredged the waters and Qin opened the roads. Here, the true spirits reside, and auspicious responses abound. We must secure their blessings to fulfill our devout prayers.

Thus, we dare to present the Yellow Register in solemn fast and inaugurate the Luo Heaven Jiao. May the host of sages cast their light upon us, and the myriad spirits descend with their blessings. Together, may they stabilize Heaven’s course and eternally uphold the imperial design. Dispel the gloom over the divine capital, that we may once more behold the sacred sun; unify the chariots and script of the realm, that we may preserve the Tang’s enduring reign. Grant that our lands remain at peace, our people at ease. Let no beacon fires blaze on the borders, and let the customs of the land resound with songs of praise. Avert disasters before they arise, and dissolve the lingering faults of the past. We vow to remain steadfast in devotion, repaying the divine work.

We dare not presume further.

*Universal Invocation for the Luo Heaven Jiao*

We have heard that the mysterious work governs all, and the transformative power of the Dao spreads forth. It endows forms with images, coalesces spirits, and circulates qi. Heaven covers and Earth bears, arising from the boundless; sun and moon illuminate, giving rise to the ten thousand things. As for the ascent and descent of yin and yang, the passage of kalpas and the shifting of epochs, Heaven and Earth have their cycles of nine and six, while the sun and moon have their waxing and waning.

To seek deliverance and protection, we must rely on the true spirits. We, in our humble station, have encountered an era of flourishing fortune. We have been undeservingly drenched in extraordinary favor, ascending to singular honors. Dragon tablets and tiger tallies have apportioned the weight of mountains and rivers; golden statutes and jade laws have entrusted us with the lives of the people. We constantly reproach ourselves for our inadequacy in governance, ever mindful of the perils of excess.

Yet now, as the Central Plains face manifold trials and Heaven’s course grows arduous, the altars of state hang in peril, and the realm is steeped in suffering. In training and marshaling our forces, we can but hold fast to our resolve to serve the state; from afar, gazing toward the divine capital, we find no path to support Heaven’s cause.

Now, in examining the apterial signs and consulting the sacred charts, we find the Great Wandering of the Four Spirits in the lands of Yong and Qin, and the Lesser Wandering of Heaven’s Unity near the region of Liang and Shu. Earth’s Unity has descended to the Palace of Kun, and the Comet of Lunar Eclipse entangles the Well Mansion. Gazing upon the celestial degrees, our dread deepens.

Thus, we dare to unfold the scriptures of the Numinous Treasure, follow the standards of the River Chart, establish the Grand Luo Heaven Jiao, and open the sacred altar of the Yellow Register. We reverently beseech the Golden Gates and Jade Capital, invoking the myriad sages; we proclaim to all spirits within and beyond the cosmos. We rein in the horse of the mind to bare our hearts, and entrust our prayers to the incense dragon. May we be deemed worthy of divine regard and granted the descent of numinous power.

We humbly implore the deities of the Three Realms and all heavens, the Four Offices and Five Emperors, the sovereigns of Qian’s origin and the august spirits of the earthly courts. Bestow the unfathomable power of yin and yang, and lend the boundless force of transformation. Let the divine armies secretly assist, and the true responses subtly manifest. May the great enterprise be revived, and all directions know peace. May the imperial foundation stand forever, and the Four Seas be cleansed. Sweep away the baleful stars from the vast sky, and exterminate the leviathans in the mighty waves. May we ever gaze upon the sacred sun and together uphold the Heaven of Yao.

Grant that our domain remain secure, calamities stilled, the five weapons sheathed, and the four seasons harmonized. Let the people know no fear of plague, and the harvests promise abundance. In the Three Rivers and Six Garrisons, may the people, the spirits of the land and waters, all enjoy joy and well-being, together attaining purity and auspiciousness. May the lost souls and lingering consciousnesses of the six destinies and three paths bathe in the mysterious grace to quicken their spirits, ascend to the Crimson Mound, and receive blessings. Whether living or dead, moving or still, may all be revived and restored.

We vow to pour forth our loyalty and filial piety, striving to meet the divine gaze.

We dare not presume further.

*Invocation for the Luo Heaven Jiao to All Spirits*

We observe that humanity serves as the host of the spirits, and the spirits rely on humanity for transformation; the spirits bless humanity, and humanity depends on the spirits for aid. From Heaven’s mandate to Earth’s governance, from states to households, from antiquity to the present, all follow this Dao.

Our Great Tang, whose virtue was sown by Gaoyao, whose blessings were bequeathed by the sagely ancestors, has illuminated the Central Plains and transmitted its legacy through twenty emperors. The mysterious wind has fanned the myriad lands, and the imperial grace has suffused the Nine Provinces. All beings have basked in its sheltering care.

Yet now, as fortune has turned to adversity and the times have brought displacement, Heaven’s course remains unsettled, and the Emperor’s Chariot has not returned. Loyal ministers and righteous knights all hold fast to their resolve to serve the state; gazing toward the sun and looking to Heaven, none dare abandon their duty to the king.

Now, as the Lesser Wandering of Heaven’s Unity entangles the region of Liang and Shu, and the Great Wandering of the Four Spirits resides in the lands of Yong and Qin, the Comet of Lunar Eclipse traverses the Well Mansion, and Earth’s Unity has descended to the Palace of Kun. The apterial signs make this clear, and our dread and concern deepen.

Herewith, in reverent adherence to the mystic canons and with diligent study of the numinous ordinances, we have prepared the precious Yellow Register Fast and established the Grand Offering of the Heavenly Veil. Below, we have delved into the Nine Abysses; above, we have ascended to the Three Pure Realms. Solemnly arraying the rites of repentance, we humbly beseech the response of sympathetic resonance.

We prostrate ourselves before the august deities and holy sages, trusting that they will look with compassion upon our sincere devotion. May their divine might thunder forth, and may propitious winds reverse the baleful omens. Sweep away the perils that assail the azure vault, and extinguish the miasmic vapors that shroud the imperial capital. May the grand design be eternally secured, and the great enterprise of restoration flourish.

Next, we pray that the borders and regions of the realm be freed from calamity and obscurity. May the gathering of misfortunes be dispelled, and the qi of harmony and peace be summoned. May the dragon spirits be harmonious, and wind and rain be evenly regulated. May pestilence and plague be kept at bay, and weapons of war be truly sheathed. We vow to govern with diligence, that our efforts may complement the works of the divine. With millet and grain, fragrant and pure, we offer our utmost reverence; with pondweed and water plants, we fulfill the solemnity of the fast. We pour forth our earnest entreaties, prostrate and unable to contain ourselves.

*Memorial for the Life-Span Offering of Prince Shu to the Transformation of Immortal Ge*

Prostrate, we reflect: the vault of heaven arrays its luminaries, with the Dragon Star presiding above; the square earth shapes its forms, with the transformations of immortals apportioned below. Truly, they oversee the registers of destiny and govern the order of humankind. We have received the mystic mechanism and have long enjoyed illustrious protection. Early on, we were graced with abundant favor and entrusted with the governance of this multitude. Though we hold the frontiers of six marches, our virtue is meager and shallow; though we oversee the sacred sites of manifold transformations, our sincerity brims with joy and honor. We constantly fear that our governance may falter, failing to meet the scrutiny of the true immortals.

Now, as the Great Unity traverses the regions apportioned to its course, we dread that calamity may befall the lands of Liang and Yi, or that in the borders of Yong and Qin, the Comet of Lunar Eclipse may entangle the Well Mansion, and Earth’s Unity may bring disaster to the Palace of Kun. Consulting the apocryphal texts, we are filled with dread and concern. Moreover, this year is the ding-mao year, which marks the year of our own life’s origin; this month is the second month of spring, the season of our birth. We approach the transformation of our life’s origin, and on this day of our nativity, we reverently prepare incense and lamps, earnestly offering our prayers and supplications.

We humbly implore the Primordial Honored One to look upon us with compassion, and the host of sages to deign to witness our devotion. May our plain entreaties ascend to the celestial palaces, and may great blessings be bestowed upon the earth below. May the imperial enterprise be revived, disasters cease, and the imperial cortege return to Qin; may the realm and its borders enjoy peace and prosperity, and the inauspicious fortunes be dispelled, bringing auspicious omens to Shu. Thus may we fully realize our resolve to serve the sovereign and truly fulfill our heart’s concern for the state. May the hundred grains flourish, all beings enjoy harmony and peace, the dragon spirits bestow their favor, and pestilence and plague be kept at bay. May our seven ancestors ascend to heaven, and their years be prolonged. We vow to propagate the Dao and its transformations, in repayment of the divine grace. We are prostrate and unable to contain ourselves.

May this prayer be offered to the Southern Dipper:

We humbly acknowledge that the mysterious Dao divides and unfolds, initiating the mechanism of transformation. Clear and turbid are fixed in their ascending and descending positions; yin and yang operate the pivot of punishment and virtue. The Southern Dipper governs life, bestowing prosperity and encouraging goodness; the Northern Palace records death, compiling transgressions to restrain wrongdoing. The divine luminaries employ these to transform humanity, while the sovereign uses them to achieve governance. Not even the most minute detail is overlooked, and this has remained constant from ancient times to the present.

Your servant, born under the guidance of true teachings and revering the profound instructions of the Dao, dares not forget exhortation and self-cultivation. Yet, burdened with office in these troubled times, though I strive with diligence and reverence, I still fear neglect and deviation; though I remain vigilant and anxious, I am justly reproached for occupying a position without merit. In suppressing treachery and eradicating evil, I have sometimes enforced penal statutes, sometimes overseen punishments, sometimes administered the lash. In rewarding soldiers, I may have permitted executions; in feasting guests, I could not avoid the slaughter of animals. I fear that through such acts, unintended harm may have been inflicted, giving rise to deep enmity and grave offense.

Moreover, as I advance in years, my minor destiny encounters calamity. The stars that entangle me are illumined by Mars. The moon passes through *Shen* and *Wei*, while the celestial tally resides in the hour of my birth; my position faces *Chou* and *Yin*, where the flying banner strikes the point of destruction. Apprehensive of this convergence of misfortune, I am all the more alarmed.

Though I examine myself and reflect, tempering punishments and acting with caution, reducing feasts and moderating wine, avoiding excess and guarding against transgression, I still fear that misfortune has not been dispelled and blessings have not manifested. Reverently consulting the canonical texts and devoutly approaching the sacred mountain, I follow the ritual forms of the Southern Dipper, adhering to the celestial divisions of the supreme mystery. The ninefold subtle lamps cast their radiance, arrayed to correspond with the six stars; the incense of unified virtue rises in clouds, its hue ascending to the Three Primes. The bamboo hall summons both the void and the real; the pine pavilion may descend the true numina.

Thus, laying bare my heart, I dare to hope for divine favor. We prostrate ourselves and pray: may the six august palaces of the upper saints suspend the registers of death to prolong life; may the five exalted stellar deities shatter the chariot of misfortune and pour forth blessings. May grievances and resentments dissolve, calamities and perils be pacified. May kin be secure, borders and towns prosperous. May wind and rain be harmonious, grains abundant. May bandits and thieves not arise, and pestilence and plague not occur.

We humbly beseech that the *Lingbao Jade Scriptures* and the *Red Emperor’s Celestial Writ* descend to illuminate the southern cinnabar, bestowing benevolent grace upon the earth below. May we forever receive steadfast fortune, fulfilling our prayers. We are prostrate and unable to contain ourselves.

**Memorial for the Life-Renewal Offering of Vice-Governor Zheng Xu**

We humbly acknowledge that the Dark Heaven suspends its signs, and the Dipper and Pole Star hold their exalted station. They govern the ten thousand beings with impartiality, and steer the four seasons to complete the year. Below, they oversee the registers of destiny and govern fortune and misfortune. Whatever is felt is communicated; whatever is prayed for is answered.

Your servant, since youth, has reverently gazed upon your majestic power. I regard the Seven Stars as the pivot of Heaven and Earth, and the Five Qi as the foundation of all transformation. They command fortune and misfortune, and regulate the spirits. I have ever turned my heart toward the Supreme Mystery, and in times of difficulty, I have always turned to the Northern Dipper. Repeatedly, I have received manifest blessings, and auspicious signs have descended in abundance. My movements are as if followed by a shadow; my affairs are as if answered by an echo.

At times, I have wished to resign my post, seeking physicians to cure my ailments. At others, I have feared treading upon the mechanisms of misfortune, shunning ill and pursuing good. Or, when my aspirations were assailed by slander, or my flaws stirred by suspicion and resentment, I have secretly poured out my sincerity to the boundless heavens, silently borne my devotion through endless nights. The Most True has ever been my witness, and every prayer has been granted.

Yet, entangled in manifold affairs, I have been unable to repay the divine grace. I have long resolved to purify myself, hoping to inaugurate this offering. Now, Heaven has heeded my deepest yearnings, and the gods have aligned with my long-held wishes. By fortunate appointment, I find myself within the jade precincts of the immortal realm, in the very shadow of the jeweled capital, amidst the mist-laden verdure and towering walls of this city.

Moreover, as this is my life-renewal day, coinciding with the autumn season, I have been able to personally ascend the pine and cypress heights, treading deep into the clouds and mist. I have performed the rites of the Three Offerings with due solemnity, fulfilling my official duties, while also discharging the prayers of accumulated years and realizing my private devotions. In reviewing my duties and reflecting on my heart, I am both honored and overjoyed.

Thus, I dare to present this memorial with reverence, preparing incense and lamps. Though the humble offerings of mountain herbs and rainwater are unworthy to move the sagely gaze, by the virtue of responding to sincerity and seizing the moment, I pray that my foolish devotion may be received.

I hope to repay the grace of the past and await the blessings of the future. Grant me auspicious fortune and secure well-being. May the county be free from peril, the harvests abundant, the people harmonious, and customs prosperous. May near and far dwell in peace.

If your servant’s life is afflicted by clashes in the Five Phases, or if the Nine Luminaries of Heaven’s pattern traverse inauspicious paths; if governance has been unclear, or rewards and punishments misapplied; if new grievances or old debts, past killings or unintended harms remain, I beg that they all be swept away, and that eternal grace and protection be bestowed. I am prostrate and unable to contain myself.

---

**Memorial for the Life-Renewal Offering of Attendant Gentleman Sun Tu**

We humbly acknowledge that the Two Qi first divided, and the Five Phases set in motion. They beat the bellows of yin and yang, and hold the pivot of life and death. They nurture all without partiality, shaping and harmonizing without weariness. They govern longevity and brevity under the Five Emperors, and assess good and evil before the Three Officials. The Northern Dipper holds its exalted station, presiding over all beings.

Your servant, though obscure and unworthy, has received the grace of your shaping power. Clad in cap and gown, I have ever feared my undeserved position. Following the luminous teachings of the plain scholars and upholding the model words of the mysterious sages, I still fear that my every movement may err, and my conduct may stray from the Dao. It is difficult to ascend to good fortune, yet easy to accumulate faults.

Moreover, I dread the shifting of the Three Paths, lest I encounter misfortune when the Nine Luminaries traverse inauspicious positions. This year, the Celestial Talisman descends upon the direction of the Hook and Strangler, and my minor fortune coincides with the position of the Hidden Chant. Among the Thirteen Mansions, the Moon’s Comet has passed; in my great fortune and life-year, I still dwell in clash and break.

With such apprehensions, I fear to tread upon misfortune. Thus, on this day of my life-renewal, I dare to earnestly present this offering in repentance. I pray that the Perfected Sages deign to look upon my sincere prayers. Pardon past sins and dissolve grievances; bestow future blessings, increase my emoluments, and prolong my years. May my family be secure, and public and private affairs harmonious. I shall forever bear the boundless grace of the august assembly. I am prostrate and unable to contain myself.

---
*End of Scroll Nine of the* Guangcheng Collection
*Scroll Ten of the* Guangcheng Collection *begins*

**Memorial for the Ritual Offering Commanded by Vice Censor-in-Chief Li Chou**
Composed by Du Guangting, Grand Virtue of Literary Works for Imperial Service, Purple-Robed and Bestowed, of the Supreme Clarity Palace in the Upper Capital

We humbly observe that the Two Images mold and blend, the Three Origins engender and transform. They shape all beings and nurture the myriad regions. From the celestial treasury we receive our mandate and form; our lifespan’s brevity or length, our emoluments’ duration or transience—all are bound to it. In establishing oneself, one reaps the causes of sin or fortune; in traversing fate, one encounters the reckonings of good or ill. Heaven records and Earth examines, their governance impartial.

Your servant fears that in the Three Destinies and Five Phases, calamity may strike; that among the Nine Stars and Seven Luminaries, baleful influences may descend. Yin and Yang bear times of punishment and conflict; emoluments and fate meet with ominous decline. Moreover, we dread that transgressions accumulated over lifetimes remain unexpiated, that wrongs committed across generations still coil unresolved. Mortal understanding cannot fathom these, nor can the Dao of the gods be known. Without recourse to ritual supplication, there is no means of absolution. Thus, on this day of my life-renewal, I reverently prepare incense and lamps. Gazing upon the celestial patterns, I lay bare my heart; facing the star altar, I pour forth my sincerest pleas. Daring to hope that the Perfected Sages will deign to look upon my earnest devotion: may the Three Officials strike my name from the ledgers of sin, may the Five Emperors erase my entry from the registers of disaster. May past stains be scoured clean, long-standing grievances dissolved. May I be spared death in the Northern Palace and reborn beneath the Southern Culmen. May the Celestial Bureau augment my emoluments, may the Director of Destinies prolong my years. May my family dwell in harmony, public and private affairs in clarity and peace. I shall forever bear the boundless grace of the august assembly.

---

**Memorial for the Vow-Fulfilling Ritual Offering by Attendant Gentleman Zhang Daoheng**
We have heard that the celestial symbols hang from the Nine Heavens, their radiance streaming through the ten thousand beings. The Emperor’s Chariot wheels in its course, the sagely power reaching far and wide. It carves out the Four Seas without partiality, bestowing blessings upon all living things without dominion. Prayer is invariably answered; vows are surely fulfilled.

Your servant, in the second year of Great Favor, encountered peril and distress—my anxiety exceeded treading upon fire, my danger surpassed walking upon ice. Unable to secure safety from dawn to dusk, how dared I hope to preserve my body and life? With utmost sincerity, I poured forth my pleas, yet found no gate to voice my grievances. I could only fix my thoughts upon the azure vault and secretly beseech the Mystic Dipper. Silently, I vowed a great vow, hoping to redeem profound calamity. By good fortune, the Great Dao deigned to look upon me, the Perfected Ones responded to my entreaty. They extended the blessing of cherishing life, opened boundless grace. My sins were washed away, all grievances dispelled. Gazing upon Heaven’s mercy, my gratitude deepened; yet how could I repay the mysterious workings of creation?

Soon after, I was constrained by official duties, the journey affording no leisure. Years passed, my sincere vow unfulfilled. Moreover, as I traversed rivers and mountains, journeying back and forth, I repeatedly encountered disturbances and frequently faced hardship and peril. By good fortune, I escaped the clash of arms and evaded violent misfortune—all through the sheltering protection I received, which redoubled my reverence and gratitude.

Now, on this day of my life-renewal, at the Jade Bureau of Numinous Transformation, before the Hall of the Seven Origins of the Northern Dipper, in the presence of the Great Emperor of Mystic Eminence, I reverently prepare the ritual altar to fulfill my past vows. Formerly, I pledged an offering of *x* strings of cash, to be presented in five installments by the eighth month of this year. We humbly beseech the Perfected Ones of the Dipper’s midst, the high officials of the Mystic Bureau, to perceive our earnest devotion and graciously turn their boundless favor. May our long-standing vows be fully realized, may divine blessings widely bestow their grace. May sins be pardoned and disasters removed, may auspiciousness be extended and blessings conferred. May years and emoluments increase, may perils and distress be dissolved. May our families dwell in peace, public and private affairs in steadfast good fortune. We shall forever bear the covering protection of the Dipper’s august assembly.

---

**Memorial for the Scripture-Recitation and Ritual Offering for His Mother by Gentleman of the Ministry of Personnel, Zhou Xiang**
We have heard that the Three Caverns’ precious scriptures and the Nine Heavens’ true formulas, congealed in the void and blended with primordial *qi*, form their patterns. Dragon scripts and phoenix chapters trace their origins to the remotest beginnings; jade tablets and seals proclaim them before Heaven and Earth. In their greatness, they govern and order the cosmos, safeguard and stabilize the kalpas, secure the dynastic succession, and manifestly protect emperors. In their lesser aspects, they harmonize the Five Phases, regulate the Six *qi*, dispel evil and deliver from distress, benefiting beings and aiding humanity. Through cultivation, calamities may be dissolved; through recitation, auspiciousness may descend.

Your servants’ mother has entered a year of decline and distress, afflicted by illness and suffering. Our anxiety runs deep, yet we know not where to turn for supplication. Daring to rely upon the Perfected Sages, we lay bare our sincerest hearts. We humbly pray that the Three Treasures’ mighty spirits will command the attendants of the scripture bureau to resolve the conflicts of the Five Phases and avert the ominous decline of the Three Destinies. May emoluments be augmented in the Southern Heaven, may life be prolonged in the Director’s register. May the Six Palaces be regulated, all ailments healed. May we forever receive the covering protection of their grace and enjoy the blessings of long life.

Respectfully, at the Jade Bureau of Transformation, we recite scriptures and perform the ritual offering, secretly knocking upon the gates of the Perfected Ones.

---

**Memorial for the Life-Renewal Ritual Offering on the Jiazi Day for Vice Commissioner of Pacification Zhang Lin by Mo Ting**
Your servant has heard that the Dao of Heaven is impartial, aiding those who possess virtue. When merit extends to beings, blessings know no limit.

Vice Commissioner of Pacification for the Chuan Circuit, Zhang Lin, serves his lord without partiality, repays knowledge with utmost loyalty. His resolve remains unwavering from beginning to end, steadfast through wind and rain; his plans are manifold, growing ever more vigorous with the passing of seasons and the chill of winter.

At present, the four frontiers lie in turmoil, and the two garrisons stand embattled. The mobilization of arms has drained resources, while expenditures swell beyond measure. Heavy levies would surely plight the people, yet light taxes cannot meet the demands of supply. Through sagacious counsel, he has ensured the army’s provisions are abundant—grain piled high as mountains, weapons and armor massed like clouds. No man complains of toil, no matter is left unaddressed. Thus has he bolstered the might of our forces, poised to achieve the triumph of punitive justice.

Yet Vice Commissioner Zhang’s Three Life-spans still encounter misfortune; within his Two Cycles, the qi of his Jia-year fate and official salary wanes. The Celestial Talisman descends upon his Palace of Destiny, while Saturn retrogrades into his House of Sorrow. Fearing these portents of calamity, I have exhausted my sincerity in prayer, entrusting my plea to the imperial altar, and humbly beseech divine aid. May the Ten Flowers bestow blessings, may the Three Saints turn their radiance toward him. Let the gods of the heavens grant their benevolent gifts, that disasters naturally cease; let the Nine Bureaus absolve his transgressions, that his official salary and lifespan be extended. May he forever enjoy peace, and together with the realm, secure the frontier’s tranquility.

With utmost urgency and reverence, I dare not overstep, yet my devotion compels me.

---

**Prayer for the Ritual Offering by General Luo**
I humbly observe that the dual qi, pure and congealed, manifest the Dao of Heaven and Earth’s flourishing integrity; the Five Agents, interdependent, bear the grace of Qian and Kun’s nurturing power. As for the length of one’s life-record, the abundance of one’s official salary, the sins and fortunes of one’s conduct, and the auspices and misfortunes of one’s fate—none escape the oversight of the celestial bureaus or the influence of one’s primordial destiny. All is governed, examined, and recorded, great and small alike.

I privately fear that the constellations and Five Phases, in their celestial courses, may bring ill omens through their conjunctions; that the Nine Palaces and Three Life-spans, in their interplay of yin and yang, may coincide with perilous junctures. Thus do I tremble with apprehension, lest calamity take root.

Now, on this propitious day of the Beginning of Winter, I offer my prayers with utmost sincerity, meticulously performing the ritual offering. Gazing upward, I earnestly beseech; looking toward the earthly realms, I concentrate my mind. I await the descent of benevolence, the bestowal of boundless fortune. May misfortunes and disasters be eradicated, may transgressions and faults be absolved. Grant him auspicious omens, augment his lifespan and salary. Let his sins be stricken from the Northern Bureau’s ledgers, and his life-record inscribed in the Southern Prosperity’s registers. May his family, both seen and unseen, dwell in peace. May he soar upon the celestial paths, ever basking in the light of sun and moon; may he rest within the mortal realm, forever sheltered by the true spirits’ protection.

With reverence, I dare not presume further.

Humbly I have heard that the celestial patterns shift and turn, cycling through the Three Origins to complete the year; the transformations of yin and yang draw upon the Dao of Heaven to manifest their works. The blessings of moisture extend to both the seen and unseen realms, their principles constant across past and present. Those who magnify benevolence and uphold righteousness, who embody harmony and radiate concord, receive from Heaven auspicious omens, and the spirits manifest their felicitous favor. Yet if one’s conduct strays from vigilance and caution, if one’s will aligns with perversity and deceit, one treads the path of hardship and peril, foreshadowing obstruction and adversity. The principle of retribution—swift as echo follows sound—stands resplendently clear.

I, by contrast, am but a mediocre and unworthy man, long since burdened with official rank and emolument. Though I strive to maintain solemn reverence and advance with awe and sincerity, I constantly harbor the fear of being mocked as a snipe clashing with a clam, and ever dread the reproach of the greedy cormorant. Moreover, I am charged with disciplining the ranks of soldiers, dutifully guarding the frontier walls. Blades and arrows remain in use, the roll of drums has yet to cease. Crushing the strong and blunting the sharp, I merely execute the strategies of capture and suppression; yet in the course of battle, unintended killing and mistaken harm may give rise to grievances and hidden resentments. Such thoughts weigh heavily upon me, deeply occupying my mind.

Now, as the Autumn Emperor reviews merits and the Earth Official examines the registers, every transgression and blessing is raised, no detail—however minute—left unrecorded. If I have committed faults of presumption or negligence, errors of killing or wounding, offenses of the six emotions, or guilt of the three karmic actions; if there remain unresolved lawsuits or unredressed enmities—my deeds inscribed in the Black Ledgers, my name recorded in the Courts of Darkness—I beseech that a path of repentance and absolution be granted, and that the grace of remission and dissolution be bestowed. May I thus be enabled to exert myself and renew my conduct.

As for the baleful stars that cast their misfortune, the inauspicious years that bring calamity, I likewise pray for deliverance, that I may be preserved in peace and security. Above all, I entreat for my nine generations of ancestors, that they ascend to the Three Realms of Heaven. May they escape suffering and transcend the depths, fulfilling their nature and flourishing in life. May the weapons of war in the four directions be swiftly sheathed, and the myriad households soon return to the peace of plowing and weaving. May the common folk’s songs and chants resound, and the wilderness be stilled of dust and turmoil. May all return to the winds of purity and stillness, and the great Dao of the Inaudible and Invisible be universally realized.

With utmost reverence, I prepare the libation and offering, earnestly presenting this memorial. From afar, I invoke the immortal altar, gazing upward in hope of true protection.

I dare not presume further.

---

Memorial for the Life-Rite of Minister Ma

I, in my mediocrity and insignificance, have presumptuously received the favor of destiny, mistakenly occupying a position of rank and inheriting the honors of office. Commanding the war chariots, I carry out the statutes and decrees. At times, I succeed in pacifying towns and cities, sweeping away the treacherous and wicked. Externally, I repel invaders and foes; internally, I soothe the weary and afflicted. Yet when feasting guests and rewarding troops, the slaughter of livestock is unavoidable. In eradicating corruption and punishing evil, reliance upon penal laws is essential. Though my actions are not self-serving but aimed at securing the people’s peace, I privately fear that in the moments of sentencing and execution, errors in severity or leniency may occur; in the throes of killing and wounding, the line between intent and accident may blur. Such anxieties fill me with trepidation, lest I incur divine censure.

Moreover, I worry that in the cyclical years of my life, I may encounter inauspicious declines; that the five stars of my natal chart may be afflicted by baleful conjunctions. Should such calamitous alignments occur, I may yet fall into peril and danger. I further fear that my nine generations of ancestors, still dwelling in the shadows, have not been delivered; that my six relations, bound by lingering attachments, remain confined. Contemplating the long night of the underworld, my soul trembles; reflecting upon the gates of darkness, my heart quails.

Yearning to express my most earnest devotion, I lift my sincerest offerings in supplication. Relying upon the hour of my birth, I prepare the full measure of purifying incense. With mind attuned to the numinous transformation, I envision the distant sacred altar. I present the ritual offering with solemn reverence, and proffer this memorial in fervent prayer.

I humbly implore that the Primordial Origin bestow its protection, that the Great Dao extend its compassion. May the radiance illuminate the courts of the Yellow Springs, and decrees descend from the palaces of Fengdu. May the Nine Ancestral Spirits be delivered, and all sufferings dissolved. May they ascend to the Azure Heavens of the Living Spirits, and shed their forms in the Vermilion Caverns of the Immortals. May blessings extend to descendants, and grace embrace the clan.

For all past transgressions and endless grievances, may they all receive the cleansing of repentance and be restored to harmony. I beseech that my sins be stricken from the records, and my name inscribed in the registers of life. May disasters and misfortunes be quelled, and my allotted span of fortune and emolument be prolonged.

Furthermore, I pray that blessings flow to the rivers and springs, and that grace extend near and far. May weapons of war be swiftly laid down, and pestilence and disease vanish. May the fields return to plowing and mulberry cultivation, and the people attain wealth and longevity. Even unto the hidden and obscure beings of the deep, the distant and estranged realms of the vast, may all together bathe in the winds of the Mysterious, and ascend to the domains of the Dao.

I vow with utmost sincerity to forever uphold this boundless compassion.

I dare not presume further.

---

Memorial for the Rite at Mount Qingcheng

I humbly observe that as the vast qi gradually congeals, the myriad mountains rise in majestic splendor. Loftily supporting the celestial pole, they firmly stabilize the earthly realm.

Memorial for the Rite at Mount Qingcheng

In that southwestern realm, its heights reach the stars of Shen and Jing. Gathering numinous essence and amassing auspiciousness, it cradles the radiance of sun and moon; layered emerald peaks and piled mists enfold the abodes of immortals. Its rank surpasses all sacred peaks, its bounty second only to the Three Isles. As the felicitous court of all under heaven, it crowns the finest landscapes of the realm. Towering terraces stand in array, where the secret traces of the Yellow Emperor’s chariot yet remain; vast waters branch beside it, where the divine works of Great Yu may still be witnessed. Ever manifesting its responsive signs, it shelters the living.

Of late, rains have lingered beyond ten days, and springs surge forth in tumult. Though red cliffs and verdant ridges echo with tales of collapse, the vermilion halls and crimson pavilions remain untouched by calamity or alarm. Such manifold marvels further attest to its luminous power.

I, undeserving, have been laden with extraordinary favor, entrusted with this weighty charge. My governance has yet to bring peace, and my anxious devotion runs deep. I fear my own transgressions may have summoned these unusual portents from the immortal peaks; that encroaching misfortune may have drawn forth these warnings from the divine summits. Day and night, I examine myself, as though perched upon ice or embers. With no path to lay bare my heart, I can only offer the utmost sincerity in prayer and repentance.

Thus, in accordance with the sacred statutes, I reverently present this grand rite, humbly beseeching your gaze and protection, that my faults may be redeemed.

I dare not presume further.

---

Memorial for the Life-Span Rite by Minister Ma

I have heard that as the primordial transformation unfolds, the Three Powers draw upon its origin. Embodying heaven and earth, it forms all images; moved by its nurturing warmth, spirits coalesce. Hence, the register of life hangs at the Celestial Gate, and the threads of existence are tied to the Dipper’s pivot. Every action, great or small, every gesture, fine or subtle—none escapes the watchful gaze of the Eight Spirits, nor the exhaustive scrutiny of the Ten Rectifiers. Good deeds, though hidden, inscribe one’s name among the immortals; transgressions, once noted, consign one to the ledgers of the dead. Through such rewards and punishments, humanity is guided.

Above all, the Life-Span Deity presides over the recording and judgment of these accounts. Reflecting upon its profound decree, I am compelled to cultivate myself with earnestness.

I, unworthy and insignificant, possess no cunning strategy. I have only served with integrity, offering my life for the times. Yet my labors remain unfulfilled, and I am burdened by the weight of my inadequacy. Fear and humility grow within me, even as my responsibilities deepen.

Moreover, in the aftermath of war within the capital’s precincts and the abandonment of fields, the weary have not recovered, and wounds remain unhealed. To soothe them is like offering dew from my lips; to agitate them risks flooding the ditches. Yet I have been suddenly tasked with overseeing six districts, tending to the three labors of agriculture. Whether toiling in summer’s heat or winter’s cold, though human effort is strained, the harvest still depends on heaven’s timing.

Thus, I pour forth my sincerest devotion, gazing upward in prayer for divine aid. On this day of my life-span rite, I dare to reverently present this offering of repentance. May the true sages deign to look upon me, and may blessings gather abundantly. Pardon my presumption in holding office, and reward my earnest devotion. Let weapons be swiftly stilled, and granaries overflow. May the people be spared the suffering of pestilence, and the land freed from the dread of flood and drought.

May my nine generations of ancestors ascend beyond, and the Three Realms be cleansed of turmoil. Should the stars portend misfortune, or the years bring calamity; should unjust punishments or reckless rewards mar my rule, or unintended harm befall others—may all such faults be illuminated and forgiven, universally absolved. I vow eternal devotion, in gratitude for your true grace.

I dare not presume further.

A Memorial Prayer for the Benming Rite at Green City’s Mo Courtyard

I prostrate myself, reflecting: born of qi and shaped in form, I depend entirely upon the mysterious transformation of the Dao. My allotted span and destined emolument are ordained by the true courts on high. Yet I fear that in the course of my conduct I may incur faults and transgressions, or that within the cycle of years I may encounter misfortune and calamity. Without the power of the gods, repentance and purification cannot be achieved. Thus I presume to address the true mirror of heaven, reverently preparing the rites of offering.

This mountain is the supreme seat of the Five Peaks and the Four Waterways, a blessed land of immortals. Within its caverns stand jade towers and golden palaces, hidden from the profane world; below lie ancient halls and ruined terraces, their traces ever shifting. Beams collapse like broken rainbows, tiles scatter like paired mandarin ducks. Were no effort made to repair them, the paths would soon be overgrown with weeds.

I, unworthy, hold office here and have undertaken their restoration. Having completed the work, I now present its adornments: images of the Five Peaks and Nine Rivers are depicted, the true forms of the River Earl and the Stream Maidens rendered, their regal crowns solemn and majestic, pearls and jades arrayed in splendor. It is as though one ascends the shell-paved towers of the immortals, or draws near the jeweled palace of the dragon. The white walls now gleam with radiance, and the mysterious virtue of the gods is all the more revered.

May the celestial precincts of this lesser city forever rely upon such blessings. In autumn’s gratitude and spring’s prayers, may we ever receive their gracious favor.

On this day of my original destiny, I humbly prepare a feast of praise and invocation. I implore the gods to turn their chariots in response, to send down their divine grace. Bestow upon me the extension of my allotted span and emolument, and aid me in averting misfortune and calamity. May the kin of both realms enjoy peace, and the cattle and people of this land thrive in tranquility.

I vow to pour forth my sincerity, to repay your boundless compassion. I dare not presume further.

**Jiao Petition of Mo Tingyi on the Jia-Shen Day of His Original Destiny at Mount Qingcheng**

I have heard that the wondrous origin responds to its time, and the primordial essence initiates its course. The Three Luminaries divide their radiance, and the myriad beings are shaped in form. Between the round and pure above and the square and turbid below, they alternately serve as hosts and guests; within the realm of the sun and the paths of the stars, each fulfills its appointed office. In great matters, they govern kalpas and unfold the cosmic pattern; in small, they scrutinize the good and evil of human conduct. Their discernment surpasses the balance and mirror, and no blade’s edge or hair’s tip escapes their notice.

I humbly consider that the Nine-Chambered Grotto-Heaven is the assembly hall of the host of perfected beings, where cinnabar cliffs reflect the sun and emerald valleys yawn to the clouds. It is the place where phoenix banners come and go, and where rainbow standards gather. Though I have presumptuously received the charge of governing this land and have been permitted to approach these immortal mountains, I have consumed only coarse fare to discipline my heart and drunk icy waters to purify myself. Yet my merits have failed to compensate for my shortcomings, and my transgressions must surely be known. How, then, in this proximate presence, dare I deceive the gaze of the perfected immortals?

Moreover, I fear that as the Nine Celestial Bodies proceed in their courses and the Three Destinies shift, fortune and goodness may not endure, while calamity and misfortune remain unfathomable. With earnest and trembling sincerity, as if treading upon perilous ground, I now, on the day of my original destiny, renew the rites of prayer and jiao offering. To the celestial thoroughfares and earthly expanses, to the water palaces and stellar abodes, I present my utmost sincerity, lifting my gaze to implore luminous protection.

I humbly beseech that disasters be dissolved and transgressions absolved, that blessings be extended and auspices bestowed. May my span of life and emolument only increase, and may misfortune and peril naturally cease. For those departed, may the Nine Mysteries open the way to deliverance; for those living, may the two realms enjoy peace. May all beings within this domain together receive the shade of fortune. May the war chariots rest their steeds, and may the frontier regions know no anxiety. May I long rejoice in the era of tranquility and forever bear the grace of the numinous perfected.

I dare not presume further.

---

**Jiao Petition of Mo Tingyi to the Nine Luminaries**

I have observed that the Two Images divide their splendor, and the Three Origins array the luminaries. They govern the covenants of remorse and fortune, of good and ill, and hold sway over life and death, sin and blessing. Their dominion leaves nothing unmastered, and both the hidden and the manifest are bound to their decree.

I, though dull and common, have long revered the true and orthodox. Presumptuously bearing the favor of imperial insignia, I have been granted rank and emolument. Ever mindful of the bounds of my office, I have feared neglecting my duties; in caring for the people and pacifying the realm, I have not dared to forget self-discipline. Yet I still worry that my actions may stray from reverence and caution, that my daily faults and flaws may accumulate, offending the numinous spirits and covertly inviting adversity.

I further fear the advance and retreat of the Five Planets and the movements of the Four Luminaries. Should they reside in the palace of my life and destiny, or alight upon positions of weakness and ill fortune—this year, the Celestial Talisman descends upon my life trigram, while Jupiter has not yet emerged from my natal palace. Among the twenty-eight lunar mansions, the eclipse spirit traverses its path, and my minor destiny aligns with the Celestial Net. Privately, I fret that fortune may turn to calamity, and that my destiny may wane while my emolument dwindles.

According to the inner ranks of the *River Chart* and the secret texts of the *Grand Mystery*, I pour forth my earnest entreaty, laying bare my heart in full ritual observance. Gazing toward the resplendent gates of the Canopy of Flowers, I stand as if before the Nine Rays; beholding the palaces of the stars, the sun, and the moon, I empty my sincerity in crimson devotion.

I humbly implore that the radiance of the celestial throne may descend to illuminate the dark and murky, dispelling obscurity; that the divine light may extend its brilliance, shattering the chariot of misfortune and burning away the net of sin. May my years be preserved, and my rank and office ascend. May the people of this domain enjoy health and peace, and may the kin of both realms know safety and prosperity. May the immortal mountains bestow their favor, and may no pestilence harm the people; may the numinous precincts grant their auspices, and may the year bring the hope of abundant harvests.

With pure and earnest sincerity, I seek to repay the profound merit of the Dao.

I dare not presume further.

---

**Jiao Petition of Lord of the River to the Northern Emperor**

I have observed that the Seven Governors hold supreme authority, and the Five Numinous Elders preside in mystery. Their positions command the Northern Culmen, and their jurisdiction extends over the central heavens. From the fortunes and misfortunes of earthly regions to the calamities and blessings of celestial patterns, from the Five Phases and Six Qi to the Three Destinies and Nine Palaces, the weal and woe of all things are subject to their scrutiny and judgment.

For years, warfare has raged, and the people have suffered devastation. The pain of their plight pierces my flesh and bones. Thus, I dare to present this jiao offering, pouring forth my prayers in full devotion. With earnest sincerity, I knock upon the gates of the Purple Tenuity and lay bare my heart before the celestial patterns. Truly, I hope for compassionate regard and the descent of auspicious blessings. May the noxious qi be dispelled from the plains and fields, and may the baleful stars retreat from the asterisms of the well and net.

May this riverine land know peace and prosperity, and may all things flourish anew. May the weapons of war be sheathed forever, and may my allotted span be renewed. May the mists of the Nine Heavens part, revealing once more the light of the sun and moon; may the smoke over the Three Shu clear, and may the blessings of clouds and thunder be bestowed anew.

I now reverently bear the Emperor’s mercy and protection.

I dare not presume further.

---

**Jiao Petition of Lord of the River to the Empress of the Zhou, Earthly Deities, and All Gods**

I have observed that this is a renowned precinct of the celestial domain, a sacred tract of the lesser city. It is a blessed land of dragon spirits, a mighty bulwark of the Celestial Emperor.

Though I am but a humble and insignificant being, I have been entrusted with the governance of this land, and by some misfortune, I have been charged with the stewardship of this domain. For ten years now, I have lived in daily trepidation. Yet from the moment I first assumed this duty, I was met with hardship. The Yellow Turbans rose against Qin, and the imperial carriage fled to Shu, where the wandering court of ten thousand souls remained for five years. Exhausting all strength to uphold the heavens, my devotion to the realm ran deep, and my efforts in restoring order bore fruit. Even upon the imperial return, rebellion flared—Shi Li raised arms, and Gan Neng seized the moment. Xiu Sheng amassed forces at the lower rapids, while Guo Qi rallied in the heart of the army. The imperial carriage stood but a short distance away, yet the shock of battle shook its wheels. By the sagacious might of the throne and the borrowed power of the gods, these threats were quelled in succession, securing the great chariot’s safety. Moved by such divine aid, I have ever held this gratitude in my heart.

Now, however, the times remain unsettled, and men give free rein to chaos. The Emperor’s Chariot moves once more toward Chen Cang. The Central Plains burn with the fires of war, and the Six Directions know no peace. Though my heart aches with concern for the realm and my resolve to aid the sovereign is unshaken, I cannot offer the loyalty of Ji Shao, for mountains and rivers divide us; nor can I shed the tears of Yuan An, for I have no means to attend the imperial guard. In distant reverence of the gods’ power, I trust they will grant their saving grace. Thus, I present this jiao offering, humbly beseeching divine communion. May the grace of aiding the right prevail, and may the celestial pace be steadied; may the force that curbs excess be lent, and may the roots of evil be swept far away. May the imperial carriage return to the capital above, and may the precious mandate endure for ten thousand generations. With libations of peppered wine, I forever repay this radiant mercy.

I dare not presume further in my earnest entreaty, laying bare my heart in utmost devotion.

---

**Jiao Petition to Mount Ge the Transformed**

This immortal mountain stands as a pillar of the earth. Its eighty-one grottoes divide the sun and moon within the land; its twenty-four peaks weave mist and rosy clouds at heaven’s edge. It silently governs the balance of sin and fortune, overseeing all living beings. From my earliest days, I have revered the mysteries of the Dao and long cherished purity and stillness. In this era of sagely rule, I have been honored with a role in its flourishing; in dreams, I have wandered the sacred peaks, ever holding the aspiration for freedom. Yet worldly affairs have weighed heavily upon me, stifling my true longings. Now, as the season turns to mid-autumn and the rites of the full moon approach, I gaze afar at the emerald peaks, distant beyond the red dust. With reverence, I prepare the jiao altar to offer my sincere prayers. May the tiger banners and dragon pennants depart from the palaces of the Eight Extremes; may the crane-drawn and swan-borne chariots descend, if only briefly, from the carriages of the Three Immortals. Accepting this modest offering, bestow upon us extraordinary blessings: let the harvests be bountiful, let calamities cease, let the unseen and the seen alike share in fortune, and let both household and state know peace. May the imperial destiny rise like a lofty ridge, and may the years of Tang endure beyond the cycles of kalpas. I vow to maintain purity and devotion in service of the divine radiance.

I dare not presume further.

---

**Jiao Petition to the Nine Stars of the River Lord**

I have heard that the Nine Origins govern the pole, arraying the constellations within the Purple Tenuity; the Seven Governors shed their light, guiding the host of stars along the Yellow Way. They point to the Celestial Handle to oversee all phenomena and turn the Big Dipper to rule the hundred spirits. Life and death, fortune and misfortune—all are subject to their governance. At the time of my birth, in this very month, Mars and the dark stars of the Dipper’s handle converged upon my fate. Trembling with dread, I fear the onset of disaster. With crimson sincerity, I humbly beseech their divine protection. Reverently, I conduct this great jiao, pouring forth the depths of my heart. May the Nine Sages extend their compassion, descending in the Emperor’s Chariot to grant blessings; may the Seven Perfected bestow their favor, turning the Dipper’s handle to dispel calamity. May the movements of the Twenty-Eight Lodges bring forth auspicious fortune, and may the divisions of the Twelve Palaces forever still their troubles. I pledge my loyal and steadfast heart in gratitude for the divine beings’ regard.

I dare not presume further.

---

**Jiao Petition for the Harmony of the Zhou Heavens**

Though I am unworthy and base, I have been burdened with great responsibility. Elevated to the heights of the imperial terrace and stationed in the lofty bastion of the frontier, I have poured forth my heart like one who holds the sun in devotion, yet I have achieved no merit in aiding the sovereign. Of late, the four frontiers bristle with ramparts, and the Central Kingdom knows no peace. Warhorses gallop unceasingly, and chariots remain harnessed. Some among the inner court have turned traitor, while distant lords have betrayed their grace. No sooner was the nest of the owl destroyed and the imperial carriage returned than news of punitive campaigns arose, compelling another imperial progress. As a subject, how can I not burn with indignation? In silent meditation, I burn incense and yearn for the blessings left by the sagely ancestors; in prostration, I present petitions and await the aid of the unseen hosts. Indeed, the false king and his vile ministers were beheaded in succession; the treacherous general Zhu Zhi met his end in swift succession. In distant reflection of this hidden support, my sincerity deepens. Recently, the Great Unity has traversed the heavens, its light now shining upon Shu’s domain. The Five Planets shift their courses, some entering the palace of my fate. Fearing that my meager virtue has invited misfortune, I dread the onset of further calamities. Ever vigilant, I dare not rest in complacency.

Thus arose Zheng Junxiong and Han Qiu, who conspired across two lands and swiftly raised arms. They severed all bonds of grace and trust, violating the defenses we had heard of. They ravaged the living, burned commanderies and towns, leaving several provinces in ashes and a thousand li scarred. Moved by this hidden grievance, my pain cuts to the bone. Therefore, I ascended to beseech the Supreme Dao and openly prayed to the true spirits—not for my own sake or my household, but with a heart that ever grieves for state and people. Thereupon, Heaven repented its calamity, and the Great Dao bestowed its numen. Those who harbored treachery were soon eradicated; their adherents, all swept away. The frontiers grew still again, and the ravaged lands began to heal. Han Qiu perished in defeat, and Junxiong was beheaded like an owl. Roads gradually reopened, and long-buried wrongs neared redress.

Yet in this season of reaping, the slain were not few. Gazing upward, I recall the decree of cherishing life—how can I rest easy in such sorrow? Looking down, I mourn the souls wandering Mount Tai, their desolation unending. Thus, I compose my spirit, knock in stillness, bow in reverence, and turn my heart homeward. I perform rites of gratitude and repentance, pouring out my earnest prayers to Earth and Heaven. May the Mystic Sages, in their boundless grace, look kindly upon my sincerity. May their radiance illumine the sacred altar, their vast blessings flow forth, washing away transgressions and quelling disasters. May the living enjoy peace, and the hidden paths open to prosperity.

I have further heard that all stars bow to the Pole, and the hundred grains pay homage to their source. Yet these rebels, defiant of court and Heaven’s Dao, still fester near our borders, stretching across several provinces. Their mountain strongholds stand in sight, long havens for the wicked. Like swarming bees or gathering ants, they rally with hoes and staves. For twenty years, they have spurned the enlightened transformation. Seizing the moment when the waters brim over, I shall break them like bamboo. For the state, I shall punish the treacherous; for the people, I shall remove their scourge. I humbly implore divine power to amplify our martial might.

The Underworld commands thirty thousand troops, ever dispelling pestilent qi; the Grotto Springs host twenty-five generals who suppress the usurping fiends. The true Dao smites the perverse, and the gods aid the righteous. Embracing this decree, I once more pour forth my red heart. I prostrate myself, trusting that Your August Brilliance will deign to heed my petition and turn back to grant Your luminous protection.

May the lands of Chang, Lu, and Zi flourish, forever free from the scourge of serpents and boars. May the grasses, trees, and thickets all transform into the forms of blades and spears. Let all know the power of imperial might, and let the people’s songs once more extol the king. Thereafter, we shall reward the turtle-walled city, present our memorial at the phoenix towers, sheathe our bows, and unarmor our troops, returning horses to pasture and oxen to rest. May the harmony of fish and water endure, and the Dao of ruler and minister flow unimpeded. With utmost sincerity and blood-deep earnestness, may the great Dao bear witness. Unable to contain my reverent plea for grace, I prostrate myself in trembling devotion.

*Here ends Volume Ten of the* **Guangcheng Collection**
*Volume Eleven of the* **Guangcheng Collection**
*Composed by Du Guangting, Grand Master of Imperial Edicts, Purple-Robed Master of the Inner Offerings at the Supreme Clarity Palace in the Upper Capital*
*Memorial for the Water Bureau: Prayer for the Repair of the Weir*

I have heard that the great Dao bestows its works, shaping and perfecting all things. The true spirits establish their stations, governing all living beings. As for the luminous deities of the water bureaus and the rightful overseers of mountains and forests, each administers reward and punishment to shelter the multitudes. This county commands the upper reaches, long renowned as a bustling prefecture. Its tax burdens are heavy, and its farming and planting abundant. The weirs it guards are tied to its safety and peril.

The weir I oversee lies along those rushing currents. Since the floods began, it has repeatedly collapsed. Though we labor day and night, exhausting our strength and hearts, repairs are swiftly undone, and collapses soon follow. Is this the natural course of the water’s veins, beyond all prevention? Or is it the work of dragon spirits, resisting all obstruction? Anxious and desperate, I have nowhere to turn for aid.

Moreover, food is the sky of the people, and the people are the foundation of the state. Should the autumn harvest falter, famine will surely follow. This fertile land of the celestial storehouse borders the lower rapids, while the households of the lesser city adjoin its flowing waters. If inundation strikes, the silt and sand will shift. To save those drowning in these waters, we must rely on divine power.

I humbly implore the great Dao to extend its grace, the radiant spirits to cast their gaze, pitying the farmlands and considering the lives of the people. Turn your unfathomable divine work and lend your impartial sagely power. Bestow your aid and protection, that we may attain safety. Let millet and grain flourish forever, and the granaries of the capital overflow with hope. Avert the calamity of rising waters and submerged hills, and align this year with an era of abundance and prosperity. With offerings of duckweed and pondgrass, I dare not betray your divine favor.

*Memorial for the Five Talismanic Stones of the River Lord*

The Three Treasures radiate their light, and the Five Scripts nurture transformation. They condense the qi of water, fire, wood, and metal, forming the writings of clouds, mist, dragons, and phoenixes. They safeguard the cosmos and stabilize heaven and earth. Since their descent to the mortal realm, they have protected and aided all living beings. Yu the Great used them to achieve success, and Confucius revered them in song. No household or state fails to honor and practice them.

Thus, they are employed to subdue spirits and deities, pacify mountains and rivers, dispel pestilent qi, and purify palaces and cities. Even the construction of dwellings falls within their purview of warding and pacification. Recently, within my jurisdiction, I oversaw the building of a new residence. Having completed this great task, I now conduct a grand offering. Following the standards of the *River Chart* and the rites of the *Numinous Treasure*, I have inscribed the true talismans and maintained the sacred incense and fire.

I hope thereby to dissolve transgressions, summon the proper spirits, and invoke the divine officials to grant eternal protection. I humbly beseech the Primordial One to witness and bless, and the host of sages to extend their compassion. Command your offices to bestow their auspicious favor. May my dwelling and kin know peace and health.
