This place lies near the celestial region of the Great Fire, and my own palace of destiny may face its influence. With trepidation, I examine my heart and find myself shaken and fearful. Thus, I gaze upon the mountain of fortune in my life’s destiny and look up to the transformations of the immortals. Through the Three Primes, I offer prayers, and to the Nine Luminaries, I present my devout pleas.

I humbly implore the divine perfected of the grotto heavens, the attendants of the incense halls, and the august sages of the Dark Heaven to descend with their blessings. Grant me your resplendent favor and talismanic signs, and dissolve the disasters and calamities that mark my fate. May I receive your protection and truly attain peace and well-being.

Above, I pray for the imperial enterprise to match the heavens, the sagely plan to stabilize the mountains, the Yi and Luo rivers to herald a revival of the realm, and the eight waters and three mountains to harmonize with radiant prosperity. May weapons be sheathed across the nine wilds, and may all under heaven share a common culture and governance. May I be inspired to steadfast loyalty, forever supporting the wise and sagely ruler. Unable to contain my devotion, I prostrate myself.

A Memorial Prayer by the King of Shu for the Lunar Eclipse in His Life Palace at the Jade Bureau’s Ritual of Transformation

I have heard that the great Dao, in its boundless numinosity, initiates transformation through primordial harmony. It illumines the Three Luminaries in the heavens above and governs the six qi in the midst of the sky. Dispensing the power of nurturing and fostering all things, none fail to flourish; wielding the handle of cold and heat, warmth and coolness, no governance is unequal. Thus do the Five Planets bear the talismans of the Great Emperor, adjudging merit and fault; the Ten Spirits execute the decrees of the Great Unity, presiding over fortune and misfortune. The celestial stems and earthly branches admit no deception, for they are the foundation of all ages.

I, your servant, have encountered this sagely era and, though unworthy, am dusted with singular honor. My mountains and rivers command the might of the Well and Net constellations; my lands hold the weight of the earth’s cardinal corners. Yet I constantly fear that my fortune may exceed its measure, and truly dread the entanglement of calamity.

Now my virtue remains unrefined, and the Great Vault of Heaven issues its warning. At the new moon, the sun suffers partial eclipse in the region of opposition; at the full moon, the moon undergoes waning in the position of my Life Palace. The Flying Celestial Mars descends upon my fateful hour; the stem of my official rank and the tone of my natal sound both encounter the qi of decline. I fear that misfortune may take form, and my anxiety deepens.

Therefore, I follow the mysterious statutes, rousing my sincerity to utmost devotion. I offer fragrant oblations at the Jade Bureau and array the ritual of the libation altar. Gazing toward the Three Radiant Ones, I beseech their grace; praying across the entire heavens, I invoke blessings.

I humbly implore that your luminous presence deign to look upon me, that your divine resonance bestow favor. Grant auspicious signs to my Three Lives and Five Phases, and dissolve the calamities portended in the celestial field of my Life Palace. Any past injuries, accidental killings, karmic debts, or long-standing grievances—may all be absolved and forever rendered pure and fortunate.

Above, I pray that the imperial enterprise endure, that the sagely lifespan be prolonged. May the prosperity of Qin and the glory of the Great Han be restored, and may the dwelling at Luoyang rival the splendor of the ancestral Zhou. May weapons be laid down, and both Chinese and barbarians revive in harmony. May I pour forth my heart in service to the state and truly align with the protection of Heaven.

Unable to contain my fervent devotion, I prostrate myself in utmost reverence. Respectfully submitted.

**Prayer for the Pacification of a Dwelling**

I have heard that the qi of the Dao flows and spreads, giving rise to the division of the Three Powers. Yin and yang unfold the mechanisms of transformation, while water and wood initiate the images of mutual generation. The winds of nests and caves have now given way to the construction of dwellings. Thus, we cultivate the harmonious qi of the two forces and embody the Five Phases in our regulations. Truly, we rely upon the transformations of the spirits to shelter all living beings.

I, in my mediocrity and ignorance, fail to comprehend the profound principles. Following the times, I have undertaken renovations and, within my limited capacity, initiated construction. In the labor of earth and timber, I have observed no taboos; in the cutting and digging, I have caused great disturbance. Perhaps I have encroached upon the royal directions or violated the Dao of Heaven. As a result, the dragon spirits have not guarded their posts, and the dwelling is ill-suited. I fear that misfortune and decline press near, prolonging calamities and hardships.

With utmost sincerity, I turn my heart to the Great Dao, bow my head to the Three Honored Ones, and, following the luminous precepts of the *Lingbao*, perform the Grand Offering of the Five Emperors. Reverently, I confess and repent, prostrating to invoke the talismanic writ. I repent for past transgressions and offenses, praying for the blessings of future peace and tranquility.

I humbly beseech the Two Modes to bestow auspicious signs and the Five Emperors to grant good fortune. May all evil and misfortune be dispelled, and the dragon spirits firmly guard their posts. May the household enjoy purity and prosperity, and all movements be met with health and peace. May enterprises flourish and livelihoods thrive, ever receiving beneficial protection. May public and private affairs flow smoothly, and all kin and dependents live in safety.

Thus, I shall forever bear the grace of the Most High and the multitudes of honored ones, as well as the protection of the Five Emperors.

---

**Prayer for the Eight Seasonal Offerings**

I have heard that the Great Dao bestows its transformations, and the primordial qi shapes all forms. It forges the multitudes of beings, giving rise to distinctions of purity and turbidity, firmness and softness. It unfolds the eight seasonal nodes, fixing the directions of spring, autumn, winter, and summer. Thus, it examines and judges fortune and misfortune, overseeing the clarity of transgressions and blessings. Its benevolence extends throughout the state and the household, and its grace encompasses both the living and the dead.

We, your servants, have been fortunate to live in this flourishing era and have long revered the transformations of the Dao. We rely upon the power of the spirits for our nurturance and depend upon the sagely might for our cultivation. Yet, we fear that in dwelling among the common folk and establishing ourselves in the world, we may not be without faults. In past lives and the present existence, we must have accumulated flaws. Perhaps within the Five Phases and Three Lives, we have encountered inauspicious conjunctions; or beneath the dark and luminous stars, we have been subject to their influences. In such trepidation, we have resolved to seek solace through offerings.

Now, as we encounter this propitious season, we unite in utmost sincerity. This is the time when Heaven’s origin inaugurates the cycle, the day when the Great Sage extends his compassion. We lift our hearts to the numinous transformations, bow our heads at the jade altar, and, with pure incense and flowers, reverently present our offerings and prayers.

I humbly beseech the Most Exalted to witness and protect us, and the multitudes of sages to take pity. May they extend boundless compassion and bestow limitless blessings. May the sins and afflictions of past lives, the grievances of successive generations, past transgressions, and future misfortunes—through the power of renewal at the eight seasonal nodes and the grace of amnesty from the Three Palaces—all be swept away and forever granted purity and good fortune.

May we, your servants, along with our ninefold ancestors and sevenfold kin, receive blessings in the Southern Palace; and may our kin and relatives be freed from the records of death in the Northern Bureau. May public and private affairs harmonize, and may our lifespans and fortunes be long and distant.

Thus, we shall forever bear the grace of the multitudes of sages and their protection.

Memorial for the Grand Zhou Heavenly Rite of Offering

We humbly acknowledge that the Great Dao is all-pervading and harmonious, wherein all talents shine forth. As yin and yang rise and fall, the principles of good and ill fortune are thereby distinguished; as good and evil circulate in cycles, the texts of sin and blessing are thus revealed. The Jade Void Great Emperor and the Golden Portal Primordial Sovereign command the perfected spirits, bidding them to govern all. The Three Officials and Five Emperors preside over the bureaus of reward and reproof; the Southern Dipper and Northern Origin oversee the registers of life and death. Their mighty statutes are fully established, unerring through countless kalpas.

Thus, the cinnabar tablets and mysterious scriptures contain the secret arts of cultivation and expiation; the rites of praying to Heaven and repenting transgressions hold the luminous statutes of confession and purification. Gazing upward in reverence of their vast compassion, we dare to present our humble petition.

Your servant, having been favored by fate’s conjunction and born in an era of flourishing fortune, has—despite my common and unworthy nature—been graced with extraordinary favor. Reflecting upon my sojourn in this world, dwelling in purity while treading the turbid, serving my lord and honoring my parents, governing my household and correcting the realm, I have striven to uphold loyalty and integrity, laboring diligently in public service. Yet blessings have been elusive, while transgressions and errors readily accumulate.

Moreover, of late, while attending upon the imperial retinue, I have encountered times of hardship and sorrow. Rapacious rebels defied Heaven, and dark clouds obscured the sun. Auspicious vapors gathered only to shield the imperial chariot upon the layered crags, while demonic dust enshrouded the avenues of the capital in gloom. It was a moment when loyalty and righteousness demanded action, when a minister’s duty called for the offering of his life. Thus, I was able to grasp the Pivot of Heaven with my hands and stand firm against the leviathan’s waves, securing the imperial throne and exhausting my sincerest devotion. Thereupon, I was undeservedly granted exceptional favor and suddenly entrusted with weighty and perilous responsibilities—commanding encampments of valiant warriors across a thousand *li* of frontier lands. Ashamed of my lack of supervisory and pacifying abilities, I can only express my earnest trepidation.

I fear that in past lives, this present existence, and through countless kalpas, I have failed to attain true rectitude, thereby accruing manifold transgressions. Perhaps I have offended Heaven’s principles above, violated Earth’s propriety below, clashed with human sentiments in between, or contravened the nature of things around me. Tenfold entanglements accumulate externally, while the three karmic actions arise within. At times, I have aided the rightful and eradicated treachery, punishing the wicked to assist the mandate; at others, I have caused harm—whether intentional or accidental—while upholding the law and maintaining order. Or perhaps the movements of celestial bodies have brought adverse influences, or the cycles of the three destinies have coincided with decline and peril. The eight trigrams and nine palaces bear the numbers of punishment and obstruction; karmic debts and litigations contain the texts of interrogation and retribution. These hidden and obscure matters are subtle and difficult to fathom.

Only through devoted observance may I ascend to knock upon the mysteries of the void, hoping to attain spiritual resonance and receive the protection of the sages. Therefore, in accordance with the true methods of the *He Xun* and the sacred statutes of the *Zheng Zhou*, I offer sincerity as vast as seas and mountains, pouring forth earnest supplication throughout Heaven and Earth. With reverence, I present this rite of offering to express my solemn devotion.

We implore the Three Luminaries to turn their radiance upon us and the multitudes of sages to cast their gaze in mercy. May they absolve our past transgressions and bestow extraordinary blessings. May our sins be expunged and our names inscribed in the registers of life. May karmic debts be reconciled and calamities swept away. May our ninefold ancestors and sevenfold kin alike be bathed in boundless grace; may our sixfold affines and ninefold relations all be nurtured by mysterious compassion.

May the riverine borders be tranquil and the people’s dwellings harmonious. May customs be free of pestilence, and the countryside resound with songs of joy. May the dark bureaus and nether courts be illuminated by divine splendor, and may all flying and crawling creatures receive the blessings of nourishment and moisture.

Above all, we pray that the nation’s path be smooth and level, the sagely body at ease and flourishing. May the five weapons be sheathed, and may all living beings enjoy peace and well-being. May the imperial carriage swiftly return to the capital of Qin, and may the symbols of governance once more be displayed at the gates of Wei. Gazing at Heaven and longing for the sun, our words arise as our hearts hasten forth. We cannot fully express our devotion.

**Joint Memorial for the Life-Renewing Jiao Ritual**

We humbly submit: The Great Dao sheds its radiance, and the Three Spirits bestow their origins. Heaven and humanity establish their stations, while the myriad transformations divide their courses. Endowed with qi, some are pure, others turbid; granted fate, some meet fortune, others misfortune. Once darkness and light are distinguished, sin and blessing become manifest.

Thus, the Most High extends boundless compassion, and the Primordial Honored One shows mercy and protection. In the southern palace, the Repository of Extended Life is opened; in the northern capital, the statutes of merit and goodness are arrayed. The Two Leaps array their stars, shining impartially to illuminate all; the Three Officials and Five Emperors unfold vast pardon and rule with sovereignty. Their intent is that all may together bathe in non-action and attain purity and stillness, that beings may ascend to the fruits of the Dao and their names be inscribed on the ranks of the Perfected.

We, your servants, have presumptuously been blessed by divine power and fortunately encountered this flourishing era. We have heard the wondrous teachings of the Mystic Scholars and trod the broad path of benevolence and righteousness. Seated, we draw from the goblet of Yao; in motion, we sing of sagely virtue. Reflecting on ourselves, we are deeply moved with reverence and joy.

Yet we fear that in past kalpas and this present life, our conduct and bearing have often transgressed, frequently offending the unseen and the manifest. The defilements of the six senses are hard to dispel; the transgressions of the three karmic actions are not easily accumulated. On the ledgers of Wenchang, our good names remain unrecorded; in the halls of Fengdu, our sins are already marked. Moreover, we dread that in our current years, calamities may strike, and baleful stars may descend. Perhaps in constructing earth and wood, we have violated taboos; or in accidental harm or mistaken killing, we have bound ourselves to grievances and enmities. Thus, our years are silently stolen, and our blessings and fortune subtly diminished. Without the aid of this sacred assembly, our profound sincerity would be difficult to express.

Now, as white dew congeals in the morning and the clear autumn arrives in season, this is the day for repenting sins and praying to the Perfected, the time for extending grace and invoking blessings. We therefore lead those who share our devotion to take refuge in the Supreme Dao. Bearing ritual offerings, we bow our heads before the numinous altar, baring our hearts to the celestial palaces and fixing our thoughts upon the stellar abodes.

We humbly implore the Three Primes and the Upper Saints, the hosts of the Ten Realms, the mighty deities of the Southern Culmen, and the attendants of the Northern Terrace: in consideration of our earnest devotion, descend with your luminous presence. Bestow blessings upon the living and the dead, and quell misfortune and calamity forever. May we, your servants, and our nine generations of ancestors and seven lineages all ascend to heaven; may our five clans and six relations together enjoy peace and safety. May our sins be eradicated, our fortunes and longevity extended, our households serene, and our endeavors harmoniously fulfilled. May the five phases and three destinies forever be free from harm and conflict; may our private chambers and public halls long bear the blessings of prosperity and integrity. We cannot fully express our devotion.

**Zhang Daoheng’s Vow to the Northern Dipper**

We humbly acknowledge that the celestial patterns descend as foreknowledge, illuminating all things without exception; the Emperor’s Chariot revolves in its course, and no supplication fails to reach its mark. Though I am but lowly and obscure, I have been graciously favored with your divine regard. In the second year of the Great Shun era, I fell into dire peril, my very life hanging in the balance. I poured forth my sincerest devotion, beseeching the mysterious workings of the Dao. Thereupon I made a solemn vow, pledging one hundred thousand strings of cash. Soon after, I regained peace and was granted absolution. Though my life as a mere ant has been preserved, the grace of the true spirits remains unrequited. Since then, pressed by urgent travels and toiling north and south, I have seldom encountered a fitting occasion to repay this debt. The weight of ice and fire in my heart has left me sleepless and fearful.

Now, turning my heart toward the numinous transformation, I bow my head before the jade altar. With reverence, I prepare incense and lamps, meticulously performing the rites of offering. From the fourth month of this year until the present, I have five times presented the pledged sum, fulfilling the one hundred thousand strings. Moreover, at the Jade Bureau’s Hall of the Northern Emperor, I have commissioned the sculpting of eight statues of the Northern Dipper Perfected Lords, thereby expressing my long-held devotion and repaying the profound grace of the Dao. May the sagely compassion deign to accept this offering, so that the vows of old may be fulfilled on this day. May past sins be erased, lingering misfortunes swept away, enmities reconciled, and years of prosperity extended. May public and private affairs align with auspicious harmony, and may my kin enjoy the blessings of peace. May the living and the dead alike know tranquility, and may all beings partake in this grace.

---

**Prayer for the Military Marshal’s Household Altar**

We have heard that the Great Dao fuses with the true, and the Heavenly Worthy expounds its teachings. In the era of Red Clarity, the *Lingbao* revealed its charts. The eight assemblies formed its scriptures, congealing beyond the vastness of the firmament; the five talismans traced their traces, proclaiming the great abundance within. The Five Emperors received them to deliver humanity, and the Nine Heavens obtained them to establish order. Bestowed upon the earth below, they protect the state and succor the people, subduing malevolent spirits and eradicating evil. All undertakings are permitted to proceed in accordance with their decree.

Recently, as the construction of my dwelling nears completion, I fear that transgressions may have been committed, difficult to examine in full. Following the mysterious statutes, I humbly request the issuance of talismanic commands. I have reverently prepared the Yellow Register, submitting a memorial to the Pure Capital. I have inscribed the texts of the Five Directional Great Emperors, adhering to the Three Caverns’ rites of suppression and exorcism. Below, I notify the spirits of the five lands; above, I memorialize the Nine Subtleties. May the host of sages bestow their compassion, and may the myriad spirits grant their protection. May the talismanic officials be commanded to proclaim their duties, descending with their numinous power to spread their true *qi*. May demonic forces be purged, and dragon spirits pacified. May the Eight Trigrams and Nine Palaces, the Five Phases and Six Jia, the forces of yin and yang, the punishments and slayings, and the Generals of the Grand Year each guard their respective directions, forever dispelling calamity.

May any lingering corpses, residual *qi*, metal-and-earth demons, stagnant specters, wandering souls, hidden spirits, and obscure shades—each by the power of virtue—be allowed to depart freely. May this dwelling be preserved in peace, forever blessed with good fortune.

**Petition for the Three Assembly Offerings**

We humbly recall that human life is endowed by the two *qi*—yin and yang establish the body, while the hun and po guard the self. Should the slightest disharmony arise, misfortune and adversity follow. The days of the Three Assemblies mark the time when the three hun ascend to present their reckoning. Sin and blessing, fortune and calamity—no detail escapes notice. Lifespans are lengthened or cut short, rewards and punishments meted out with perfect clarity. Thus, one must accumulate virtue, and if not, at least perform meritorious deeds to redress transgressions, praying for auspicious responses to secure long life. The profound sages’ admonitions and the true scriptures’ teachings—how dare we not heed them to discipline body and mind?

For several years, on the days of the Lower Assembly, we have jointly conducted offerings and prayers, exhausting our devotions in reverent practice. Yet recently, entangled in worldly affairs, we inadvertently let the propitious festival pass. Our hearts trembled with unease, and we dared not rest at ease. Now, we have selected another auspicious day, invited virtuous companions, and together prepared incense and fire to hold this special offering. In the stillness of the cold night, we concentrate our minds and direct our thoughts, trusting that the true numina will descend and our sincere prayers will reach them.

May the myriad sages turn their radiance toward us, and may the thousand perfected ones reflect our devotion. Grant our supplications, dispel calamities and misfortune. Restrain the po and bind the hun, fulfilling each aspiration for cultivation. Transform ill fortune into good, opening the path to longevity. Some among us suffer from the decline of the Three Life-Spans or the stagnation of the Nine Palaces. Some endure the baleful influence of celestial omens or the entanglement of inauspicious fate. Some bear unresolved karmic debts or lingering afflictions. Some carry the weight of past injuries, accidental killings, or deep-seated transgressions. We beseech that all be purged, that we be granted luminous protection. May our households be blessed, and may our nine generations ascend to heaven. May public and private affairs flourish with harmony, and may our kin enjoy the blessings of peace.

**The Emperor’s Petition for the Southern Dipper Offering**

We humbly observe that the Three Luminaries adorn the heavens, illuminating all existence. The host of stars hangs as celestial signs, governing all forms. The Southern Dipper and Wen-chang oversee the register of life, serving as the foundation of the yang’s nurturing warmth and the arbiter of the emperor’s destiny. According to the *Heavenly Origin* and *Supreme Clarity* scriptures, on the fifth day of the fifth month, when the day of *bing-wu* arrives, blessings are bestowed, mercy extended, lives aided, and all beings benefited. All things are harmonized, and the state and its people are pacified. The yang’s power is thereby sustained, and its blessings universally bestowed.

This year, the four stars of Fire, Water, Metal, and Earth converge in the domain of *Shichen*. Moreover, the sun’s course aligns favorably, and all are in proper submission. At the new moon of the fifth month, the sun was to be eclipsed yet remained whole. By the full moon, the moon was to wane yet suffered no loss. Thus, this fifth day coincides with *bing-wu*, a moment of pure yang. Though we are unworthy and dull, we reverently receive this profound grace. Ashamed that our governance remains incomplete and our influence not yet universal, we dare to hope that this flow of kindness may extend even to our humble selves. May the Great Dao extend its compassion, and may Heaven grant its protection.

May the Nine Provinces and Four Seas enjoy peace and the people thrive. May the years be bountiful, the Six *Qi* balanced, the seasons regular, and the Four Times harmonious. May bows be sheathed and warhorses retired, oxen released from labor. May all attain the blessings of preserved life, and may the virtue of cherishing life be widely cultivated. With sincere devotion, we bow before the numinous altar. Gazing upon the Eight Luminaries, we lower ourselves in reverence, hoping the Nine Radiant Ones will shine afar. Witness this offering of wine and prayer, and grant us auspicious blessings.

The morning’s brilliance manifests the numina’s power, and the unseen aid of the spirits is already evident. As heaven and humanity resonate, the fulfillment of this covenant may be expected. We await the great unity of civilization and the harmony of the realm. With utmost reverence, we receive and uphold this profound compassion.

**The Emperor’s Petition for the Circumpolar Offering**

I have heard that when wind, rain, frost, and snow arrive unseasonably, the stars and constellations display their portents; when pondweed and water-plants may be offered, Heaven and Earth bestow their blessings. Looking back to the ancients, this is indeed a universal principle. I, your humble servant, reverently ascend the great throne and devoutly uphold the grand design. I dare not rest at ease, as though standing upon ice or treading a valley, ever shifting; the seven changes of the jade pitch-pipes weigh upon me, for I fear the common people are not yet at peace. Should even one thing be out of place—whether through misguided governance, misapplied punishments, or unfulfilled benevolence and trust—then weapons may yet linger on the borders, and the calendar not yet unified between Hua and Yi. Flood and drought remain unregulated, and prosperity eludes us. Famine, plague, and pestilence continue to afflict the prefectures and counties; bandits and deceivers still run rampant in the villages. Though I have practiced frugality, encouraged sharing, reduced my meals, and curtailed expenditures; though I have kept far from music and sensual pleasures, forever forsaking the hunt; though I dare not forget self-discipline amid humble vessels of clay and shell, nor seek amusement in pheasant-feather ornaments or tiger-amber trinkets—still, I fear the celestial bureaus may yet record my faults. My ignorance and shame weigh heavily, and I have no means to offer repentance.

Recently, the Metal and Fire stars, along with the Water and Earth luminaries, have all gathered in the region of Shu, converging in the domain of *Shichen*. The sun and moon have entered their eclipses, and even the historians of the new moons have set down their brushes. The sun’s path has shifted, and the astrological divisions have shown their favor. Yet how can these auspicious signs all be mere coincidence? Thus, I redouble my resolve for self-cultivation and deepen my vigilance. Seizing this auspicious noon-day hour, I humbly respond to the profound grace of the Supreme Mystery.

The numinous officials are distant, the Purple Palace most solemn. Though I have made my declarations in full, I fear my sincerity and clarity may not reach them. With fasting and purification, I have chosen this day to present my earnest words. The silent altar stands in solemn dignity, its rituals observed beneath the cold light of the second watch; the ethereal immortals and sages descend, bestowing blessings upon the mortal realm. I prostrate myself in hope that the Eight Directions may be at peace, the common people secure and prosperous, the state fortified, and the altars of soil and grain eternally tranquil. May the Six Treasuries be well-ordered, the Nine Virtues duly fulfilled. May officials in caps and robes faithfully serve, and the written script unite all under heaven.

*Petition at the Offering on Mount Anle in Luzhou*
I reflect that Chu and Shu share a border, a land of great importance in the southwest. The river surges with myriad currents, and mist gathers upon a thousand peaks. The Celestial Emperor gathers his glory here, and dragon spirits guard its bounds. This sacred land alone commands such renown. Its triple-tiered incense smoke mingles with the moonlight, and its eight caves conceal the abodes of transcendent immortals. Ever does it bestow victory and aid upon the people. Free from the harms of drought and flood, its customs preserve the auspiciousness of peace and integrity. Thus, the waters flow smoothly for those who sail upstream, and hemp and silk flourish abundantly. Revering the majesty of the Three Observances, I receive the gracious favor of the Two Perfected. This is proclaimed far and wide, recorded in scriptures and diagrams. With heads raised and hearts fixed, all sing of the profound bounty.

I, your servant, am bound to the imperial chariot, yet my gaze longs for the forests and springs. Often do I pity the white leopards and black apes that play among the mushroom rocks; the cassia peaks stretch before me, and though my steps are earthbound, my spirit wanders. Thus, I offer this modest incense and present my solitary plea. At the Northern Emperor’s Abbey, where I reside, the ritual implements for offerings are incomplete. Though the rites for invoking blessings have been performed, the music of soaring frost remains wanting. I have heard that within these immortal mountains, sacred instruments abound. Yet without a set time for their testing, their resplendent tones remain obscured. The Dao responds to sincerity, and bells may indeed be moved. I humbly wish to reduce what is in excess to supply what is lacking. Taking from the verdant peaks, I would transfer them to the imperial capital. May their pure sounds gradually rise through the vermilion clouds, and their mighty resonance be heard within the Purple Forbidden precincts. I pray that my sincere prayers be granted, that these treasures may forever guard the capital.

**Prayer for the Efficacy of the Sacred Mountains’ Spirits**

Composed by Du Guangting, Grand Master of the Interior for Sacred Offerings, Bestowed with Purple Robes, at the Supreme Clarity Palace in the Upper Capital

We humbly observe: the Great Dao fuses essence, giving rise to the Two Modes. The Primal Honored One spreads transformation, sowing the seeds of the myriad spirits. All receive the mandate of governance, together securing peace for the state and its lands. Revered are the host of numinous presences, who indeed gather blessings and felicity.

Since the founding of the dynasty—heaven’s will aligned with the people’s—this realm was established. Though it has not yet attained the perfection of grand peace, it has fortunately become a land of abundance. The four quarters have submitted, and the hundred lords are assembled. The hearts of the people are steadfast, and heaven’s intent is manifest.

Yet at times, instruction strays from righteous principle, and affection binds to partiality. Great responsibilities of prosperity and splendor are entrusted, and the weighty authority of oversight and nurture is conferred. The base and the eminent alike grow wanton, indulging their whims, forgetting filial piety and reverence. They employ the seductions of treachery, stirring the ferocity of rebellion. Arrows and stones threaten the imperial carriage, and the drums of war resound near the attendants.

Still, we rely on the grace of High Heaven and the descent of numinous transformation. The hearts of owls and jackals were not tolerated; the fumes of wolves and jackals were swiftly extinguished. Before day could turn to dusk, all was swept away. Within and without, peace was restored, and the seas and lands rejoiced.

Thus, an auspicious day was chosen to repay the majesty of the spirits. From afar, we offer our sincerity in proclamation, exhausting the purest of oblations. We dare to hope for their discernment and protection, that lasting peace and stability may prevail.

**Prayer for the Water Spirit at the Unmooring of the Fleet by Zong An, Attendant Censor of Zhenjiang**

We humbly observe: the transformative power of the Dao extends everywhere, and the blessings of the spirits universally reach. Above, they embrace the state and its lands; below, they extend to the bonds of humanity.

We all rely upon the salvific protection of the spirits, silently borrowing their sustaining power. From ancient times to the present, never has this failed—both waters and lands enjoy tranquility.

I, though possessed of but ordinary talent, have fortunately encountered this sagely era. In the great work of statecraft, I have no merit worthy of bamboo and silk; yet through profound grace, I have been repeatedly favored by the creation of Heaven and Earth. Suddenly, I received the sovereign’s commendation and was publicly entrusted with the military tally—ascending Han Xin’s altar of purification, receiving Lü Hou’s golden axe. The sacred grass was bestowed to mark my command, and the chariot’s hub was pushed forth for my expedition. Though I tremble with awe at this responsibility, I dare not decline the trust placed in me. Choosing an auspicious day, I received my orders and set forth.

Moreover, the Chu Gorge lies upstream, the Jin River rushes downstream. A thousand vessels follow in the imperial wake, while ten thousand currents surge forward in competition. The emperor, ever mindful of the true numen, is deeply concerned by these hidden perils. His imperial heart is ever devoted to reverence, seeking to spread transformation and harmonize neighboring lands, while also extending counsel to embrace distant realms. This mighty host of keen warriors embarks first upon this journey. As we prepare to cast off and ride the current, we purify our sincerity and offer this sacrifice.

We humbly invoke the Great Sage of the Primordial Dao, the Five Venerable Elders, the divine commanders of the mysterious offices—may they bestow vast blessings and mighty fortune. May swift waves ensure safe crossing, and turbulent rapids transform into tranquil flows. May the myriad leagues of waterways be opened, and the hundred spirits grant their protection. May the great enterprise flourish, and the grand foundations be further broadened. May the central court be shielded from without, and all together attain auspicious fortune.

**Prayer for the Life-Span Sacrifice by Zhou Xiang, Acting Official**

We have heard that Heaven’s scrutiny is most discerning, responding to all that is felt. The spirit-way is upright and just, with no prayer left unanswered. Ever does it extend its salvific benevolence, fulfilling the wishes of those who supplicate. Disasters are dispelled, and blessings flow forth like echo answering sound. I hold these words in reverence, ever maintaining a humble and devout heart. Whenever my fate has allowed, I have prepared offerings and performed rites, striving to deepen my sincerity and truly receiving bright protection.

Yet I fear that worldly affairs remain unsettled, and transgressions easily accumulate. Bound by the constraints of official duty, regrets and faults are hard to escape. As the stars cast their light upon me, this year’s fate is marked by decline and peril. I dread the entanglement of calamity and dare not hope for fortune’s favor. Since joining the military in neighboring provinces and patrolling distant frontiers, I have twice encamped in war chariots through the cycles of the heavens. Lacking the proper rites of memorial and petition, I must have incurred the fault of negligence. I had intended to wait for our triumphant return to perform the rain sacrifice and offer thanks. But now, as we are still engaged in fortifying our ramparts and have not yet sheathed our bows, the incense and lamps have long been neglected, and no place of peace has been reached. Thus, I hasten my heart toward the numinous realm, distantly knocking upon the gates of the Most True. I prepare the offerings for the threefold sacrifice, presenting them together at a single altar.

We humbly beseech the Mystic Sage to look down upon our sincere devotion. May calamities be dissolved and disasters dispelled, life extended and fate preserved. May past stains be cleansed and former faults erased, that we may witness the completion of our success and forever attain abundant fortune.

**Prayer for the Life-Span Sacrifice to Lord Ge’s Transformed Spirit**

We humbly observe: the two qi derive their numen, and the Five Phases bear their forms. The law of the vaulted heavens determines fate, while the substance of the vast earth shapes all beings. Sin and fortune, good and ill—all arise from hidden judgments. In the workings of the heart and the path of conduct, all is governed by their decree.

Moreover, burdened with exceptional honor and long entrusted with weighty responsibilities, we reflect upon our limits and station, ever filled with trepidation and shame. Whenever we approach the altar of memorials and sacrifices, how dare we forget the rites of reverence and awe? Through our devout offerings, we aspire to repay the grace of sovereign and kin.

Now, as the day of the Primordial Lady arrives, we come before the sacred northern precinct of our life-destiny, kindling incense and flame to beseech the True Immortals. May they look upon our sincere devotion and bestow boundless fortune. May our transgressions be purged and our years prolonged, our dwelling secure and our people at peace. May no calamity or pestilence assail the four borders, and may agriculture and sericulture flourish in abundant harvests. Thus shall we pour forth the loyalty of sunflowers turning to the sun, forever upholding the era of Great Peace.

With utmost reverence and devotion, we submit this prayer.

**First Memorial for the Transformation of the Ten Thousand Immortals**

We humbly observe: this is the famed region of Nine Ridges, where the traces of the Three Immortals’ transformations abide. Above, it connects with the Heart Mansion of the heavens; below, it guards the Brocade River. Clouds and mist weave radiant brocade, while pines and cassia stand tall amid the hues of mist and haze. The Five Palaces rise in lofty splendor, their forms evoking the rites of the Western Numinous and Southern Culmen; the Four Auxiliaries shine in mutual brilliance, arrayed as the Eastern Florescence and Northern Perfected. Most eminent in scenic grandeur, it alone commands the marvels of seclusion. Slanting against the jade wheel of the moon, it overlooks the stone ravine.

Yet of late, as master and disciples stirred in turmoil, the clash of gongs and drums resounded, comets streaked across the sky, and frost-tipped spears gleamed over the fields. Warriors who moved like bears and cranes did not return; recluses who rinsed in streams and rested on stones departed in indignation. Gazing upon these once-exalted wonders, we find them now overgrown and desolate. The gilded towers’ splendor is dulled by dust, and the grand halls’ adornments are marred by moss. Reflecting on this ruin, we can but sigh in lament.

Moreover, as this day of our life-destiny aligns with this site of transformation, it is fitting to renew our vows and repay the True Spirits. Thus, we have commanded the Daoist of the Three Caverns, Tang Dongqing, to fell timber and gather artisans, to measure the stars and select an auspicious day. With the Wind and Winnowing Baskets in alignment for the task, and the propitious hour of *jiazi* at hand, we reverently announce our intent to the Perfected and solemnly perform the Great Sacrifice.

We humbly pray that the True Spirits will look upon our earnest devotion and grant us felicitous omens, that no calamities may intrude, and that our endeavors swiftly come to fruition. May we restore the legacy of the sages of old and establish a model for the kalpas to come. May our merit resound through the Grotto-Heavens and be inscribed upon the cloud-vales.

Thus do we wish that the True Spirits will extend their divine protection, that the riverlands be tranquil, crops abundant, and pestilence dispelled. May we receive the elixir of the Nine Auxiliaries and hear the profound principles of the Double Mystery. Ever shall we turn our hearts toward the Pole Star, aspiring to fulfill the blessings of the Supreme Perfected.

With utmost sincerity, we submit this prayer.

**Memorial for the Sacrifice to Lord Ge’s Transformed Spirit, Presented by the Minister of Works on Behalf of the King**

We humbly observe: the sacred mountains of Supreme Purity are the site of Lord Ge’s numinous transformation. A marvel of the riverlands, they are a court of fortune for all under heaven. Jade caverns yawn to shelter clouds, and jasper peaks rise to obscure the sun. At dawn, iridescent mists disperse; at night, divine torches take flight. Stalactites gleam in secluded grottoes, and springs murmur over deep treasures. The radiance of the Nine Wells manifests its own numen; the vital stirrings of the Three Perfected ever abide. The Cranes’ Observatory stands at the center, while the Constellation of the Responding Dragon shines above. Crimson halls and azure eaves stretch in succession, their ancient forms still visible. The halls of Xiao and the steles of Wei stand in ordered array, their ancient traces preserved.

Ever do these wonders proclaim their auspicious signs, extending even to the isles of the immortals.

The minister, by virtue of his appointment as the envoy to the Prince of Shu on the occasion of His Highness’s natal day, has been entrusted with this transformative mission. Only recently have the bonds of governance been secured, and already the realm stands complete. Towering pavilions and storied terraces snatch the morning radiance from sheer cliffs, while wind-swept casements and cloud-kissed beams lend marvel to the sacred groves. The cavern-heaven has been opened anew to shelter the brocade-clad capital. Within its forty prefectures, the granaries overflow with each year’s abundance; across its five thousand *li* of mountains and rivers, the people thrive in prosperity. All have received the bounty—who does not know the grace bestowed? The minister, humbly shaped by this molding influence, has indeed been deeply touched by the workings of creation. In reverent prayer and gratitude, he has prepared this offering of incense and libation, beseeching the power of the Dao.

May the Nine Heavens grant their favor, may the host of sages look down in witness, and may the radiance of their presence illumine the sincerity below, bestowing vast blessings. May the Three Rivers mirror the expanse of peace, may the eight lands be cleansed of dust. May harvests flourish and disasters dissolve like mist. May the divine elixir be conveyed to ensure long years, and may the merit of serving the sagely court perpetually exalt the great treasure. May the altars of state be twice secured, and may the realm forever enjoy felicity. The minister, unable to contain his fervent prayers and yearning for grace, prostrates himself in utmost devotion.

With respect, this petition is humbly submitted.

---

*Ran Chuchou’s Prayer of Return to the Northern Dipper*

Prostrate, I reflect: the celestial symbols of the Supreme Mystery shine upon the earth below. The Emperor’s Chariot turns in its course, the Dipper’s handle directs its sway. Sin and fortune, good and ill—all are governed by this sovereign will. We, your servants, having received our charge, journeyed far upon the Way. We traversed hardships, scaled perilous heights, and faced every trial. Yet with each step, we held fast to our sincere devotion, silently entreating the mysterious perfected ones. By grace, we were granted the favor of your protection and attained the blessing of peace. Overwhelmed by this divine benevolence, our hearts burn to repay it. Thus, on this appointed day, we have prepared the rites of incense and prayer, kindling fragrant offerings to fulfill our vow and bow in gratitude for your boundless grace.

We humbly beseech the exalted immortals to accept our modest tribute. May calamities be dispelled and misfortunes swept away. May rank be elevated and years prolonged. May our comings and goings be smooth, our public and private affairs auspicious. May no path be obstructed, and may our families dwell in safety. May we ever bask in the light of sun and moon, and faithfully serve our radiant and sagely lord. We cannot express the fullness of our devotion.

---

*Prayer of Thanksgiving for the Completion of the Purple Radiance Grotto*

Prostrate, I reflect: the Great Dao is formless and silent, yet the immortals manifest its wondrous transformations. They reveal its boundless efficacy and bestow its unfathomable mysterious power. In secret, they aid emperors and kings, and unseen, they uphold states and nations. From ancient times to the present, the records shine with their glory. Thus did Emperor Yao wander to Guye, the Yellow Emperor ascend Juci, King Mu of Zhou sail the Jasper Waters, and the Han Emperor visit Mount Kun. All gazed upon mist and clouds, beheld ice and snow, and thereby secured long reigns, brought order and peace, achieved great prosperity, and rightfully manifested the protection of the Dao.

Yet I, of meager virtue, have dared to undertake this grand endeavor. How could I presume to neglect reverence before the Golden Gates and Jade Capitals? How could I fail to hold in awe the Nine Pures and Three Realms? Thus, I have ever maintained a heart of utmost sincerity.

In the second year of Yongping, the ren-shen year, on the twenty-first day of the seventh month, ding-mao, a prophetic text bestowed by the Most High Lord Lao was obtained in Shifang County of Hanzhou. Jade scriptures were left in the immortal’s abode, and bronze talismans were engraved upon the fertile earth. Birth dates, life mandates, times, days, and names were recorded, tracing the unbroken succession of generations and clarifying the prolonged blessing of Heaven’s mandate.

On the twenty-fourth day of the eighth month in the fourth year, wu-zi, Wang Chengshang, Military Commissioner of Lizhou, memorialized that the numinous grotto of this mountain had revealed the presence of divine immortals. Thereupon, he commanded Ren Keyan, Master of Ceremonies, and Yang Zhishu, a high-ranking official, to present a formal report of gratitude, reverently responding to the radiant numen.

On the first day of the tenth month, jia-zi, as the jiao altar was first opened, auspicious manifestations were again witnessed. Cloud banners and feathered screens appeared amid the jagged cliffs, while crane-like immortals with divine bearing arrayed themselves within the grotto’s entrance. These events surpassed those of Huishan and Yaoshui, and their splendor exceeded that of Guye and Juci. Overwhelmed by such auspicious omens, we were filled with awe.

Thus, after consulting the classical rites, we have specially undertaken this act of enfeoffment and veneration. On the jia-shen day of this month, Daochang Mountain was renamed Xuandu Mountain, Yangmo Grotto was renamed Zixia Grotto, and Jinggu County was renamed Jinxian County. The spirit of Xuandu Mountain was enfeoffed as Duke of Jade Purity. We established an altar and renovated the temple halls, from the initial planning to the completion of the work. Repeated sightings of true forms further manifested the numinous favor.

We respectfully dispatch Du Guangting, Grand Master for Glorious Happiness, Left Remonstrance Gentleman, Master of Broad Accomplishment, and Duke of Cai, along with twelve others, bearing ritual gifts of silk, incense, and flowers, to perform the Golden Register Daoist rites in accordance with the Mysterious Canon at the Zixia Immortal Abbey. As this occasion coincides with the Lower Prime Festival, a most solemn observance, we duly present this offering of gratitude and again display the honors of enfeoffment.

We humbly beseech the assembled sages, perfected ones, immortal officials, and celestial administrators of the grotto-heavens to witness our sincere devotion and bestow upon us their mysterious blessings. May the nine lands be governed in peace, and the ten thousand regions united in harmony. May the heavens and earth, the palaces of the living and the courts of the dead, ever extend their benevolent grace. May the mandate of our dynasty endure for generations, and may we perpetually enjoy the fortune of prolonged prosperity. We bow our heads and present this reverent petition.

---

**Memorial for the Life-Destiny Jiao of Lord Zong Kui of Yangzhou**

We have heard that all forms and natures derive their existence from the Great Dao, and all lives and destinies are bestowed by the Supreme Mystery. We receive the compassion of Heaven and Earth’s sheltering embrace and share in the power of qi’s transforming and nurturing force. Through diligent cultivation and reverent devotion, we honor the true numina.

Reflecting upon myself, a mere speck of dust, I have repeatedly received the imperial grace. I have served within the palace as a counselor and without as a guardian of the frontier. Yet I have rendered no droplet of merit, and my heart is ever filled with the fear of overreaching.

Now, within the celestial cycles and the palace of my destiny, dark stars are in conjunction, and Mars stands in opposition. Fearing the convergence of misfortune, I have nowhere else to turn for prayer. We recall that the Most High has transmitted texts, and the Primordial August One established teachings. The Orthodox Unity tradition prescribes rites of expiation, and the River Chart outlines the procedures for jiao offerings. If we exhaust our sincerity and diligence, we shall surely receive manifest protection.

Therefore, on the day of my life-destiny, I dare to perform the Nine Luminaries Jiao, purifying my heart and returning to the Mysterious Ultimate. We humbly beseech the assembled perfected ones and great sages to look down upon our bright sincerity. Cleanse our transgressions, dissolve our karmic debts, dispel calamities, and prolong our years. Increase our emoluments in the Southern Palace and remove misfortune from the Northern Mansion. By purifying our hearts and restraining our conduct, we may repay the grace of the true sages above; by serving the state with loyalty, we may forever requite the virtue of sovereign and parents. I am unworthy.

---

**Memorial for the Life-Destiny Jiao**

We have heard that the virtue of Heaven and Earth prioritizes life, and the grace of creation and nurturance is rooted in fortune. I have been favored with good fortune and have enjoyed a flourishing era. I have received the compassion of the Three Luminaries’ illumination and the beneficence of the sagely sovereign’s exalted favor. My service in the provinces has been met with honor, and my career has been marked by distinction.

Yet I ever fear that fortune may turn to calamity and remain vigilant in preserving my prosperity through restraint. My apprehension deepens, and I dare not rest at ease. Now, within the celestial cycles and the palace of my destiny, Mars stands in opposition, and dark stars are in conjunction. Gazing upon the celestial signs, I contemplate in silence—how may I offer thanks? Reflecting upon my humble existence, I strive to cultivate my resolve, yet my anxiety only grows.

Thus, on the day of my life-destiny, I have prepared the River Chart Jiao rites, reverently presenting my sincere devotion in the hope of receiving the mysterious compassion. We humbly pray that my disasters and misfortunes be dispelled, my inauspicious influences eradicated. May my years be prolonged, my emoluments increased. May I fully express my reverent devotion and forever repay the protection of the Most True.

---

**Memorial of Gratitude and Fulfillment of Vows by the Lady of Yueguo on Behalf of Military Commissioner Lord Zong Kan**

We have heard that the Perfect Dao mysteriously pervades all, responding to circumstances and answering prayers. Though our cinnabar hearts reside in the mortal realm, the mysterious perception of the Upper Clarity is ever moved.

**Memorial of Gratitude and Fulfillment of Vows by the Lady of Yueguo on Behalf of Military Commissioner Lord Zong Kan**

The echo responds without partiality, the shadow follows without obstruction. My husband, Wang Zongkan, and our son, Chengzhao, led troops last year to suppress rebellion, serving the state and the throne. Besieged in a lone city, they endured for months on end. Smoke signals flared with urgency, yet word from them remained scarce. My spirit raced toward Baomian, my gaze stretched toward the mountains and rivers—endless anxiety, no path for prayer. Thus, I reverently approached the Daoist temple to present a memorial, solemnly arranging the ritual platform to invoke the celestial hosts. Through the resonance of the true spirits, protection was granted. Soon, the fortified walls were breached, the ferocious rebels crushed. The mission of pacification was accomplished, fulfilling the sagely reward. Kin reunited, the army returned in triumph. Though victory stemmed from sagacious strategy, divine aid played its part. Now, on this auspicious day, I offer thanks for the mysterious blessings. Renewing the rites of memorial and jiao, I present my fragrant gratitude. With utmost sincerity, I bow and light incense, invoking the true chariots of the thirty-six palaces and beseeching the great rites of the eighty-one excellences. May auspicious radiance descend upon the altar, may boundless favor forever bestow fortune upon our land. May the sagely chart endure, may our clan flourish. I vow to uphold my reverent devotion, ever repaying the warmth of the numinous true. Overwhelmed by gratitude for this sacred grace, I cannot express the depth of my reverence.

---

**Memorial for the Rite of Disaster Dispelling by Attendant-in-Ordinary Mao Xun**

We have heard that the qi of the Dao flows forth, its mysterious power forging all things. The Three Spirits bestow endowment, heaven and earth hold sway over covering and bearing. The five planets govern the cycles of cold and heat, the turning of seasons. Thus, all lives and destinies are bound to the celestial gates. Fortune follows goodness, calamity follows excess—all shaped by divine transformation. It is fitting to devote oneself to reverence and uphold the numinous blessings. From my earliest years, I have been blessed by sagely favor, showered with extraordinary grace. From the northern court to the southern palace, I have repeatedly been honored with appointments; draped in crimson and purple, I have reached the height of splendor. Yet I have always striven to repay the state with loyalty and to discipline myself with caution. Still, I fear that the reckoning of yin and yang may align with misfortune, that baleful stars may cast their light upon me. Construction may disturb the dragon spirits, or my conduct may falter in reverence. My heart, unexpressed in prayer and repentance, is ever filled with trepidation. Now, as my life-destiny faces its cyclical turn, celestial omens descend upon the northeast. The great cycle resides in *xu*, the *kuigang* prevails. The earth star lies hidden in my life palace, its opposing light casting upon the *chou* position. Fearing the onset of disaster, my alarm only deepens. We have heard that the Southern Mansion of Wenchang governs life and merit, while the Northern Palace of the Dipper corrects transgressions. Fortune and misfortune are measured without error, retribution mirrors reflection. The true teachings open the path of repentance, where sincerity finds response; the mysterious scriptures prescribe the rites of gratitude, where prayers are answered. Thus, on this auspicious day, I humbly prepare the jiao offering, baring my cinnabar sincerity in hope of moving the true perception. I pray that my disasters and obstructions be dissolved, my misfortunes purged, my calamities pacified, my transgressions eradicated. May my emoluments and years be increased, may blessings and fortune be bestowed. I vow to uphold loyalty and filial piety, repaying the grace of sovereign and parents. Forever inscribed in my heart, I rely solely upon the mysterious compassion. Overwhelmed by the need to repent, pray, and beseech, I cannot express the depth of my reverence.

---

**Memorial of Fulfillment of Vows to the Nine Heavens True Lord of Mount Lu by Zhang Chongyin**

We reflect upon the majestic region of Zhenyi, where Mount Lu’s true traces reside. Its rank surpasses the Five Peaks, its domain commands the Nine Rivers. Jade towers and golden cities encompass the hidden abodes of immortals; Lu Peak’s cloud canopy shelters the lofty capital of the true saints. Amidst its verdant stillness, it rises above the vast waves. Each time I have gazed upon it in prayer, it has bestowed fortune and blessing. In recent years, exiled by imperial decree, I drifted like a lone leaf upon the waters. Passing through this sacred realm, my heart prayed to the true lords above, hoping for their merciful aid, offering libations of peppered wine. My sincerity moved them, and signs of response appeared. Yet soon, the path was blocked by weapons, waves startled the ships. My solitary sail was cut off, and I spoke of returning by another route. My unfulfilled devotion remained, the mysterious protection unrequited. Now, as sagely grace is proclaimed and I rest in the Shu capital, I seek the Daoist temple to fulfill my long-held vow. I present the jiao offering, reverently conveying my bright sincerity. We have heard that where there is sincerity, there is response—the Dao is omnipresent. Though the feathered banners may be distant, are ten thousand *li* truly far? Though the chariots of judgment descend, are the Three Rivers too remote? Receiving this cinnabar sincerity, may vast blessings be bestowed. May my former vows be fulfilled, may extraordinary grace extend afar. I pray that my sins be absolved, my disasters forever erased. May I aid in the governance of Yao and Yu, may I enjoy the longevity of two heads and six bodies. May I devote myself to loyalty and filial piety, serving sovereign and parents. I vow to cultivate reverence and devotion, relying upon the power of the Dao. Overwhelmed, I cannot express the depth of my reverence.

---

**Memorial to the Southern Dipper and Northern Dipper by Zhang Chongyin**

We have heard that the Three Spirits established their positions, and the myriad forms received their shapes. Embracing the perfect harmony of yin and yang, they contain the true essence of heaven and earth. Thus, talents and destinies are bestowed, each with its office. They govern life and death, their gates and barriers distinct. Even the most minute matters are recorded, nothing escapes scrutiny. I humbly consider my past and present lives, spanning countless kalpas. Transgressions accumulate, sins manifest. My conduct may not align with the divine, my actions may lack reverence. Now, as celestial signs cast their light, my life-destiny faces misfortune. Disasters arise, yet I know not how to avert them. Today, I bow before the jade transformation, reverently facing the jasper altar. Having chosen an auspicious day, I solemnly present the jiao rites. I pray that the Six Saints of the Southern Palace bestow a new name upon my life, that the Seven Perfected of the Northern Dipper erase my name from the register of death. May the Three Officials absolve my sins, may the Five Emperors dispel my disasters. May past vows be fulfilled in these sacred mountains, may blessings descend from the sagely grace. Furthermore, as I receive the imperial decree and prepare to journey to the court, I face the perils of rivers and mountains, the dangers of land and water. I rely entirely upon your bright protection, humbly offering my profound sincerity.

Having reached the imperial domain and been granted supreme fortune, how dare I forget my devotions to repay the true spirits?

I, Wang Zongkui of Hanzhou, humbly submit this *jiao* prayer for the pacification of my dwelling.

I have heard that when the Great Primal divided, the Three Spirits established their positions. The customs of cave-dwelling gave way to the construction of halls and houses; since the rise of high antiquity, sages have instituted teachings in accord with the times. Thus they shielded against cold, heat, dryness, and dampness, prepared for wind and rain, and regulated the cycles of darkness and light. As the forms of things multiplied, so too did the scope of their analogies expand. They ordered them by Qian and Kun, Zhen and Dui, embodied them in the five tones—*zheng*, *yu*, *gong*, and *shang*—and propelled the interplay of yin and yang, wielding punishment and virtue. The stems *yi*, *xin*, *geng*, and *gui* were arrayed in their respective offices; the branches *zi*, *wu*, *chou*, and *yin* were distributed among their governing spirits. At the boundaries of the Six Spirits and Four Killers, dragon and tiger forces clash; in the domains of Five Yellows and Nine Purples, auspicious signs converge. The Dao encompasses all in its embrace, and the reckoning of merit follows the stars and sun. Thus we examine fortune and misfortune, and indeed, clear evidence emerges. Magpies follow the Grand Year to aid in evading the General; how much more, then, should we revere the most numinous and never forget caution?

Recently, finding my dwelling crude and unsuitable, I chose an auspicious day to rebuild. I sought the great and sturdy, rejecting excess and extravagance. I emulated the ancient ways of thatching and rammed earth, heeding the admonitions of mountain-carved beams and algae-adorned pillars. Now the plastering is complete, and the construction finished. Yet I fear that in the raising of baskets and shovels, I may have violated taboos; in the course of labor, I may have offended the spirits. Perhaps I have transgressed the suitability of the Five Surnames or neglected the essentials of the Two Dwellings. Maybe I have damaged the earth’s veins, pierced hills and plains, defiled auspicious spirits, or suppressed inauspicious sites—thus inviting disaster without having confessed my faults.

Therefore, I have carefully studied the mysterious classics and redoubled my sincerity. Reverently performing the great *jiao* rites, I humbly invoke the True Writs, open the *Lingbao* Red Scriptures, and follow the talismanic commands of the *Dongxuan*. I dispel malign forces and pacify the dragon spirits. I seek forgiveness for past transgressions, beseeching the removal of calamities and the bestowal of blessings. I pray that the Three Honored Ones deign to witness, that the Five Emperors cast their radiance, that the Eight Assembled Mighties be commanded, and that the Three Primordial Officers and their subordinates safeguard my dwelling and purify its environs. May they absolve the sins of the past and grant future purity and fortune. May I truly receive their protection and ever enjoy peace.

Within this dwelling, the local earth gods and former occupants—whether ancient or recent, of diverse surnames—are also included in this *jiao* altar’s offerings. May they partake of this sincere rite, each preserving their tranquility. Ascend to the courts of blessing and bring no harm. May my entire household receive grace, my nine clans share in prosperity. May I ever incline my heart toward loyalty and filial piety, upholding the virtue of ruler and kin.

I, Ma Shimu, humbly submit this *jiao* prayer for the Soil Star.

I reflect that when the primordial *qi* divided its splendor, the Three Luminaries shone forth, illuminating all beings and governing the myriad regions. They follow the Yellow Path with constancy, adorning the vault of heaven without disorder. In great matters, they govern the cycles of heaven and earth, the rise and fall of states, the alternation of fortune and misfortune, the balance of safety and peril. In lesser matters, they oversee human morality, the fortunes of years, the length of destinies, and all such affairs, which are subject to their dominion.

Within my body’s palace, the Soil Star’s radiance has passed. In my natal constellation, the Dark Void has traversed. Both major and minor transits have encountered clashes and obstructions. In the domain of my fate, the Celestial Talisman has taken residence. Disasters and dangers have piled upon one another; illness and misfortune have clung like chains. Though I have consulted the three physicians, my long-standing ailments remain unrelieved. I fear these are the consequences of sins accumulated over lifetimes, weaving this web of misfortune; past transgressions have led to these present obstructions. Perhaps in my duties, rewards and punishments were unclear. Since establishing myself, errors and faults have amassed. The spirits have meted out their reproach, and my years and fate have been troubled.

Day and night, I have been consumed by worry, wishing to offer prayers and seek absolution. Thus, I have studied the astrological texts and examined the ritual codes. Reverently approaching the sacred altar, I earnestly perform the *jiao* rites. Gazing toward the Central Quarter, I pour forth my sincerity; beholding the celestial images, I direct my thoughts. Bowing, I burn incense and lay bare my repentance. I pray that the hosts of sages in the Mysterious Bureau bestow their great compassion, that the Most High Dao and the exalted ones descend their life-sustaining grace.

May sins and transgressions be absolved, disasters and misfortunes dissolved; may enmities be reconciled, and calamitous retributions leveled. May the hundred meridians flow freely, the six *qi* harmonize and regulate. May illnesses and sufferings be healed, and blessings and auspiciousness converge. May life be prolonged under the Southern Dipper, and death averted from the Northern Palace. With reverence, I receive the benevolent protection of the Dao, and dare not betray the gracious favor of the true spirits.

*Guangcheng Ji*, Scroll Twelve—Concluded
Composed by Du Guangting, Grand Master of Imperial Edicts and Bestower of the Purple Robe, Inner Offering Attendant of the Great Pure Palace
*Zhou Tian Ci* for the Birthday of Vice Commissioner of Pacification Zhang

I have heard that the Dao divides into the One *qi*, while humanity corresponds to the Three Spirits. Good and evil arise from the sincerest depths, and fortune and misfortune respond to the Mysterious Ultimate. If one cultivates noble aspirations, they shall surely align with extraordinary omens. Moreover, situated upon this sacred mountain, overlooking the immortal grottoes, burning incense and offering prayers, I pour forth my earnest entreaties—surely these shall resound before the divine and manifest abundant blessings.

The Vice Commissioner of Pacification of Dangchuan, Zhang Lin, is endowed with far-reaching judgment and upholds a heart of purity and uprightness. His discernment is impartial, his loyalty unwavering. In serving the public and honoring his lord, his mind is as clear as still water; in governing subordinates and relieving the people, his guidance is as effortless as a turning wheel. Moreover, his encampments bristle with tiger-like troops, and his seasonal rewards are ever generous. Though warfare has raged for years, provisions have been transported across a thousand *li* without fail. His words are ever for the state’s welfare, his ambitions never for personal gain. Constantly diligent and reverent, he forgets sleep and meals. All who receive his beneficence know his grace.

I, your humble servant, a lowly official, have been lifted on fragile wings. Relying on his protection, I now soar with resolve. Thinking to beseech the true spirits, I offer this prayer in gratitude.

Now, as the warmth of yang stirs and the valleys awaken to spring, I recall his birth and reverently perform the *Dahui* rites. Gazing upon the celestial patterns, I present my earnest pleas; turning my heart toward the rivers and mountains, I offer devotion. Incense mingles with the clouds of the streams, lamps blend with the moonlight on the peaks. A thousand crags lie in stillness, the midnight wind is clear. I display the rites of solemn reverence, preparing the offerings of water plants and sacred herbs.

I humbly pray that the radiance of the Three Luminaries may shine upon him, and the winds of the Ten Immortals descend. May they witness the sincerity of this libation and bestow luminous blessings. May his lifespan extend to twice nine and six, and the disasters of the Five Phases and Three Destinies be averted. May his virtuous deeds flourish upon the immortal ranks, and his hidden merits illuminate his lineage through the ages.

Then may the frontier regions know peace, and the borderlands be tranquil. May pestilence and plague be dispelled, and weapons of war set aside. May the sagely lord perfect the governance of *wu-wei*, and the provincial defenses display the grace of soft submission. May all beings, seen and unseen, attain their proper places, and all creatures, soaring and sinking, fulfill their destinies. Dare I forget my duty to refine and uphold this, in service to the flourishing and bright?

I, your humble servant, Mo Tingyi, offer this *Jiao* prayer for the Nine Palaces and Celestial Talismans.

I have heard that the vast and profound forms the body, and the Central Yellow establishes its position. It governs water and fire as their sovereign, and crowns metal and wood as their lord. Thus, it nurtures the myriad spirits and encompasses the Five Wefts. Above, it oversees the state; below, it extends to human relations. Fortune and misfortune are its charge, and safety and peril are bound to it.

This palace falls under the *Zhen* trigram, where the Five Ghosts converge. The *qi* of destiny flies like a banner, and this month coincides with its influence. Fearing the onset of disaster, I am deeply anxious. Reverently selecting an auspicious day, I meticulously perform the *jiao* rites. I humbly pray that the true spirits witness my sincerity and bestow great blessings: turning peril into safety, transforming misfortune into fortune; dissolving calamities, averting disasters, increasing emoluments, and prolonging years. May my family and dependents enjoy health and peace, and may public and private affairs harmonize. I cannot express the fullness of my devotion.

**Prayer for the Southern Dipper Rites**

Reverently considering: the Great Dao congeals in truth, and the mysterious power nurtures all life. Though the sources of purity and turbidity differ, the positions of yin and yang are distinct. The Upper Palace of the Southern Dipper truly governs the register of life. Above, it extends to the state; below, it reaches all human relations. Longevity and emoluments, whether abundant or meager, are all subject to its dominion, without distinction between the great and the minute.

We, your servants, have been blessed to serve this sagely dynasty and personally witness the flourishing of the Dao. Yet, though we have received the gifts of heaven and earth, our actions and intentions may still err. In navigating the world and conducting ourselves, how could we be free of faults? Failing to repent and atone, we have thus invited calamity and peril. Moreover, we fear that the stars of our fate, the Nine Palaces, and the Three Destinies may bring us misfortune, punishment, or conflict. The ways of the spirits are profound, and mortal understanding is limited. We must rely on incense and offerings to express our earnest prayers.

Daring to select an auspicious day, we humbly perform the grand *jiao* rites. We pray that your radiant light shines down, and your mysterious gaze descends upon us. Witness our sincere devotion and bestow upon us boundless blessings: dispelling disasters, averting misfortune, increasing emoluments, and prolonging years. May our names be erased from the ledgers of the underworld and inscribed in the registers of the living. May public and private affairs harmonize, and our families enjoy health and peace. May the living and the departed alike receive your grace and protection. We cannot express the fullness of our devotion.

---

**Prayer for the Pacification of a Residence by Hu Xian, Court Attendant**

I have heard that the *Yijing* presents its teachings through images, drawing from the principle of great strength. The sages established laws to replace the crude dwellings of old. The construction of halls and houses has been a constant from ancient times to the present. Their positions are determined by yin and yang, and their designs are shaped by the balance of punishment and virtue. The spirits are thus commanded, each to their duty. To defy them brings misfortune and calamity; to follow them brings good fortune and blessings.

Recently, my residence failed to shelter me from wind and rain. I took the opportunity to renovate it, making improvements as needed. Months passed, and the great work was completed. Yet I fear that in excavating earth and transporting stones, in raising the low and lowering the high, the tools may have trespassed where they should not, and the digging may have offended the spirits. Without performing the *jiao* rites of repentance and gratitude, I am constantly filled with apprehension and concern.

Moreover, the land on which my residence stands has seen five families succeed one another over the years, and its presiding spirits have changed many times. I worry that their consciousness lingers, still lingering in delay. Relying on this *jiao* rite, I pray that all may be elevated and released.

Thus, I have solemnly prepared the courtyard and reverently established the ritual altar. I invoke the talismans of the *Lingbao* scriptures, following the canons of the *Tai Xuan*. I beseech the true sages to descend and witness my sincerity.

I humbly pray that the Five Emperors and the host of spirits will look upon my devotion. May the envoys of the talismans be commanded to proclaim the decree to the earthly authorities. May the dragon spirits be pacified, and all offenses be dissolved. May misfortunes be eradicated, and true *qi* flow abundantly. May unmanifested calamities be averted, and new blessings be bestowed. May lingering *qi* of the dead and stagnant wandering souls be cleansed and relocated. From the seen to the unseen, may all find their rightful place. May the symbols of the Six Jia and Five Phases, the Nine Palaces and Eight Trigrams, each rest in their proper domains, forever ensuring steadfast good fortune. May my household enjoy peace and prosperity, and may my diligent efforts in cultivation meet the favor of the true spirits. We cannot express the fullness of our devotion.

---

**Prayer for the Earth Net Rites by Hu Fan, Minister of Works**

I have heard that the Five Planets receive their essence from the cosmos, and the Three Powers take their positions in the universe. They bear the molding force of the Supreme Dao and are nurtured by the mysteries of the Highest Mystery. Yet as the cycles of time shift, yin and yang rise and fall. Fortune and misfortune alternate, and cold and heat follow their course. Adversity gives way to prosperity, and calamity is followed by blessing. This is the natural principle of all things, an unchanging truth.

How could I, in my mediocrity, dare to forget caution and reverence? Within my current year, I find myself in a period of misfortune. My great fate resides in the year of *jia-chen*, and my minor fate stands upon *ding-si*. Moreover, these two months coincide with the Earth Net region of the Four Palaces, and my own trigram’s position may bring about a convergence of misfortunes. There is no one to whom I can turn for expiation.

I further fear that the stars of my fate may align with adverse influences, and the flying banners of destiny may respond to changes. The Five Phases may clash, and the Three Destinies may weaken. Though the Horse of Post has arrived this year, I fear that calamity may still overcome fortune. Reflecting on my conduct and examining my heart, I recognize the need for repentance and prayer to express my earnest devotion.

Thus, I have selected an auspicious day to reverently prepare the *jiao* altar, inviting the descent of the august spirits in hope of their illumination. I humbly pray that the Three Officials and Five Emperors will look down upon my sincerity, and that the Lords of the Dipper and the Pole Star will bestow their boundless grace. May the register of extended life be bestowed, and blessings be granted. May the records of accumulated sins be burned, and my faults be pardoned. May disasters be dissolved in the Earth Net, and misfortunes be eradicated in the *Xun* Palace. May my lifespan be renewed, and my good fortune assured. May public and private affairs harmonize, and my family enjoy peace. May I forever receive your aid and protection, and never betray the blessings of the true spirits. We cannot express the fullness of our devotion.

---

**Prayer for the Rites of the Original Destiny on Xin-You Day by Yin Juhong**

Reverently considering: the Great Dao manifests its power, and the Three Spirits initiate all things. We receive our forms and destinies, and our marks and signs determine our lives. Our bodies are nurtured by the union of *kun* and *qian*, and our fortunes are aligned with the celestial and earthly bureaus. The Three Officials examine and record our deeds, leaving no sin or blessing unaccounted. The Five Emperors govern, and all matters of life and death are bound to them.

I, your humble servant, am but dust and ignorance, yet I have been blessed to serve this illustrious and enlightened age. My name is recorded in the central offices, and I stand among the inner ranks. In the presence of the phoenix and unicorn halls, I tread with shame, for my steps are many. Beneath the light of the sun and moon, I measure my limits and grow ever more fearful. My meager merits remain unnoticed, while my accumulated faults must be profound.

I constantly worry about the stains of past lives and the sins of this one. Without repentance and purification, how can they be absolved? Moreover, I fear that the Three Destinies, Five Phases, celestial patterns, and yearly fortunes may bring me misfortune or calamity. I may have offended the spirits and the lords who govern, or violated the teachings of benevolence, righteousness, mystery, and Confucianism.
