Perhaps I have harmed others for my own gain, or caused accidental injury through carelessness. My sins are easily accumulated, while my good deeds are difficult to accomplish. Perhaps my lifespan is short, or my emoluments meager.

Thus, on the day of my original destiny, I have prepared the *jiao* rites. Along with my prayers, I offer them to the enlightened spirits. Yet, as I have traversed perilous paths and witnessed the turmoil of the divine land, fleeing through forests and mountains or hastening along roads, I have endured five such journeys. There has been no time to perform the *jiao* rites, and my incense and lamps have been neglected. Sleep and sustenance have brought me no peace.

Now, as I bear the imperial command to the southwest, halting my steed at Min and Jian,
the roads lie unobstructed, and the passes and bridges stand wide open.
The emperor’s grace flows like celestial waves, reaching even the distant four frontiers;
joyous voices and radiant faces resound and shine throughout the land.
Moreover, this Lesser City is in truth a realm of immortals—
here, one may still the heart and offer earnest prayers,
here, one may invoke blessings and seek the true Dao.
Thus, I have divined an auspicious day, aligning it with my original destiny.
Bearing the tokens of faith, I prepare incense and flowers,
and at this very moment, I make up for the rites long neglected.
Sincerity reaches the spirits, and their divine insight must surely perceive it.
I humbly beseech that my crimson devotion be accepted,
and that vast blessings be bestowed in return.
May past vows be fulfilled, and new grace be granted anew.
May my disasters and misfortunes be dispelled, my official rank and lifespan extended.
May the living and the dead alike know peace, and all my kin and dependents be secure.
Above all, may the altars of state flourish and the cosmos be serene.
May the Three Luminaries follow their proper courses, and the Six Qi harmonize.
May martial might recede and civil culture thrive, the times be peaceful, and the people prosper.
May the imperial carriage return in triumph, and the dragon’s destiny be forever firm.
May all these prayers be answered in full, and the era of Great Peace be witnessed at last.

---

**Prayer for the Empress’s Original Destiny *Jiao* Rite**

I have heard that the Great Dao bestows its scriptures, and the Mysterious Origin propagates its teachings,
aiding the times and assisting the state, spreading transformation and delivering the people.
Its merits precede even the symbols of antiquity, its benevolence extends beyond all things.
As the sacred texts are revered in the highest courts,
the prayers of humanity must reach the heavens;
as celestial grace descends upon the earth,
the blessings of the true realm are surely granted.
All beings receive protection, great and small alike.

This year, my major destiny encounters the position of the Three Killers.
My minor destiny, governed by the Wood Branch, lies in decline and weakness.
The Celestial Stems and the tones of official rank are both obstructed by Earth.
The Flying Banners and Four Killers remain in the Tiger’s domain.
The Net Star treads the palace of my surname, while Saturn lingers in the constellation of discord.
Mars, in its course, approaches my life palace.
The year’s progression, moreover, falls under the Earth Net.
The physicians’ diagnoses reveal that my visceral *qi* remains unbalanced,
my constructive and defensive energies disharmonious, my vital *qi* depleted and thin.
The six pulses have not recovered, and the nine palaces remain weak.
I fear misfortune may arise, and my fate grow even more dire.
I also fear that from past lives, karmic debts remain unpaid,
and with each passing thought or action, new transgressions accumulate.
Thus, I must rely on these memorials and prayers, hoping they reach the spirits in repentance.

Therefore, in accordance with the luminous statutes, I have selected an auspicious day,
prepared the words of petition, and presented this memorial with reverence.
I beseech the celestial officials and divine soldiers to descend, witness, and protect me.
May my internal organs be at peace, and external misfortunes be averted.
Above, may the baleful influences of the stars be dissolved;
below, may the afflictions of my destiny and the harms of the year be erased.
May enmities be reconciled, and debts and disputes settled.
May the Six Qi flow freely, and the hundred passages be regulated.
May my frailty and peril be transcended, my lifespan and rank increased.
May the Northern Palace reverse my brief years,
and the Southern Culmen inscribe long life upon me.

I humbly implore the Perfect and Great Dao, the Three Supreme Ones,
to ever expand their compassionate salvation
and grant the blessings of peace and truth.
I vow to remain steadfast in loyalty and filial piety, to discipline body and mind.
To praise the enlightened ruler’s nurturing benevolence,
and repay the profound grace of the Dao’s creation and completion.

---

**Daoist Memorial for the Emperor’s *Jiao* to the Great One and the Kindling of the Golden Register Lamps**

I have heard that the One *qi* gave birth to all forms, and the myriad beings depend on it for their beginning.
On high, it suspended the celestial bodies, clearly distinguishing the firm and the yielding.
The power of governance rests with the Most Sagely.
Heaven commands the emperor to shepherd the people,
and the emperor receives Heaven’s mandate to rule over them.
At the dawn of the Regulator’s brilliance, the positions of ruler and minister were established;
in the age of abdication and warfare, both virtue and the Dao were practiced.
In times of peril, the mysterious virtue shines ever brighter;
in eras of decline, vast blessings spread ever wider.

The August Martial, Wise, and Filial Emperor of Great Shu,
his virtue matching the vast heavens, his merit extending to all living beings,
received the Mandate in accord with Qian,
eternally securing the Three Realms.
Divine intelligence aids his counsel, and the human world’s Jade Candle aligns with the seasons;
the rhythms of pitch and calendar harmonize, and the celestial Pearl Bag follows its proper measure.
The people flourish, and the years bring abundant harvests.
Auspicious omens and felicitous signs are recorded day and month.
Yet still, he labors by day and remains vigilant by night, reverently serving Heaven.
He honors the unseen and the manifest, toiling for the welfare of the millions.
His sole concern is to relieve the suffering of the people, his heart untouched by pleasure or distraction.
He ponders the myriad regions, ever striving for benevolence and longevity.

Recently, as the Four Spirits governed the course of destiny, they resided in the Palace of the Salty Pond.
The Directing Talisman descended upon the fields of the Hall of Light.
Warfare arose anew, yet swift victory was achieved.
Those traitorous rebels, who broke their oaths and plotted treason,
now face the ruin they sought—like drifting pestles or scorched trees.
This is the result of the spirits savoring his sagely virtue, Heaven aiding his imperial might.
The transformation of calamity into fortune is witnessed,
and the signs of national peace and prolonged destiny are revealed.

Now, as the year draws to a close and the seasons prepare to shift,
I give thanks for the profound grace bestowed thus far,
and pray for the bright blessings of the coming spring.
To repay his sagely efforts, I offer my utmost sincerity.
I kindle the divine lamps of the Golden Register and prepare the grand *jiao* of the River Chart.

I humbly beseech the Most High to witness and respond.
May the Ten Spirits ever bestow their radiant favor,
and for three years, may blessings be fully granted.
May the precious destiny endure forever, and the ancestral temples know peace.
May the emperor’s longevity match the Five Peaks, his brilliance equal the Two Luminaries.
May the Eight Directions submit to his transformation, and the myriad states rest in harmony.
May all attain the customs of the Dao, and the rebels of unruly lands be swept away.
May the Crown Prince shine with double brightness, and the civil teachings flourish.
May he assist in the sagely plans and extend the great enterprise.
May the six palaces and hundred officials unite in their support;
may the millions of people and the six armies all enjoy renewed well-being.
May the dragon spirits secretly guard him, and the rivers and mountains remain ever secure.
May the hidden and the manifest, the soaring and the sinking, forever receive his vast grace.

**Prayer for the Crown Prince’s Offering of the Grand Jiao and the Lighting of the Golden Register Lamp on Behalf of the Emperor**

We have heard that the mysterious transformation first divided, and the Two Modes took form. They fused and settled into the positions of yin and yang, while the divine and luminous wielded the power of governance. The Supreme Heavenly Worthy and the August Emperor of the Highest sit upon the Purple Tenuity, overseeing all, dispatching divine envoys to traverse the realm. Thus, the Five Phases and Eight Winds, Heaven’s One and Earth’s Two, stir the clouds and mists, riding the stars in their celestial courses. Gazing afar across the Nine Wilds, they secretly bestow admonitions; traversing all directions, they reveal omens of fortune and misfortune. From antiquity to the present, who would dare forget vigilance and self-cultivation?

Your servant, by the mandate of the Straight Talisman, resides in the Hall of Light; by the movement of the Four Spirits, occupies the position of the Completed Pond. It is fitting to purify and cleanse, to offer prayers with utmost sincerity.

The Emperor, receiving the mandate from the Supreme Mystery, grasps the talisman and inherits the lineage. He extends the transformation of magnanimity and frugality, fostering the foundation of purity and tranquility. He seeks to harmonize the Great Peace and bring well-being to the myriad states. Recently, neighboring domains betrayed righteousness, violating borders and breaking covenants. They ravaged the common people and encroached upon commanderies and cities. Yet swiftly, the malevolent were pacified, and all pernicious vapors dispelled. The command and guidance arose from sagely counsel, while divine power truly aided in the assistance.

Now, the frontiers are secure and serene, the Han’s borders purified and orderly. The stellar cycle has turned, and the year’s rhythm draws to a close. On this day of *ren-shen* in the month, the first dawn of the new year, we prepare the altar and reverently offer thanksgiving. We perform the Grand Jiao of the Supreme Unity and kindle the divine lamp of the Golden Register. Below, it illuminates the hidden passes; above, it reaches the Supreme Ultimate. It sweeps away accumulated calamities and stagnation, extending and bestowing blessings and felicity.

We humbly pray that the ancestral temples remain secure and prosperous, that the altars of soil and grain stand firm. May the precious chart endure forever, and the sagely longevity stretch afar. May he surpass the glory of the Fire Deities of the Cloud Palace, and transcend the legacies of the Han, Ji, and Zhou. May he swiftly achieve unification and attain Great Harmony. May the six palaces exemplify support, and the hundred officials unite in loyal sincerity. May the Three Luminaries shine brightly, and the Four Seasons harmonize. May the year bring abundant harvests, and the customs be free of pestilence. May the dragon spirits rejoice, manifesting the auspices of the Five Winds and Ten Rains; may the rivers and mountains flourish, flowing with the blessings of horse-drawn carriages and ritual vessels. May our earnest sincerity be made manifest, ascending to the true numina. We look up in prayer for the grace of their scrutiny and protection, that they may broadly bestow vast and enduring blessings.

---

**Prayer for the Jiao on Behalf of the Commander of Jingyuan Army on His Natal Day**

We reflect that the Supreme Way gives birth and completes, its mysterious work molding and shaping. It governs the lordship of yin and yang, distinguishing the categories of the myriad beings. All receive their essence and form, looking up to rely on divine transformation.

Your servant has been blessed to receive the shade of the Dao and has presumptuously borne the favor of the court. Clothed in the light of imperial grace, I oversee military affairs. Yet my merits and achievements remain unremarkable, while my dust-like transgressions run deep. Day and night, I examine and follow, daring not forget vigilance and exertion. Yet I fear that my cultivation may be lacking, my conduct often straying, accumulating faults and blemishes, without offering repentance and purification.

Perhaps the Five Phases and Three Destinies have their times of punishment; the Nine Luminaries and arrayed stars, their moments of scrutiny. Perhaps old grudges remain unresolved, or past debts unabsolved. The ways of the divine are inscrutable, and human understanding cannot fathom them. Thus, calamities and stagnation may arise, with no means to express remorse and seek forgiveness.

On this day of my natal destiny, I reverently offer the Jiao and libations. Following the statutes of the Heavenly Perfected, I prostrate myself and present the Great Petition. We humbly beseech the August and Sagely to respond, the True and Numinous to scrutinize and protect. May they perceive our earnest sincerity and bestow mysterious grace, dissolving calamities and leveling misfortunes, extending the span of life and increasing its blessings. May they secretly augment my official emoluments and broadly remit my transgressions. May they untie past enmities and bestow future blessings. I vow to devote myself to loyalty and filial piety, forever serving ruler and kin.

---

**The Emperor’s Prayer at the Jade Bureau Altar in the Dragon Prosperity Abbey**

We reflect that Heaven arrays the constellations, and Earth spreads its renowned regions. The resplendent symbols hang in the celestial net, while the blessed courts stand in the square marshes. The luminous wield their authority to protect the state and the household.

We note that the Jade Bureau and Terrace of Mystery is where the Primordial One descended in traces. Locked within this metropolis, it lies close to the city gates. Though the years have deepened, its numinous radiance does not fade. Its emptiness and stillness differ not from the forests and valleys, yet its auspicious influence often extends to the common people. We have always held it in reverence, never daring to forget our devotion.

Since we reverently received the mandate of Heaven and established the court, the vermilion gates and palace portals have been aligned with the proper yang positions; the frost altars and feathered halls have followed the appropriate reforms. Yet the stone chambers and grotto gates, the true image of the Venerable Lord, remain. Morning and evening, the rites of incense and candles are performed with utmost reverence. Approaching the dragon steps and phoenix gates, we redouble our purity and solemnity. This place can indeed share eternity with Heaven, enduring forever.

Yet we fear that the dragon spirits and officials of yin and yang, in their activities and disturbances, may have alarmed the multitude with their clamor. Having trodden upon and harmed them, we now offer prayers and repentance through the Jiao. From this auspicious day, we prepare the incense altar. Though our devotion may not reach far, the true numina will surely perceive it.

We humbly beseech the Primordial One to bestow protection, the Great Dao to open its grace. May they remit past transgressions and bestow future blessings. May the precious chart endure forever, and the altars of soil and grain remain secure. May wind and rain be harmonious, and the dragon spirits conciliatory. May calamities be swept away, and sins and faults leveled.

Should the Straight Talisman and Supreme Unity’s movements shift to other regions, or the Fire Star and Earth Star’s scrutiny fall upon our person, we pray that their power may turn to protect and sustain us, bringing clarity and peace to our humble self. May beacons not flare at the four borders, and pestilential vapors not afflict the people. We forever pledge our sincere devotion, offering it up to the mysterious bounty.

---

**Edict for the Jiao Offered to the Famous Mountains and Great Rivers**

We reflect that the Dao arrays the Three Realms, and Earth bears the multitude of beings. Some are the lands where immortals cultivate and refine, others the domains where perfected officials govern. Their numinous foundations are visible, their divine transformations boundless.

We reverently serve the Supreme Mystery and gloriously receive the great treasure. Looking down, we follow the regions, purifying our sacrifices. Recently, the affairs of state and military have been numerous, and weapons have been employed year after year. We have not yet been able to attend to all, and thus constantly harbor trepidation. We seek to express our reverence and devotion, hoping to dispel calamities and faults.

We now command the Daoist masters of the Three Caverns, together with the envoys dispatched, to solemnly prepare the jiao rites and secretly convey our supplications to the mysterious gaze of the Dao. May the four seasons be abundant, the six qi unassailing. May longevity be extended, the state and house flourish. May the imperial lineage and throne endure, the hundred ministers and thousand officials prosper, from the court within to the lands without, and may the multitudes of the realm all equally receive blessings and protection. With reverence, we entrust these blue petitions, humbly presenting our sincere devotion.

**Edict for the Jiao Offered to Master Zhang of Xianju Mountain**

The Emperor of Great Shu respectfully bows his head to Master Zhang, the Perfected One of Dao who attained transcendence on Mount Beimang. Of the exalted perfected of the Purple Palace and the lofty adepts of the Dark Continent—riding the whirlwind, mounting the void, seated in being yet dwelling in non-being—they ascend the boundless to roam in spirit, enter the primordial chaos to conceal their radiance. Some manifest their signs to the state and altars, aiding the people at large; others secretly assist emperors, jointly purifying adversity and obstruction. Li Shunxing preserved the tranquility of Emperor Jing, Tao Zhenbai lent his support to King Xiao. In the *zi* year, you subtly admonished the Prefect, hoping for the secret enlightenment of Emperor Zhaolie. Those who heed your counsel receive felicity and great fortune; those who disregard it court misfortune and sorrow. Your brilliance, inscribed on silk and bamboo, shines as brightly as the sun and moon.

Now, among the common folk, Guo Hui has gathered herbs at the Xianju Abbey and discovered a bronze tablet left by the Perfected One in the Tianbao era. Its sixty characters form a perfect cycle, with names and dates fully recorded; its two centuries of concealment remain intact, with coin inscriptions and seal scripts all preserved. The succession is clearly evident, the days and hours unerring.

Where lichen encroaches and earth erodes, divine generals must surely guard and preserve; the verification aligns with the tally, truly bearing the Perfected One’s manifestation. Reflecting upon the vast virtue, it openly accords with auspicious omens. This matter surpasses the *Red Hidden* and *Yellow Charts*; its principle excels the phoenix’s bearing and dragon’s burden. Having witnessed the decree of prolonged prosperity, how dare I forget the reverent and diligent heart? Thus, I establish the altar of offering, hoping to repay the profound virtue. Still, I clear the brambles and thorns, selecting an auspicious day to commence the work. May emerald railings and vermilion eaves renew the old site; may the towers of Chen and distant pillars once more recognize the path of return. Earnestly I pray to the Perfected Spirits, that they may witness this bright requital. From the distant Thirty-Six Heavenly Palaces, may their majestic radiance descend; through the fourteen thousand *jiazi* cycles, may I forever bear and revere. [Unworthy as I am...]

**Prayer of the Crown Prince at the Offering on Xianju Mountain**

I humbly consider: where sunlit chambers adjoin rosy clouds, there lies the celestial metropolis; where jade altars and cassia halls stand, there is the worldly court of fortune. Whether the abode where Perfected Sages feast and wander, or the dwelling where immortals and spirits reside, all conceal marvels and nurture excellence, unfolding blessings and flowing auspices, aiding and protecting humanity and heaven, subtly assisting the state. This ancient abbey indeed reveals extraordinary omens. It has received the Perfected Tally of the Tianbao era, revealed in the *Secret Records of Lord Lao*. Golden script and avian seals, seal characters coiled like dragons—distinct and luminous, the auspicious traces appear newly made; brushed clean, the lichen’s marks yet remain. Several millennia ago, it foretold the sage lord’s unfolding of the chart; two hundred years of prosperity await our emperor’s reign. Imperial name and dynastic surname, birth date and year—each is clearly set forth, layer upon layer of verification. The subsequent text records my humble virtue, listing names in full. Having examined the writings of the charts and registers, my reverent devotion grows ever more earnest. Gazing afar at the misty peaks, I look up in gratitude for the numinous grace. Thus, at this altar of libation, I nurture the distant aspiration to burn incense and cultivate the Dao. Above all, I wish that the grand foundation may be firmly established, boundless as the vast seas; that the sagely longevity may be prolonged, towering higher than Mounts Min and Emei. May the Nine Regions follow in harmonious transformation, may the myriad realms return to benevolence. I vow my sincere loyalty and filial piety, to match the protection of the Perfected Spirits. [Unworthy as I am...]

*Guangcheng Collection*, Scroll Thirteen [concluded]
*Guangcheng Collection*, Scroll Fourteen

The *Ritual Hymn for the Emperor’s Offering at Mount Xianju*, Composed by Du Guangting, Grand Virtue of Literary Composition by Imperial Commission, Purple-Robed Bestowal, and Inner Attendant at the Supreme Clarity Palace in the Upper Capital

We humbly observe that sagely sovereigns and enlightened kings must attain auspicious omens, receiving the charts and registers amid songs of praise. Thus, enthroned in the majesty of a hundred million, they are deemed worthy of the Mandate of Heaven. Now, as Your Majesty approaches the sixth year of ascending the great throne, the transformative teachings have yet to bring peace to the living, and the distant frontiers still resist the true calendar. With trepidation and vigilance, You dare not rest in ease. You fear the inequity of punishments and the impropriety of rewards. Troops encamp across the plains, for the people’s prosperity remains unfulfilled; bleached bones fill the rivers, for the toll of slaughter knows no end. Ever mindful of these burdens, You seek to atone for transgressions and redeem faults. How could one dare speak of prophetic texts, when even the most learned remain unworthy?

This year, on the eighth day of the seventh month, Guo Jiongzhi, a commoner of Shifang County in Hanzhou, unearthed a bronze tablet while gathering herbs at the Abbey of Transcendent Dwelling. The tablet measured seven inches in length and four in width, inscribed with sixty characters:

*"The Record of Laozi’s Communication with Heaven states: In the ding-mao year, the king born in the jia-xu, yi-hai years shall enjoy two hundred years of life. The Son of Heaven: Wang Congjian, Wang Yuanying, Wang Wanggan, Wang Yue, Wang Ze, Wang Daoyi."*

The five characters in seal script remain undeciphered.

The text further states: *"At the Huazhang Hongdao Monastery north of Mang Mountain in Luozhou, [the tablet] was left during the Tianbao era."* This clearly heralds the advent of a sagely successor.

Reflecting upon my meager virtue, I am suddenly entrusted with such extraordinary auspices. It speaks of the prolongation of the celestial mandate and records the succession of descendants. Clutching this profound boon of the mysterious, I can only respond with trembling awe. Daring to pour forth my deepest sentiments, I humbly offer this sacrifice in gratitude.

May the sacred precincts of the morning court summon the famed mountains, each drawn by chariots of immortals, to partake together in this crimson sincerity. May the altars of state be secured, the people universally at peace. May wind and rain arrive without fail, and weapons be sheathed in lasting stillness. I rely wholly upon this numinous radiance, holding it deeply within my heart.

Respectfully submitted,
*The Emperor’s Ritual Text for the Libation of Divine Talismans in Repayment of Heavenly Grace*

I have heard that when Heaven bestows its favor, it manifests portents in the *Hetu* and *Luoshu*; when the Emperor models himself upon Heaven, he receives the mandate and bears the tally in accord with destiny. From antiquity to the present, this has been the ordained pattern, with the celestial mandate passing in succession.

My reign has chanced upon this mysterious fortune, yet my virtue remains shallow and dim. Following the decline of the Earthly Power, the myriad people were left without refuge; at the inception of the Golden Stem’s resurgence, the realm united in acclaim. Reverently upholding the *Tianbao* mandate, now in its sixth year.

I have ever risen before dawn to don my robes, and forgotten food until dusk. With trembling caution and reverent care, I serve the lofty heavens above. Now, bronze tablets bearing sacred script have emerged from an ancient temple, revealing the portent of the Supreme’s descent of blessings and fulfilling the sign of Heaven’s mandate received. My name and the cyclical year are fully inscribed—this was foreordained in the Nine Heavens, predetermined eons ago. The secret talismans shine forth, the true writ blazes in splendor, proclaiming the enduring of the august throne and manifesting the eternal design for posterity. Reflecting upon myself, I remain ever vigilant and awestruck. Reverently mindful of the divine gaze, I redouble my efforts in cultivation. Thus, with utmost solemnity, I conduct this sacred fast and turn in devotion to the Supreme Dao, praying that manifold blessings may harmonize and forever shelter the myriad realms.

Respectfully submitted,
*The Emperor’s Supplementary Libation Text for the Transformation of the Immortal Ge’s Natal Essence*

I have heard that the constellations adorn the heavens, and the mountains stand sentinel over the earth. Through them, the workings of qi and the signs of fortune are conveyed to bless the state and the household. Whenever I perform the rites of distant reverence, I invariably invoke renewed blessings. Now, as the Emperor, I have received Heaven’s mandate, grasped the tally in accord with destiny. This mountain of my natal destiny is none other than this sacred site of transformation. Its caverns cradle clouds and rain, its peaks clash with mist and rosy dawn—surely potent numina reside here, secretly aiding and sustaining. Moreover, as this propitious season arrives, I duly prepare the libation and prayers. With uplifted heart and reverent devotion, I humbly await the radiant gaze of the divine.

May the Most Holy Ones of the myriad heavens look down and perceive my sincerity; may the Three Perfected and the host of immortals together bestow their boundless grace. May the imperial destiny endure forever, and the altars of state flourish in prosperity. May the twenty-four peaks bear witness to the Emperor’s sacred longevity, and the imperial foundation stand firm for a hundred thousand myriad years. May the Four Seas and the Nine Provinces all submit to the transformative influence of his wisdom. May the five weapons be sheathed, and the hundred grains ripen in abundance. May all ascend to the realm of benevolence and longevity, and together embrace the true and orthodox Dao.

A Memorial Prayer by Vanguard King Chenglu for the Nine Luminaries Ritual on Behalf of His Grandmother

Of the arrayed Luminaries and Five Phases, each governs sin and fortune. From the roofbeam to the eaves, all things have their overseers. In the course of birth and nurture, how could there be no ominous or auspicious responses in protection? Within the dwelling, transgressions and flaws must surely exist. We must rely on the Dao’s power and the profound efficacy of the unseen to dissolve deep calamities and grave faults.

The Primordial Sovereign established the teachings, and the Three Caverns transmitted the scriptures. Daring to follow the canonical procedures, I humbly pray for blessings and protection.

Your servant’s grandmother, the Grand State Lady of the Dai Clan, née [X], is now eighty years of age, born on the thirteenth day of the third month in the yi-mao year, at the wu-wu hour. At present, the Earth and Fire Luminaries reside in the triply harmonious quadrant, while the Celestial Talisman and Flying Banners strike against the great fortune of her life’s course. The Five Earths overpower her Water Child, and this affliction coincides with her birth hour. From such penal clashes, a minor ailment has arisen. Trembling with anxiety and dread, I dare not rest at ease.

I reflect that, though I have been favored to serve in this sagely age and inherit a legacy of blessings, I was early orphaned and bereft, and later endured family hardships. Only my grandmother’s compassionate countenance has allowed me to attend her morning and evening. With heart carved out and sincerity poured forth, I vow to pray for her distant years. Yet now her illness—a goiter—persists, as inauspicious stellar influences continue to cast their light. I fear that within this dwelling, some offense may have been committed, or that across generations, unpaid karmic debts may linger. Perhaps among the departed, there remains some unresolved grievance, or in the hidden yin realms, some indictment awaits. From these accumulated frailties and perils, I can but seek repentance and absolution.

Thus, I have selected an auspicious day and reverently prepared the ritual altar. May the Great Dao shed its radiance, and the host of honored ones look down with compassion. For your servant’s grandmother, née [X], dissolve the afflictions of disaster and fault, and extend the span of her years. Augment her official emoluments in the Southern Palace, and expunge her name of guilt in the Northern Bureau. Sweep away her illness and infirmity, and harmonize the texture of her flesh. May divine medicines secretly sustain her, and numinous officers guard her in secret. Grant her full recovery and everlasting peace. May her household forever abide in auspicious harmony, with dragon spirits standing guard and all evil vanishing away.

I can but strive to cultivate virtue in earnest, seeking to repay the mysterious workings of the Dao. I am unworthy.

The Prayer for Rain at Mount Qingcheng by the Prince of Shu

Of the Five Marchmounts, the Supreme Office presides over the Palace of Zhen in Yue. Mighty as the Celestial Kingdom, towering as the Immortal Capital, it stands in majestic grandeur, anchoring the earth below and propping the vault of heaven above. Here the numinous spirits convene, revered by both land and water. Its bounty nurtures all quarters, its embrace enfolds the Three Shu. Sunlit cliffs scatter the rays of day, while shadowed ravines harbor the clouds. When it aids the seasons, omens of blessing descend; when it aligns with sagely rule, auspicious signs multiply. From antiquity to the present, from near to far, all look up to it in veneration and rely upon it in trust.

I, unworthy, have been graced with sagely compassion and entrusted with the governance of this vital domain. My jurisdiction extends over the lands of Zisu and Qian, and the borders of Wei, Lu, Man, and Dan. My rank is the highest in the court, my duties those of generals and ministers. Yet I ever fear that my merits are slight while my blessings are profound, that fortune may give rise to calamity. Bound by duty, I tremble with vigilance, my heart heavy with concern.

Since the advent of spring, the sweet rains have failed to arrive on time. The fields yield no harvest, and the scorching sun harms all living things. Though I have repeatedly performed sacrifices and entreated the gods, dense clouds gather only over the western outskirts, while the life-giving rains do not moisten the southern fields. The people, in their distress, find no recourse.

I recall that the Great Dao has bequeathed its scriptures, and the Heavenly Master has expounded his teachings. There are protocols for memorials and rites for prayer and offering. To conduct these devotions, one must rely upon sacred efficacy. Therefore, I lay bare my heart before the cloud-wreathed caverns and bow my head upon the immortal peaks. I await the response of the true companions and hope that my sincere plea may ascend.

Grant me timely harmony and abundant harvests, deliver me with rains that follow my wish and winds that comply. Banish the plump demons to the barren wilds, and let the rain-dancing *shangyang* birds prance within my realm. Let the tribes of the cliffs and the peoples of the caves beat their drums to display their might; let the dragon spirits of the grotto-palaces shake the numinous caverns to aid transformation. Dispel the cruel drought-demons and revive the withered seedlings. May the fragrance of millet and grain be pleasing, and the hopes for granaries overflowing be fully met.

I shall strive with all my heart to govern justly and exert myself in service of the public. Above all, I seek to repay the divine compassion and receive the protection of the Dao.

I respectfully dispatch You Du, Marshal of the Palace Guard, Acting Minister of the Right of the Department of State Affairs, and former Prefect of Lizhou, Cao Yue, along with the Grand Master of Vast Teaching of the Left and Right Streets, Purple-Robed Du Guangting, to conduct the rites of prayer and offering with utmost sincerity, placing their trust in the hope of grace.

I am unworthy.

Prayer for Rain by Ge Xianhua, Prince of Shu

Humbly considering that the twenty-eight lunar mansions hang in the heavens, their patterns fixed in place, while the twenty-four mountain spirits guard the earth, their images arrayed to divide the numinous. The constellations govern the unseen and the manifest, and all transformations oversee sin and fortune. How much more so the Heart Mansion, which is the palace of the Celestial Sovereign, and the Supreme Clarity, which is the capital of the immortals? Far-reaching, it commands the long rivers, leaning against the jade peaks’ towering beauty; majestic, it overlooks the great screen of mountains, facing the fertile lands of the Bronze Horse. That distant blessed realm casts its broad shade over Yong and Shu.

This minister’s life is bound to this mountain, yet undeservedly I grasp the jade tablet of office and still dwell in this immortal domain. Ever fearful that my rank is lofty and my duty weighty, while my strength is scant and my talent slight, I oversee the five noble ranks with distant enfeoffment and govern the six garrisons as my charge. At times, rewards and punishments miss their mark; at others, governance and nurture fall out of harmony. Below, there is resentment and sighing; above, the nurturing virtue is impaired. Anxious and uneasy, I have no respite, and faults and transgressions swiftly follow.

Since the second month of spring, timely rains have failed. Dust chokes the fields and ridges, the scorching sun flaunts its might. Winds parch the outskirts and plains, and oily clouds hide their form. The people sigh in distress, fearing the loss of the year’s labor; the fish in ponds and streams gasp, soon to hang in the drying stalls. My thoughts are consumed with this burning concern, yet I have no means to knock and beseech.

As for the finest delicacies, they are fully arrayed before the temple’s visage; the fat and plump sacrificial animals are offered without stint in prayer. Yet though I exhaust my sincere heart, no response is heard. Looking up, I recall that the immortals aid all beings, making no distinction between the hidden and the manifest. The Great Dao cherishes life, universally bestowing its compassionate grace. The Supreme Lord established the rites of expiation, and the Three Heavens opened the protocols of prayer and offering.

Reverently gazing toward the divine peak, I humbly present my mortal plea. With utmost devotion, I conduct the grand offering, looking up to implore the Perfected Ones. Humbly I pray that you take pity on what I have laid forth and grant me the great private grace of forgiveness. Pardon my faults and transgressions, and bestow upon me good fortune. Let thunder and lightning display their might, and the dragon spirits rejoice. May the abundant rains soak the land, bringing about a bountiful harvest. Let the Southern Mountains resound with the hissing of serpents, and the eastern fields flourish with lush crops. May the year’s expectations be forever harmonized, and the harvests truly abundant for years to come.

I vow to diligently uphold the rites of service, to fully repay the true spirits’ favor. I am unworthy.

*Prayer for the Zhou Tian Offering by Zhao Yu, Magistrate of Shifang*

Humbly considering that heaven and earth divide the numinous, and what governs them is the Most Sagely; that the unfathomable workings of yin and yang are embodied by the Most Divine. They preside over life and death, overseeing sin and fortune, responding to every prayer and connecting with every plea.

Undeservedly, by lack of talent, I govern this troubled district. The taxes and corvée it bears are heavy, and its collection and oversight are difficult. The villages and hamlets are impoverished and desolate, making governance and pacification all the more urgent. I purify my heart to seek remedies and restrain myself to serve the public. Through the power of the Dao, I have silently received the aid of the true spirits. Their hidden assistance has helped in collecting taxes and completing the district’s affairs. The land is at peace, plagues and poisons do not intrude, and the people live in tranquility.

Thinking to repay this mysterious grace, all have exhausted their sincere devotion. Together, we honor the altar of the Yellow Register and reverently prepare the rites of incense and prayer. We also conduct the grand offering to repay the divine favor.

Moreover, this district borders the immortal mountains, and its people embrace the transformative power of the Dao. The divine merits of Minister Li remain evident, and the sacred power of Perfected Luo often manifests. They command the blessed realms of the various abbeys and mark the true seats of the two transformations. Surely, they will cast their luminous gaze upon us and accept this sincere prayer.

Humbly I pray that the Supreme Lord extend his compassion and that the host of spirits grant their protection. May they universally aid the hidden and the manifest, extending their grace to the living and the dead. May all be blessed with good fortune and receive salvation and aid. Let this region be peaceful and serene, and the hundred grains flourish in abundance. May plagues, warfare, and weapons never intrude. May all creatures, whether soaring or crawling, each attain safety.

May my nine generations of ancestors and seven generations of descendants ascend to heaven and receive blessings; may those in the three evil destinies and the nine nights of darkness depart from suffering and join the Perfected. Furthermore, I beseech that disasters and calamities be erased, sins and transgressions be swept away. May my official emoluments and lifespan be silently increased, and my years be preserved. Together, we exert our hearts and minds, all receiving vast protection.

I am unworthy.

**Invocation for the Five Talismans to Pacify Wang’s Residence in Jiazhou**

It is heard that the Great Dao sheds its radiance, and the Five Scriptures bestow their teachings. They condense the qi of spontaneity, forming the texts of emptiness and profundity. Above, they rectify the celestial origin; below, they stabilize the terrestrial order. At the center, they govern the kalpas; on all sides, they bless living beings. Revered by the Three Realms, obeyed by the myriad spirits.

Should there be a place where construction stirs earth and timber, unwittingly offending the divine or openly transgressing prohibitions, all rely on these secret talismans to pacify the directions.

I, having recently required the building of my dwelling, have now completed this great endeavor and thus prepared these rites of incense and devotion. I have established an altar of the Yellow Register, widely offering repentance and deliverance; I have performed the libations of the Five Talismans, fully employing them to secure peace and tranquility.

I humbly implore the boundless compassion of the Most High and the penetrating gaze of the Perfected. May the dragon spirits rest in serenity, and all disasters and faults be dispelled. May there forever be no fear of offense, and may we constantly enjoy the blessings of peace.

As for the deities who have long governed the five clans, may each attain rebirth and together receive deliverance. Thus, I look up to bear the immeasurable grace of the Great Dao.

---

**Invocation for the Nine Luminaries Offering by Minister Zhang**

It is heard that the Great Dao condenses its radiance, and the Supreme Mystery manifests its signs. It illumines the nine lands and nurtures all living beings. It records fortune and misfortune, discerning sin and blessing. All things, great and small, are examined; not even the finest detail is overlooked.

Yet the Golden Tablets transmit their texts, and the Jade Scriptures expound the Dharma. They open the path of repentance and supplication, and establish the rites of remorse and gratitude. With sincere devotion, one is surely granted manifest protection.

I, so-and-so, considering my own emptiness and insignificance, have encountered this fateful conjunction. My position reaches the heights of the imperial court, and my duties are heavy and pressing. In reviewing lawsuits and adjudicating punishments, I may err in weighing severity and leniency, fearing the accrual of faults. Or, in my thoughts and concerns, I may inadvertently incur resentment. Or, through past lives and this existence, I may not have dispelled karmic debts. Reflecting in quietude, I am ever filled with trepidation.

Now, as the star of Saturn transits the Palace of Obstruction, and Ketu approaches my station, Mars—god of war—stands in opposition. My birth month and life position both coincide with celestial portents. From these inauspicious alignments, calamities have arisen. With a trembling heart, I prostrate myself in devotion. Looking up to the celestial signs, I knock in supplication; with utmost sincerity, I offer libations.

I humbly beseech the Perfected and Supreme Saints, the exalted Nine Luminaries. Moved by compassion for the mortal realm, may you descend your grace and pardon. Release past grievances and karmic debts; absolve grave transgressions and deep flaws. Prolong my years, and dissolve all disasters. Grant me harmony in all functions, balance in the six qi, complete relief from misfortune, and total freedom from illness and suffering.

May I, in loyalty and service, forever repay the sagacious ruler’s favor; in purity and concentration, fully respond to the protection of the revered spirits.

---

**Invocation for the Three Primordials Offering**

Most High and Boundless Great Dao, Original Celestial Honored One; Supreme Great Dao Lord; Most High Lord Lao; Ten Directions’ Spontaneous Numinous Treasure Celestial Honored Ones; Five Elders, Lords of the Three Primordials; Three Officials of Heaven, Earth, and Water; Thirty-Six Divisions of Revered Scriptures; Great Dharma Master of the Mysterious Center; Perfected of the Supreme Ultimate, Dharma Masters of the Three Heavens; True Spirits of the Heavenly, Earthly, and Watery Bureaus of the Three Realms; and all divine offices of the Mysterious Administration.

We, humble and insignificant in this dusty world, have accumulated blessings through past lives. Having encountered the mysterious transformation, we now serve the Perfected.

**Prayer for the Three Primordials Offering**

Yet dwelling in the mortal realm, our bodies are ensnared by worldly nets. Adrift in the tides of fame and profit, we wander through cycles of life and death. We have not yet fathomed the source of transcendence, merely admiring the principles of purity and emptiness. The six passions and three karmic actions constantly weave threads of transgression. Dark ledgers and black records swiftly accumulate faults and offenses. Some bear unresolved grievances from past lives, still bound to the gates of darkness. Unintentional harm or mistaken killings remain unconfessed and unexpiated. Or the five phases and three destinies bring calamitous alignments, with malevolent stars and baleful spirits encroaching. Common understanding cannot fathom these, nor can prayers of supplication find recourse. The Three Primordials have their appointed times of judgment, and the Five Emperors lack rites for ascending to clarity. Even the nine generations of ancestors and seven lineages may yet languish in the three evil paths. Accusations and litigations drag on, while errors and transgressions pile high. When blessings are exhausted and misfortune arrives, where can one turn for repentance?

On this day of the official’s audit and recording, we collectively present this offering rite. May the Mysterious Mirror turn to us, gazing down upon our sincere devotion. Bestow blessings and extend grace, preserving life and safeguarding destiny. Open the path for the nine generations, erasing their names from the right-hand ledger of sins. Dissolve all calamities, inscribing our names in the left-hand palace of life. May we forever receive the response of the Dao, eternally bearing its boundless favor.

Above, may the imperial throne endure, prolonging the great mandate of heaven. May the mysterious peace bring harmony to all living beings, near and far, in tranquil security. May the nine grains flourish abundantly, and the five weapons of war be stilled. May the suffering souls of the nine darknesses and six destinies all receive the vast and forgiving grace, each attaining the freedom of their true nature.

We cannot express the full extent of our reverent devotion and repentant pleas. With utmost sincerity, we present this prayer.

**Prayer for the Six Jia Registers by Wang Zongzhuan and Others at the Lower Assembly**

We, your humble servants, have long been of mediocre and shallow capacity, yet our aspirations yearn for the profound mysteries. We concentrate our minds upon the wondrous Dao, surrendering ourselves to the true vehicle. We study the sacred texts of the six Jia, admiring the essential principles of longevity. Yet, bound by official duties and worldly reputations, we have been unable to devote ourselves fully to cultivation. On the days of the Three Primordials and the four beginnings of the year, incense and lamps may be lacking; at the gatherings of the five fasts and six yang days, our attention may not be wholly fixed. We fear that unintentional harm or mistaken injuries persist, along with unresolved grievances from past lives. Or our current years may be afflicted by calamitous alignments, or our natal stars may face disastrous periods. Without having performed proper repentance, our anxieties only deepen.

Daring to choose this auspicious day of the lower assembly, we present this offering and register, beseeching your grace. We humbly implore the exalted Five Emperors to descend and bestow auspicious blessings. May the true officials of the six Jia wash away our transgressions and blemishes. Inscribe our names in the heavenly registers of the living, erasing our names from the earthly ledgers of the dead. May our entire households receive protection, and our seven generations of ancestors ascend to heaven. May our official salaries and lifespans be extended, and public and private affairs remain steadfast and peaceful. We vow to perpetually burn incense in gratitude for the mysterious compassion.

We cannot express the full extent of our devotion.

**Prayer for the Three Assemblies on Behalf of Disciples**

We, your humble servants, bear the weight of the great Dharma, spreading and upholding the true teachings to enlighten and deliver celestial and mortal beings. We transmit the Dao and convey the scriptures, aiding the times and enacting transformation. Your disciples, so-and-so and others, have long admired the great Dao, surrendering themselves to the Perfected. We uphold and believe in the mysterious regulations, receiving and bearing the talismans and registers. Since their transmission, years have passed. Yet we fear that before receiving the Dao and after bearing the registers, in our conduct and intentions, we may have committed transgressions. The three karmic actions and ten celestial paths may have been wantonly marred by errors; the Three Primordials and eight seasonal nodes may not have been duly honored. Our natal year, geng-shen, may have seen lapses in cultivation. Perhaps we have consumed meat and blood, defiling the true and pure. Or we may have indulged in excessive desires, violating the precepts and prohibitions. Without the three assemblies, it would be difficult to fully repent and pray.

Now, on this day of the assembly and the time of audit and review, we jointly present this great offering, submitting this memorial to declare our merits. We repent before the Ten Heavens, surrendering our sincerity to the Three Treasures. We beseech the cleansing of past calamities and the absolution of all transgressions. May our names be recorded in the ledgers of good deeds and inscribed in the palaces of the living. May enmities be reconciled and debts settled. May the true qi flourish within, bringing joy to all faculties. May the numinous officials guard us without, dissolving all evil. Within the five phases and three destinies, and amid the dark and bright stars, may no baleful influences ever descend, and may disasters and misfortunes forever cease. May the nine generations of ancestors ascend to heaven, and the six relations receive blessings. May public and private affairs be upright and auspicious, and all movements and stillness be healthy and fitting. May our lifespans be extended and our blessings vast. We vow to cultivate diligently, repaying the mysterious grace above.

We cannot express the full extent of our devotion.

*Guangcheng Collection, Volume Fourteen Concluded*
*Guangcheng Collection, Volume Fifteen*

**Petition for the Emperor’s Natal Rites**
*Presented by Du Guangting, Grand Master of Imperial Edicts, Purple-Robed Eminence of Supreme Virtue, and Inner Offering Attendant of the Supreme Clarity Palace in the Upper Capital*

To the Boundless Dao of the Supreme, the Venerable Lord Lao, the Five Elder Thearchs, the Three Officials of Heaven, Earth, and Water, the Four Directors of the Celestial Bureaus, the Seven Stars of the Northern Dipper, the August Jade Emperor of the Highest Mystery, the Sacred Peaks and River Deities, the Earthly Courts, and the Host of Celestial Spirits of the Sexagenary Cycle:

We humbly submit: when the Two Qi shaped form and the Five Phases framed appearance, we received the virtue of the Great Dao’s creation and the grace of the Primordial Harmony’s nurturance. As for the rise and fall of life’s register, the abundance or meagerness of official emolument, the fortune or misfortune of personal conduct, and the auspiciousness or inauspiciousness of one’s fate—all are governed from above by the celestial offices and determined laterally by the natal destiny. Every assessment, great or small, is meticulously recorded.

Your servant has long been favored with profound blessings, reverently inheriting the mysterious grace. Charged with upholding the celestial mandate and responding to the times with governance, I am ever mindful of my unworthy virtue, which may fail to inspire, and fearful that rewards and punishments may err. Thus, I am filled with trepidation, steering this fragile vessel with utmost care. Relying solely on divine power, I seek to bring peace to the people.

Therefore, with a mind turned inward, I bow before the sacred altar, hoping that the power of the Dao may secretly aid me and that the numinous perfected may invisibly assist. May the five weapons of war be stilled, the hundred grains flourish in abundance, the realm within and without enjoy harmony, and all living beings dwell in ease. I vow to devote myself to cultivation, repaying the mysterious compassion above.

I cannot fully express the depth of my reverence.

**Petition for the Crown Prince’s Natal Rites**

We humbly submit: the Great Dao scatters its radiance, and the Heavenly Origin spreads its transformations, giving rise to the myriad forms and nurturing the Three Powers. Thus, true officials are commanded to oversee the registers of destiny. The waxing and waning of the Five Phases all derive from divine power, and the rise and fall of the Three Lives all stem from the numinous treasury.

Your servant has long been bathed in profound grace, occupying a position in the Eastern Palace. In attending to meals and inquiring after well-being, I strive to fulfill my duties with reverence; in cultivating loyalty and filial piety, I can never fully repay the kindness of sovereign and father. Therefore, on this day of my natal destiny, I humbly prepare the rites of offering and prayer.

May disasters be averted and transgressions repented, blessings augmented and prosperity prolonged. May the sacred person enjoy boundless longevity, the great enterprise endure in peace; may a thousand auspicious signs descend upon the precious destiny, and the flourishing age be eternally served. With utmost sincerity, I dare to hope for mysterious protection.

I cannot fully express the depth of my devotion.

**Petition for the Nine Palaces of the Celestial Patterns by Attendant Censor Cui Yin**

We humbly observe: when the Supreme Mystery suspends its patterns, the Seven Governors follow their cycles; when the earth below turns its mechanism, the Nine Palaces take flight in transformation. Through their traversal, they reveal fortune and misfortune. Thus, the Three Lives and Five Phases bring responses of disaster or blessing, while the odd and even of yin and yang manifest signs of good and evil.

This year, the flying banners of the Nine Palaces alight upon the central position, and the celestial tally descends upon my birth sign; the Five Stars proceed in their courses, with Mars opposing my natal palace. My current year falls in the region of the Earthly Net, and both major and minor destinies suffer clashes. Illness has arisen, and recovery has not yet been attained.

Daring to approach the gate of the Great Dao’s compassionate salvation and follow the Supreme’s decree for offering and prayer, I lay bare my heart before the numinous altar, gazing upward in reverence. I universally proclaim my devotion to the celestial patterns and repent before the host of perfected spirits.

I humbly implore the Six Sages of the Southern Palace to open the scriptures of long life and bestowed fortune, and the Seven Primes of the Northern Dipper to grant the power to avert death and descend blessings. May my official years be extended, and disasters dissolved. May the distant and eternal be revealed, and the brief and fleeting reversed. May the hundred faculties be at ease, and the Six Qi harmonized. May past debts and former grievances be released, and deep flaws and grave transgressions pardoned. May the Nine Mysteries bestow fortune, and my entire clan dwell in peace.

With a heart of diligent cultivation, I seek to repay the protection of the august spirits.

I cannot fully express my devotion.

**Petition at the Stone Inscription of the Venerable Lord Lao at the Stone Wall Abbey of the Mysterious Origin in Langzhou**

We humbly submit: this is a numinous capital of creation, a sacred realm of immortals. Its peaks soar across the sky, its emerald cliffs rise by the river’s edge. Before the misty peaks, the sacred ancestor’s divine presence emerges; within the pine and bamboo groves, the jade lads’ true forms stand revealed. No carving or painting could achieve this—it is the marvel of heaven and earth’s natural art.

Thus, its hidden streams flow with radiance, bestowing blessings upon those in need. It often averts disasters of drought and flood, bringing timely responses of prosperity. Yet today, the imperial carriage lingers by the Han shallows, and the road to the Qin plains remains distant. I pray to the luminous might of the Mysterious Ancestor and the far-reaching grace of the divine descendants, that the myriad households may be purified and the grasses and trees thrive in peace.

May it not be that by the bridge over the Yi River, only the remnants of Pang Xun’s faction are swept away, or by the shrine on Mount Huo, only the forces of Liu Wu are crushed. With reverence, I await the mysterious power to flourish the great mandate.

I cannot fully express my hope and devotion.

**Petition at Tianmu Mountain in Xianzhou**

We humbly submit: this mountain anchors the earth’s heart, its cavern opening the celestial eye. It harbors mist and rain, stores wind and thunder. Its cliffs conceal immortal scriptures, its springs clarify the numinous pools. The abbey’s name reflects the beauty of Fufu, and the town’s title bears the honor of "Serving the State." Through this prayer, blessings are surely secured.

Now, as the jade carriage moves in accord, the vermilion palace suffers calamity. I humbly seek the invisible assistance of the perfected, together inaugurating the destiny of restoration. May the Mysterious Ancestor’s profound power be displayed anew, dazzling the double-pupiled; may the teachings of the Four Instructions of Master Xuan be proclaimed, enlightening the fourfold vision.

May it not be that on Mount Shouchun, tales of martial aid still linger, or before the Ji Shun Shrine, only the welcome of the imperial carriage is celebrated. May the Dao’s transformation be magnified, and the true wind spread far.

I cannot fully express my reverent hope and devotion.

**Petition for the Great Rites of the Three Primes by the Empress**

We humbly observe: the Dao’s transformations shape all things, and divine power nurtures them. The Qi divides into the Two Images, bestowing the private grace of encompassing and sustaining; the Three Primes unfold their seasons, determining the handles of reward, punishment, and retribution. Thus, the Northern Capital’s Yellow Springs often serve as the season of judgment and pardon, while the Southern Culmen’s Literary Prosperity frequently bestows the grace of transcendence and ascent.

Within human relations, fortune and misfortune, good and evil all manifest. With sincere devotion, I have received profound favor.

Your servant, by fortune’s grace, has enjoyed prosperity and walked a flourishing path. Occupying the vermilion palace, I assist in stabilizing the imperial destiny. Yet I am ever mindful of my inadequate virtue, which fails to repay such extraordinary grace, and fearful that past lives and accumulated existences may harbor unresolved flaws. The Five Phases and Three Lives may yet bring calamities, with Mars approaching my natal palace and the celestial tally residing on my birthdate.

Fearing the onset of calamity and misfortune, my resolve is fixed upon repentance and prayer. As this is the season of the Great Amnesty of the Middle Prime, a time when all under heaven yearn for grace, I humble my heart before the numinous altar, bowing my head in reverence. I traverse the halls of the true spirits to offer sincerity, hoping for their turning gaze and protection; I prostrate before every divine court to bare my earnest plea, wishing for the release of transgressions and faults. May Zhou be granted peace in karmic debts and the washing away of sins and blemishes. May disasters dissolve, years and blessings be prolonged, illness and distress find no purchase, and fortune and felicity gather in abundance. May the ninefold ancestors and sevenfold progenitors ascend to the ranks of the immortals’ courts. May kin and relations all bask in the glory of the sagely sun. Above all, may the ancestral temple stand secure, the sagely lifespan stretch afar, the Purple Forbidden Palace and the Eastern Palace uphold the great enterprise, and the bulwark of the realm, steadfast as bedrock, safeguard the grand foundation. May all officials be bound in loyalty and integrity, and the myriad subjects be gathered under benevolent rule. With utmost devotion, I offer these prayers, placing my vast hopes in the mysterious compassion. I cannot but prostrate myself, gazing to heaven and longing for the sagely presence.

*Memorial of Zhao Qiu, Minister of Education, Offering a Ritual for Illness*

I have heard that the wondrous response knows no bounds, for the Dao extends its aid to all things. The mysterious compassion flows widely, bestowing kindness upon all living beings. It opens the gate of prayer, repentance, and absolution, and extends deliverance to those in distress who seek grace. Its works are accomplished without self-regard, and its blessings spread without limit. Daring to rely upon this all-embracing benevolence, I now pour forth my plea in devotion.

Your servant reflects upon his fortune and prosperity, having been honored to serve in a flourishing era. From the ranks of the imperial escort, I ascended the path to the misty heights. My merits are slight, yet my responsibilities weighty; my contributions few, yet the grace bestowed upon me profound. Ever mindful of this, I am filled with trepidation, finding it difficult to repay such favor. Recently, afflicted by calamity and stricken by illness, I have received the sagely concern that brings comfort, and the dispatch of renowned physicians to attend me. Yet recovery has not come, and my anxiety only deepens.

I reflect that my life has been spent in the dusty world, long neglectful of cultivation. In conduct and action, how could I avoid faults and transgressions? At times, I may have harmed living things without pity; at others, wielded the sword in battle, lightly ordering executions. In commanding troops, I may have failed to issue just commands; in governance, erred in rewards and punishments. In the still of night, enmities may have arisen, and in my humble person, lingering illness taken root. Moreover, I fear that across past lives and accumulated existences, unresolved offenses may yet linger. The Five Phases and Nine Luminaries may converge in misfortune. Perhaps in construction, I have trespassed against the unseen; in earth and timber, caused unwitting harm. Searching my heart and examining my faults, my repentance and prayer are only the more urgent.

Thus, I dare to present this precious memorial and conduct a grand ritual, humbly informing the spirits of the earth below and invoking the deities of the heavens above. I implore the Great Dao to extend its compassion, the Perfected True Ones to grant their protection. May the spirits who govern calamity and deliverance from distress dissolve my disasters; may the gods who bestow blessings dispel my illness and prolong my life. May my name be stricken from the registers of the dead in the courts of the underworld and inscribed in the records of immortals in the world above. May past injuries and unintended killings be reconciled, karmic debts pacified. May new sins and old blemishes be cleansed by the mysterious compassion. I vow to redouble my resolve and forever walk in gratitude for the Dao’s grace.

*Memorial of Zhang Daoheng for the Consecration of the Northern Dipper’s Seven Perfected Star Lords*

Your servant, from tender years, has reverently heard of the Great Dao. My heart has turned to the Dipper’s pole, and my thoughts fixed upon the mysterious void.

Every time I have made prayers, I have been graciously blessed. The boundless favor of the spirits fills me with gratitude, yet I find no means to repay such vast beneficence. Now, having divined an auspicious day—when the virtue of Heaven aligns with the propitious hour—I shall, within the Hall of the Northern Emperor of the Jade Bureau, sculpt the august form of the Central Dipper’s Pole Star. Together with its attendant stars, they shall be arrayed in their eightfold positions. Their robes shall shimmer with rainbow hues, their divine visages shaped like dragons and cranes. Set before the Great Emperor, they shall stand as if gathered in the midst of heaven. I have prepared this memorial to announce the undertaking and now command the work to commence. May the Seven Saints deign to descend, and may the host of spirits grant their luminous protection. May their response endure forever, and may blessings and felicity abide without end. May all hearts find a gateway for their prayers, and may all beings discover the path of refuge. I shall forever reverently tend the incense and flame, in gratitude to the Perfected Ones.

*Memorial of Du Yuanji, Court Attendant, for the Consecration of the Fire Star*

I have heard that the yang spirit manifests auspicious signs, and the virtue of Fire receives the mandate of Heaven. It divides the realm of the sun to extend its light, governing the southern quadrant and establishing its position. Thus, in the Xia calendar, it regulates the year’s labors. Thereby, it moves through the crimson heavens and cycles along the Yellow Way. Its responses are never without cause, and its judgments are impartial. Though its celestial image shines brightly, casting its influence upon all states, its dispensation of disaster or blessing extends even to the most minute. I, undeserving, have been favored with profound grace and walk in this flourishing era. Though I strive to conduct myself with purity, I have not yet attained a state free from transgression. My fate, governed by the Five Phases, unfolds within the course of years. Having consulted the arts and calendars, I find that its influence now shines upon me. Fearing the onset of misfortune, I am filled with dread. Therefore, I humbly present offerings with utmost reverence, preparing incense and lamps. I pray to the radiant spirit above, beseeching its luminous protection. May it manifestly dispel calamities and secretly dissolve past faults. May it bestow blessings and grant enduring fortune. I shall forever devote myself in earnest supplication, in gratitude for the Dao’s grace.

*Memorial of Wang Zongshou, Court Attendant, for the Consecration at Mount Zhangren*

Heaven and Earth divide their numinous essence; the Three Officials determine the registers of life and death. Yin and yang suspend their celestial images; the Nine Luminaries extend their illuminating power. The Northern Office measures transgressions, while the Southern Palace prolongs life. The stars traverse mountains and rivers, their scrutiny impartial. All within the human realm fall under their governance. I, though humble and unworthy, have received the Dao’s compassion. Yet in my conduct, I fear I have strayed from the hidden and startled the spirits. In my thoughts, I have not aligned with the divine. Daily, I encounter misfortune and accumulate faults. At times, calamity converges, and I find no means to repent and pray. This year, the Celestial Talisman resides in the Central Palace, while my own position is illuminated by Saturn. The great cycle still resides within the realm of destructive forces, and the Flying Banners are lodged in my year of fate. The Three Destinies and Five Phases may yet bring harm through conflict. The arrayed stars and five planets may further cast their influence. Thus, my path remains rough, and disasters arise frequently. Without the aid of the Perfected Ones, there is no way to repent and pray. With utmost sincerity, I have undertaken this grand rite. May the Supreme Dao and host of saints deign to bestow blessings. May they dissolve future calamities and absolve past transgressions. May the Six Offices of Destiny augment my lifespan in the Crimson Heaven, and may the Seven Sovereigns of the Celestial Records grant me felicity at the Mystic Pole. May public and private affairs flourish in peace, and my family dwell in tranquility. I shall forever bear the boundless grace of the host of saints.

**Memorial for the Nine Luminaries Rite of Minister Xianchu’s Natal Destiny**

It is heard that the Three Lights manifest auspiciousness, and the Nine Luminaries congeal their radiance. Aligned with Metal and Wood to govern the directions, the four seasons proceed in order; establishing yin and yang to set forth images, the myriad things are born and completed. They preside over the hidden and the manifest, overseeing transgressions and blessings.

Your servant, in his humility, has been granted the honor of serving the true and numinous. Fearing that in the scrutiny of conduct, faults and errors may easily arise, and that the path of cultivation has yet to align with the pristine and true, he is further burdened by the weight of his official duties, where every matter, great or small, may strike. Apprehensive of lapses in vigilance, he fears accruing further guilt and misfortune. Though he strives day and night in service, never daring to slacken in diligence, the unpredictable nature of fortune and misfortune deepens his trepidation and concern. Moreover, with the transits of his natal luminaries pressing upon him, he has earnestly undertaken rites of repentance and supplication. Thus, relying on his natal destiny, he reverently inaugurates this ritual feast, presenting offerings of faith and sincerity, arranging incense and lamps to perform the rites.

He prostrates himself, hoping that the Supreme and Reclusive Saints will deign to regard his sincere heart. May the exalted Luminaries of the celestial hours, in their boundless majesty, graciously bestow their blessings. Absolve past transgressions, dissolve future calamities. May karmic debts be settled, inauspicious omens swept away. Further augment his official emoluments and lifespan, and ever grant him felicity. May his family dwell in peace, and public and private affairs flourish in tranquility. He vows to cultivate devotion unceasingly, in gratitude for the numinous grace. [He dares not say more.]

---

**Memorial for the Jiazi Rite of the Assembly**

It is held that when the Great Simplicity was divided, the primordial essence alone moved. Yin and yang initiated transformation, and the heavenly stems and earthly branches received their foundation. The sixty true spirits govern the four seasons and oversee day and night; the eight hundred talismanic officers determine fortune and misfortune, life and death. In great matters, the state and the cosmos follow the celestial patterns; in small, calamities and blessings, transgressions and felicity are all subject to their decree. Studying the *Dragon Embryo Stone Chamber Scriptures* and perusing the essentials of the *Phoenix Seal Jade Casket*, the core principles are made clear, and devotion is redoubled.

Your servants, relying on the divine efficacy, have encountered the turning of the Dao’s fortune. Yet the dusty mechanisms remain long closed, and the snares of the world have not been cast off. Conduct and retreat do not accord with the Confucian and the arcane; every movement and rest inevitably incurs faults and errors. Further fearing that within the Five Phases there may be clashes and hindrances, and that within the Three Destinies, adversity may be encountered, without recourse to the Supreme Dao, deep stains cannot be repented. Thus, on the day of the six Jia and the first of the Five Origins, with united sincerity and resolute intent, they pour forth their earnest supplications. Gazing toward the azure vault to descend the true, they sweep the numinous altar to perform the rites.

They prostrate themselves, hoping that vast blessings will be justly bestowed, and that the impartial and luminous will regard their plea. May all be granted auspiciousness, and calamities forever dissolved. May the Azure Palace augment their emoluments, and the Crimson Registers prolong their lives. May the living and the dead alike dwell in peace, and public and private affairs together flourish in prosperity. They vow to cultivate devotion with diligence, forever repaying the numinous benevolence. [They dare not say more.]

---

**Memorial for the Natal Destiny Rite of the Assembly**

Your servants, having planted blessings in past lives, have encountered the transformation of the Dao. The Most Perfect has imparted teachings, and the mysterious principles are proclaimed and practiced. Gazing upward, they receive the grace of sheltering protection, and constantly harbor earnest reverence and concern.

Yet they fear that conduct may stray from propriety and yielding, and that every step may incur faults and blemishes. Dwelling in the world and conforming to the times, they often accumulate transgressions. From past lives to this present existence, they have seldom undertaken rites of repentance and supplication. It is heard that the Three Heavens have established the regulations for rites of offering, and the Orthodox Unity has set forth the standards for cultivation and expiation. Thus, on this auspicious day, with united sincerity, they reverently proceed to the altar to offer prayers and thanks.

They prostrate themselves, invoking the Three Officials and Nine Bureaus, the Five August Emperors, the True Lords of the Dipper and Pole, and the numinous generals of their natal destinies. May they record their earnest pleas and descend with vast benevolence. Absolve past transgressions, release future calamities. May the influences of the stellar luminaries cease their adverse transits, and the year’s fortune be freed from clashes and hindrances. May official emoluments and lifespan be augmented, and felicity and auspiciousness abound. May public and private affairs be upright and prosperous, and their clans and families secure in peace.

They vow to forever cherish the grace of protection and safeguarding, and to eternally pledge their devotion in cultivation. [They dare not say more.]

**Jiao Petition for the Gengshen Day**

Your servant, having reverently studied the true scriptures and devoutly followed the mysterious classics, observes that the Gengshen day is the appointed time for offering and reverence. On this day, the Great Emperor descends to examine the records of retribution. The Three Corpses and yin spirits submit their indictments, listing every transgression—great or small, coarse or subtle—without omission. The charges are first registered in the Palace of Supreme Mystery, then inscribed in the courts of the Yellow Springs. All who cultivate the heart must truly fear and take heed.

Hoping to seize this auspicious occasion, we join in repentance for our deep faults. We prepare fragrant offerings and reverently present this jiao petition in gratitude. We humbly beseech the Three August Ones, in their compassion and protection, to deign to witness our plea. May they reject the false accusations of the yin corpses and bestow the great bounty of the Dao’s love for life. Thus may our disasters be dispelled and our transgressions erased, our goodness accumulated and blessings amassed. May the Nine Mysteries depart the realm of cold night, and the Five Clans receive the blessings of peace and security. May all affairs be upright and auspicious, and our vows swiftly fulfilled. We shall forever cherish our devotion to cultivation, ever repaying the grace of the True and Orthodox. [We dare not say more.]

---

**Jiao Petition to the Southern and Northern Dippers**

We have heard that since the Great Image was divided, the Three Powers have established their positions. Each embodies the natural Dao and bestows effortless merit. Through non-action, heaven and earth endure; through action, decline and prosperity shift. Fortune and misfortune, regret and shame—all arise from this.

Thus, the Crimson Register of the Southern Pole governs the records of life, while the Black Tablets of the Northern Capital govern the records of death. The two palaces judge without partiality, and the lives and deaths of all beings depend on them. Your servant, long favored by virtuous blessings, has enjoyed prosperous times. Bathed in the imperial wind and nurtured by the mysterious transformation, I nonetheless fear that my thoughts and intentions may transgress the Five Constants. My accumulated faults and errors are manifest in the two registers.

The Five Phases and Three Destinies, yin and yang, foretell times of punishment; the hidden luminaries and arrayed stars decree the pace of their transits. Before I could offer prayers of repentance, misfortunes had already taken root. Thus, on this auspicious day, I reverently perform the jiao rites. The altar stands empty in the quiet of night, while the numinous transformation dawns with the morning’s clarity. My profound devotion must reach them, and the true spirits may descend.

We humbly implore the Six Sages of the Crimson Terrace, Controllers of Destiny, to open the talismans of extended life; and the Seven Perfected of the Mysterious Ultimate, Great Emperors, to remove the days of shortened years. May our anxieties turn to peace, and our years and emoluments increase. May the living and the dead alike share in this singular grace, and our kin and dependents all partake of boundless fortune. May public and private affairs be upright and prosperous, and the old and young enjoy health and well-being. We shall forever bear the boundless grace of the saints of the two palaces. [We dare not say more.]

---

**Jiao Petition to the Earth Deity of the Imperial Portrait Chapel at Longxing Abbey**

We observe that the jade towers and jasper halls, the star chambers and feathered palaces, stand in solemn array above the Three Clarities and unfold within the Eight Radiant Scenes. They are the gathering place of the myriad beings and the abode of the host of perfected. Thus, they shape the boundaries of the mortal realm and extend their influence into the human world.

When King Mu of Zhou journeyed west, he modeled his terraced halls after them; when Emperor Wu of Han gazed south, he followed the Great Unity in laying their foundations. Hence, immortal sanctuaries and numinous precincts spread across mountains and seas. Their eaves catch the wind, their rafters embrace the clouds, and their splendor adorns the misty forests. They are the dwelling of the true sages and the convergence of blessings and felicity.

Longxing Abbey was first established in the Sui dynasty and has endured through the Tang years, its history long and deep. Yet time has worn it down, and decay has lingered.
